Ijazah and Munawalah: Valid Transmission Methods in Hanafi Usul
Explaining the rukhsah methods: ijazah and munawalah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions under which ijazah and munawalah are valid proofs (hujjah) according to Hanafi usul, and distinguish between a valid ijazah and a mere blessing (tabarruk).

Core Idea
Ijazah is valid proof only if the recipient already knows the content; otherwise it is mere blessing.

This passage from Ashraf al-Anwār explains the Hanafi rules for two concessionary (rukhsah) methods of hadith transmission: ijāzah (permission) and munāwalah (handing over). While these are allowed, they come with strict conditions. The most critical is that the recipient must have prior knowledge of the book's content. Without that, the transmission is not a valid legal proof but only a spiritual blessing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the methods
Read the description of ijāzah and munāwalah. Note how the teacher grants permission and how the student receives the book.
Ijazah can be given without munawalah, but munawalah requires ijazah.
2
Extract the condition for validity
Find the sentence: 'وَالْمُجَازُ لَهُ إِنْ كَانَ عَالِمًا بِهِ ... تَصِحُّ وَإِلاَّ فَلاَ'. This states the key condition: prior knowledge of the content.
This distinguishes Hanafi view from some other schools.
3
Contrast valid vs. non-valid ijazah
The text contrasts a student who knows the book through prior study with one who only intends to study later. The latter ijazah is not a proof.
Example: studying Mishkat al-Masabih with commentaries before receiving ijazah makes it valid.
4
Apply the condition
Consider a scenario: a teacher gives ijazah to a student who has never seen the book. According to Hanafi usul, would this transmission be hujjah?
The answer is no, because the condition of prior knowledge is not met.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَكَذَالِكَ الرِّسَالَةُ عَلَى هَذَا الْوَجْهِ بِأَنْ يَقُولَ المُحَدِّثُ لِلرَّسُوْلِ: بَلِّغْ عَلَى فَلَانًا أَنَّهُ قَدْ حَدَّثَنِي بِهَذَا الْحَدِيثِ فَلاَنُ بْنُ فُلاَنٍ، فَإِذَا بَلَغَكَ رِسَالَتِي هَذِهِ فَارْوِ عَنِّي بِهَذَا الْحَدِيثِ. فَيَكُونَانِ أَيِ الْكِتَابُ وَالرِّسَالَةُ حُجَّتَيْنِ إِذَا ثَبَتَا بِالْحُجَّةِ أَنْ بِالْبَيِّنَةِ أَنَّ هَذَا كِتَابُ فُلانٍ أَوْ رَسُوْلُ فُلانٍ عَلَى مَا عُرِفَ فِي كِتَابِ الْقَاضِي. هَذِهِ أَرْبَعَةُ أَقْسَامٍ لِلْعَزِيمَةِ فِي طَرْفِ السَّمَاعِ وَالأَوْلَانِ أَكْمَلانَ مِنَ الأَخِيْرَيْنِ. أَوْ يَكُونُ رُخْصَةً وَهُوَ الَّذِي لا اسْتِمَاعَ فِيهِ أَى لَمْ تَكُنْ مُذَاكَرَةُ الْكَلاَمِ فِيمَا بَيْنَهُمَا لاَ غَيْبًا وَلاَ مُشَافَهَةً كَالإِجَازَةِ بِأَنْ يَقُولَ الْمُحَدِّثُ لِغَيْرِهِ: أَجَزْتُ لَكَ أَنْ تَرْوِيَ عَنِّي هَذَا الْكِتَابَ الَّذِي حَدَّثَنِي فُلاَنٌ عَنْ فُلاَنٍ [؟]. وَالْمُنَاوَلَةُ بِأَنْ يُعْطِيَ الشَّيْخُ كِتَابَ سَمَاعِهِ بِيَدِهِ إِلَى الْمُسْتَفِيْدِ وَيَقُولَ: هَذَا كِتَابُ سَمَاعِي مِنْ شَيْجِي فُلانٍ أَجَزْتُ لَكَ أَنْ تَرْوِيَ عَنِّي هَذَا. فَهُوَ لاَ يَصِحُّ بِدُونِ الإِجَازَةِ وَالإِجَازَةُ تَصِحُّ بِدُونِ الْمُنَاوَلَةِ فالإِجَازَةُ لاَ بُدَّ مِنْهَا فِي كُلِّ حَالٍ. وَالْمُجَازُ لَهُ إِنْ كَانَ عَالِمًا بِهِ أَيْ بِمَا فِي الْكِتَابِ قَبْلَ الإِجَازَةِ تَصِحُّ وَإِلاَّ فَلاَ. يَعْنِي إِذَا أَجَزْنَا بِكِتَابِ الْمِشْكَاةِ قَبْلَ ذلِكَ بِالْمُطَالَعَةِ بِقُوَّةِ نَفْسِهِ أَوْ بِإِعَانَةِ الشُّرُوحِ أَوْ نَحْوِ ذَلِكَ وَلَكِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهُ سَنَدٌ صَحِيحٌ يَتَّصِلُ بِالْمُصَنِّفِ فَحِينَئِذٍ تَصِحُّ إِجَازَتُنَا لَهُ، وَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ كَذَلِكَ بَلْ يَعْتَمِدُ عَلَى أَنْ يُطَالِعَ بَعْدَ الإِجَازَةِ وَيُعَلِّمَ النَّاسَ كَمَا فِي زَمَانِنَا لَمْ تَكُنْ تِلْكَ الإِجَازَةُ حُجَّةً بَلْ إِجَازَةُ تَبَرُّكٍ. وَالثَّانِي طَرْفُ الْحِفْظِ وَالْعَزِيمَةُ فِيهِ أَنْ يَحْفَظَ الْمَسْمُوعَ مِنْ وَقْتِ السَّمَاعِ إِلَى وَقْتِ الأَدَاءِ وَلَمْ يَعْتَمِدْ عَلَى الْكِتَابِ وَلِهَذَا لَمْ يَجْمَعْ أَبُو حَنِيْفَةَ كِتَابًا فِي الْحَدِيثِ وَلَمْ يَسْتَجِزْ الرِّوَايَةَ بِاعْتِمَادِ الْكِتَابِ وَكَانَ ذلِكَ سَبَبًا لِطَعْنِ الْمُتَعَصِّبِينَ الْقَاصِرِينَ إِلَى يَوْمِ الدِّيْنِ وَلَمْ يَفْهَمُوا وَرَعَهُ وَتَفَرُّدَهُ وَلاَ عَمَلَهُ وَهَدَاهُ. وَالرُّخْصَةُ أَنْ يَعْتَمِدَ الْكِتَابَ فَإِنْ نَظَرَ فِيهِ وَتَذَكَّرَ سَمَاعَهُ وَمَجْلِسَ دَرْسِهِ وَمَا جَرَى فِيهِ يَكُونُ حُجَّةً وَإِلاَّ فَلاَ، فَإِنْ لَمْ يَتَذَكَّرْ ذَلِكَ فَلاَ يَكُونُ حُجَّةً عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيْفَةَ أَنْ [؟].
And similarly the message (risalah) in this manner: that the hadith scholar says to the messenger: 'Convey to so-and-so that he has narrated to me this hadith, so-and-so from so-and-so. So when this message of mine reaches you, narrate from me this hadith.' So both of them (the letter and the message) are proofs (hujjah) when they are established by evidence that this is the letter of so-and-so or the messenger of so-and-so, as is known in the book of the judge. These are four categories of strict requirement ('azimah) in the aspect of listening (samā'), and the first two are more complete than the last two. Or it may be a concession (rukhsah), which is that there is no listening in it, i.e., there was no discussion of speech between them, neither absent nor face-to-face, like ijazah (permission), where the hadith scholar says to someone else: 'I have permitted you to narrate from me this book which so-and-so narrated to me from so-and-so.' And munawalah (handing over) is that the teacher gives the book of his listening in his hand to the student and says: 'This is the book of my listening from my teacher so-and-so; I have permitted you to narrate from me this.' So it is not valid without ijazah, and ijazah is valid without munawalah. Therefore, ijazah is necessary in every case. And the one given permission (al-mujāz lahu), if he is knowledgeable of it, i.e., of what is in the book before the ijazah, the ijazah is valid; otherwise not. That is, if we give ijazah in the book al-Mishkāt before that by reading with his own effort or with the help of commentaries or the like, but he did not have a valid chain connecting to the author, then our ijazah to him is valid. But if it is not so, rather he relies on studying after the ijazah and teaching people, as in our times, that ijazah is not a proof but a blessing ijazah. And the second is the aspect of memorization (hifz). The strict requirement in it is that he memorize what is heard from the time of hearing to the time of delivery, and he does not rely on the book. For this reason, Abu Hanifah did not compile a book in hadith and did not permit narration by relying on the book. And that became a reason for the criticism of the biased shortsighted ones until the Day of Judgment, and they did not understand his piety, his uniqueness, his practice, and his guidance. And the concession is that he relies on the book, then if he looks into it and recalls his hearing and his study session and what occurred therein, it is a proof; otherwise not. If he does not recall that, then it is not a proof according to Abu Hanifah.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Anwār, a commentary on Nūr al-Anwār, discusses the methods of hadith transmission (tahammul al-‘ilm). It begins by explaining how sending a letter or a messenger can serve as a valid proof (hujjah) for narration, provided that the authenticity of the letter or messenger is established through evidence. The author then outlines two categories: the first two of the four types of ‘azīmah (strict requirement) in the method of ‘ard (presentation) are superior, while the latter two are lesser. Following this, the text describes the rukhsah (concession) method, which includes ijāzah (permission) and munāwalah (handing over). In ijāzah, the teacher gives general permission to narrate a book he has heard, without the student having heard it directly. Munāwalah involves physically handing over the teacher’s own listening copy. The key condition is that ijāzah is only valid if the recipient already knows the contents of the book before receiving the permission; otherwise, it is merely a blessing (tabarruk) and not a proof. The passage then moves to the aspect of memorization (hifz). The ‘azīmah here is to rely on memory without depending on a written text. Imam Abu Hanifah is noted for not compiling a book of hadith and not permitting narration solely by reliance on writing, which led to criticism from those who did not understand his exceptional piety and methodology. Finally, the rukhsah in memorization is to rely on the written book, but only if the narrator looks at it and genuinely recalls hearing it from his teacher; otherwise, it is not accepted as proof according to Abu Hanifah.

Key Terms
الإجازة (al-ijāzah): Permission granted by a hadith scholar to another to narrate hadith on his authority
المناولة (al-munāwalah): The teacher physically handing his listening copy to the student with permission to narrate
الرخصة (al-rukhsah): Concession in transmission methods that do not require direct listening
حُجَّة (ḥujjah): Legal proof; valid evidence in deriving rulings

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view in this passage, when is an ijazah to narrate a book considered a valid proof (hujjah)?
A) When the recipient receives the ijazah from a well-known scholar
B) When the recipient knows the contents of the book before receiving the ijazah
C) When the ijazah is given in writing
D) When the recipient promises to study the book after receiving the ijazah

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the validity of ijazah as a proof hinges on the student's prior knowledge of the content, not merely the teacher's authority.

Hifz and the Hanafi Emphasis on Memory: 'Azimah vs Rukhsah
Explaining the strict and concessionary paths in hifz

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi distinction between 'azimah and rukhsah in hadith memorization (hifz), and identify Abu Hanifah's position on reliance on written texts.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifah insisted on complete memorization without book reliance; concession allows the book only if memory is refreshed.

This passage moves from the rukhsah methods to the stricter requirements of memorization (hifz). Imam Abu Hanifah himself never compiled a hadith book and did not permit narration solely from written notes. The 'azimah (strict path) is to rely entirely on memory from hearing to delivery. The rukhsah allows using a written text, but only if the narrator genuinely recalls the original hearing session. This lesson unpacks the rationale behind Abu Hanifah's unique methodology and its implications for the reliability of hadith transmission.

Guided Path
1
Define the two categories
Identify the 'azimah and rukhsah in hifz. The 'azimah: memorize from hearing and never rely on a book. The rukhsah: rely on a book but only if you recall the hearing session.
Abu Hanifah strictly followed the 'azimah.
2
Understand Abu Hanifah's practice
Note why Abu Hanifah did not compile a hadith book: he prioritized memory and did not allow narration from written texts without recall. This was not due to lack of knowledge but extreme caution.
The commentator defends Abu Hanifah against critics.
3
Extract the condition for rukhsah
The passage says: 'فَإِنْ نَظَرَ فِيهِ وَتَذَكَّرَ سَمَاعَهُ ... يَكُونُ حُجَّةً وَإِلاَّ فَلاَ'. The key is genuine recollection (tadhakkur) of the original session.
Without recollection, the book reliance is not proof according to Abu Hanifah.
4
Apply to a scenario
Consider a narrator who has a written copy of a hadith but does not remember hearing it from his teacher. According to Abu Hanifah, can he narrate it?
He cannot, because the condition of tadhakkur is not met.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَكَذَالِكَ الرِّسَالَةُ عَلَى هَذَا الْوَجْهِ بِأَنْ يَقُولَ المُحَدِّثُ لِلرَّسُوْلِ: بَلِّغْ عَلَى فَلَانًا أَنَّهُ قَدْ حَدَّثَنِي بِهَذَا الْحَدِيثِ فَلاَنُ بْنُ فُلاَنٍ، فَإِذَا بَلَغَكَ رِسَالَتِي هَذِهِ فَارْوِ عَنِّي بِهَذَا الْحَدِيثِ. فَيَكُونَانِ أَيِ الْكِتَابُ وَالرِّسَالَةُ حُجَّتَيْنِ إِذَا ثَبَتَا بِالْحُجَّةِ أَنْ بِالْبَيِّنَةِ أَنَّ هَذَا كِتَابُ فُلانٍ أَوْ رَسُوْلُ فُلانٍ عَلَى مَا عُرِفَ فِي كِتَابِ الْقَاضِي. هَذِهِ أَرْبَعَةُ أَقْسَامٍ لِلْعَزِيمَةِ فِي طَرْفِ السَّمَاعِ وَالأَوْلَانِ أَكْمَلانَ مِنَ الأَخِيْرَيْنِ. أَوْ يَكُونُ رُخْصَةً وَهُوَ الَّذِي لا اسْتِمَاعَ فِيهِ أَى لَمْ تَكُنْ مُذَاكَرَةُ الْكَلاَمِ فِيمَا بَيْنَهُمَا لاَ غَيْبًا وَلاَ مُشَافَهَةً كَالإِجَازَةِ بِأَنْ يَقُولَ الْمُحَدِّثُ لِغَيْرِهِ: أَجَزْتُ لَكَ أَنْ تَرْوِيَ عَنِّي هَذَا الْكِتَابَ الَّذِي حَدَّثَنِي فُلاَنٌ عَنْ فُلاَنٍ [؟]. وَالْمُنَاوَلَةُ بِأَنْ يُعْطِيَ الشَّيْخُ كِتَابَ سَمَاعِهِ بِيَدِهِ إِلَى الْمُسْتَفِيْدِ وَيَقُولَ: هَذَا كِتَابُ سَمَاعِي مِنْ شَيْجِي فُلانٍ أَجَزْتُ لَكَ أَنْ تَرْوِيَ عَنِّي هَذَا. فَهُوَ لاَ يَصِحُّ بِدُونِ الإِجَازَةِ وَالإِجَازَةُ تَصِحُّ بِدُونِ الْمُنَاوَلَةِ فالإِجَازَةُ لاَ بُدَّ مِنْهَا فِي كُلِّ حَالٍ. وَالْمُجَازُ لَهُ إِنْ كَانَ عَالِمًا بِهِ أَيْ بِمَا فِي الْكِتَابِ قَبْلَ الإِجَازَةِ تَصِحُّ وَإِلاَّ فَلاَ. يَعْنِي إِذَا أَجَزْنَا بِكِتَابِ الْمِشْكَاةِ قَبْلَ ذلِكَ بِالْمُطَالَعَةِ بِقُوَّةِ نَفْسِهِ أَوْ بِإِعَانَةِ الشُّرُوحِ أَوْ نَحْوِ ذَلِكَ وَلَكِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهُ سَنَدٌ صَحِيحٌ يَتَّصِلُ بِالْمُصَنِّفِ فَحِينَئِذٍ تَصِحُّ إِجَازَتُنَا لَهُ، وَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ كَذَلِكَ بَلْ يَعْتَمِدُ عَلَى أَنْ يُطَالِعَ بَعْدَ الإِجَازَةِ وَيُعَلِّمَ النَّاسَ كَمَا فِي زَمَانِنَا لَمْ تَكُنْ تِلْكَ الإِجَازَةُ حُجَّةً بَلْ إِجَازَةُ تَبَرُّكٍ. وَالثَّانِي طَرْفُ الْحِفْظِ وَالْعَزِيمَةُ فِيهِ أَنْ يَحْفَظَ الْمَسْمُوعَ مِنْ وَقْتِ السَّمَاعِ إِلَى وَقْتِ الأَدَاءِ وَلَمْ يَعْتَمِدْ عَلَى الْكِتَابِ وَلِهَذَا لَمْ يَجْمَعْ أَبُو حَنِيْفَةَ كِتَابًا فِي الْحَدِيثِ وَلَمْ يَسْتَجِزْ الرِّوَايَةَ بِاعْتِمَادِ الْكِتَابِ وَكَانَ ذلِكَ سَبَبًا لِطَعْنِ الْمُتَعَصِّبِينَ الْقَاصِرِينَ إِلَى يَوْمِ الدِّيْنِ وَلَمْ يَفْهَمُوا وَرَعَهُ وَتَفَرُّدَهُ وَلاَ عَمَلَهُ وَهَدَاهُ. وَالرُّخْصَةُ أَنْ يَعْتَمِدَ الْكِتَابَ فَإِنْ نَظَرَ فِيهِ وَتَذَكَّرَ سَمَاعَهُ وَمَجْلِسَ دَرْسِهِ وَمَا جَرَى فِيهِ يَكُونُ حُجَّةً وَإِلاَّ فَلاَ، فَإِنْ لَمْ يَتَذَكَّرْ ذَلِكَ فَلاَ يَكُونُ حُجَّةً عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيْفَةَ أَنْ [؟].
And similarly the message (risalah) in this manner: that the hadith scholar says to the messenger: 'Convey to so-and-so that he has narrated to me this hadith, so-and-so from so-and-so. So when this message of mine reaches you, narrate from me this hadith.' So both of them (the letter and the message) are proofs (hujjah) when they are established by evidence that this is the letter of so-and-so or the messenger of so-and-so, as is known in the book of the judge. These are four categories of strict requirement ('azimah) in the aspect of listening (samā'), and the first two are more complete than the last two. Or it may be a concession (rukhsah), which is that there is no listening in it, i.e., there was no discussion of speech between them, neither absent nor face-to-face, like ijazah (permission), where the hadith scholar says to someone else: 'I have permitted you to narrate from me this book which so-and-so narrated to me from so-and-so.' And munawalah (handing over) is that the teacher gives the book of his listening in his hand to the student and says: 'This is the book of my listening from my teacher so-and-so; I have permitted you to narrate from me this.' So it is not valid without ijazah, and ijazah is valid without munawalah. Therefore, ijazah is necessary in every case. And the one given permission (al-mujāz lahu), if he is knowledgeable of it, i.e., of what is in the book before the ijazah, the ijazah is valid; otherwise not. That is, if we give ijazah in the book al-Mishkāt before that by reading with his own effort or with the help of commentaries or the like, but he did not have a valid chain connecting to the author, then our ijazah to him is valid. But if it is not so, rather he relies on studying after the ijazah and teaching people, as in our times, that ijazah is not a proof but a blessing ijazah. And the second is the aspect of memorization (hifz). The strict requirement in it is that he memorize what is heard from the time of hearing to the time of delivery, and he does not rely on the book. For this reason, Abu Hanifah did not compile a book in hadith and did not permit narration by relying on the book. And that became a reason for the criticism of the biased shortsighted ones until the Day of Judgment, and they did not understand his piety, his uniqueness, his practice, and his guidance. And the concession is that he relies on the book, then if he looks into it and recalls his hearing and his study session and what occurred therein, it is a proof; otherwise not. If he does not recall that, then it is not a proof according to Abu Hanifah.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Anwār, a commentary on Nūr al-Anwār, discusses the methods of hadith transmission (tahammul al-‘ilm). It begins by explaining how sending a letter or a messenger can serve as a valid proof (hujjah) for narration, provided that the authenticity of the letter or messenger is established through evidence. The author then outlines two categories: the first two of the four types of ‘azīmah (strict requirement) in the method of ‘ard (presentation) are superior, while the latter two are lesser. Following this, the text describes the rukhsah (concession) method, which includes ijāzah (permission) and munāwalah (handing over). In ijāzah, the teacher gives general permission to narrate a book he has heard, without the student having heard it directly. Munāwalah involves physically handing over the teacher’s own listening copy. The key condition is that ijāzah is only valid if the recipient already knows the contents of the book before receiving the permission; otherwise, it is merely a blessing (tabarruk) and not a proof. The passage then moves to the aspect of memorization (hifz). The ‘azīmah here is to rely on memory without depending on a written text. Imam Abu Hanifah is noted for not compiling a book of hadith and not permitting narration solely by reliance on writing, which led to criticism from those who did not understand his exceptional piety and methodology. Finally, the rukhsah in memorization is to rely on the written book, but only if the narrator looks at it and genuinely recalls hearing it from his teacher; otherwise, it is not accepted as proof according to Abu Hanifah.

Key Terms
العزيمة (al-‘azīmah): Strict requirement; the originally required method without concession
الرخصة (al-rukhsah): Concession; a permissible alternative where the strict requirement is relaxed
التذكر (al-tadhakkur): Genuine recollection or recall of the original hearing session
الورع (al-wara‘): Scrupulous piety; abstaining from permissible things due to fear of falling into the impermissible

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, under what condition is relying on a written book (rukhsah) considered a valid proof (hujjah) in hifz?
A) If the book is written by a reliable scholar
B) If the narrator looks at the book and recalls the original hearing session
C) If the narrator has memorized the book entirely
D) If the book contains the teacher's chain

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the rukhsah in hifz is valid only when the narrator's use of a written text triggers genuine recall of the original hearing, not merely as a substitute for memory.

Invalid Grounds for Jarh of a Narrator
Listing and refuting invalid grounds for jarh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain the eight invalid grounds for jarh of a narrator according to Hanafi usul, and apply the principle that only jarh from a sincere, unbiased critic is accepted.

Core Idea
Jarh is only valid from a sincere, unbiased critic; eight common grounds (e.g., tadlis, joking) do not impugn a narrator.

This passage from Ashraf al-Anwar clarifies which criticisms of narrators are not acceptable in Hanafi usul. It first establishes that only a person known for sincerity (nasihah) and free from bias (ta'assub) can issue valid jarh. Then it lists eight specific grounds that some critics use but the Hanafi school rejects as valid impugnment. Understanding this list helps prevent unfair rejection of reliable narrators and preserves the integrity of hadith transmission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle for valid jarh
The passage states that jarh is accepted only from a person famous for sincerity and not from a biased person. Note the harm bias causes to the religion.
This principle governs all the specific examples that follow.
2
Review the eight invalid grounds
The author lists eight items: tadlis, talbis, irsal, rukud al-dabbah, mizah, hadath al-sinn, 'adam al-i'tiyad bi al-riwayah, and istikthar masa'il al-fiqh. For each, he provides a counterargument or example.
Some critics use these, but Hanafis reject them because they are not evidence of dishonesty or carelessness.
3
Analyze the refutation for each ground
For each invalid ground, the author provides a reason or precedent: e.g., tadlis only causes suspicion of irsal, which is not jarh; the Prophet joked; many Companions narrated young; Abu Bakr rarely narrated; etc.
The refutations rely on the practice of the Salaf and the principle of judging by known reliability rather than superficial behavior.
4
Understand the Hanafi response to critics
The passage responds to 'some hadith critics' who impugn based on tadlis, etc. The Hanafi response is that these actions are either permissible or not indicative of dishonesty.
The practical consequence is acceptance of narrations from scholars like Abu Hanifa and Muhammad ibn al-Hasan.
5
Apply the principle to new examples
Given a scenario where a narrator is criticized for being a humorist or for rarely narrating, determine whether that criticism is valid hanafi-wise.
Use the eight-item list as a checklist for commonly misapplied criticisms.

روایت بیان کرنے کی عادت نہیں تھی۔ باوجودیکہ کوئی دوسرا ان کی برابری ضبط و اتقان میں نہیں کر سکتا تھا۔ وَاسْتِكْثَارُ مَسَائِلِ الْفِقْهِ (۸) اور مسائل فقہ کو کثرت سے بیان کرنے سے چنانچہ اس وجہ سے بعض محمد ثین نے ہمارے اصحاب پر آواز بھی کیا ہے۔ بہر حال یہ بھی کوئی عیب نہیں ہے بلکہ یہ ذہن کے قومی ہونے کی دلیل ہے۔ اور عمدہ ہونے کی واضح اور روشن دلیل ہے۔ چنانچہ حضرت سید نا ابو یوسف کو ہیں ہزار موضوع حدیثیں حفظ تھیں۔ تو آپ کا کیا گمان ہو گا بیچ حدیثوں کے بارہ میں وَلَمَّا فَرَغَ الْمُصَنِّفُ عَنْ بَيَانِ أَقْسَامِ السَّنَّةِ شَرَعَ فِي بَحْثِ الْمُعَارَضَةِ الْمُشْتَرِكَةِ بَيْنَ الْكِتَابِ وَالسَّنَّةِ تَبَعًا لِفَخْرِ الإِسْلَامِ وَكَانَ يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يُدْرِجَهَا فِي
This is the commentary on Nur al-Anwar, volume three. There is agreement on this, no disagreement. In the case where some consider it jarh and some not, jarh is only accepted from a person who is famous for sincerity and not bias. Because biased people have severely harmed the religion, declaring disliked acts as forbidden and recommended as obligatory. Alas, today some of our uneducated or semi-educated (followers) have developed such tendencies, abandoning obligations and emphasizing permissible details, leaving disliked acts and choosing problematic ones. The commentators say: the jarh of such people has no consideration. Even tadlis is not accepted as impugnment. The meaning of tadlis: in trade, hiding a defect from the buyer; in the terminology of hadith scholars, hiding details in the isnad, e.g., saying 'haddathana fulan 'an fulan' instead of 'haddathana fulan qala akhbrana fulan'... because at most, it raises suspicion of irsal. But since mursal is not considered jarh, the suspicion of irsal is even less. And talbis: that the narrator mentions his shaykh by kunyah not by name, or by an unfamiliar description, so that he is not recognized among people and they do not criticize him, like Sufyan al-Thawri saying 'haddathani Abu Sa'id' which is the kunyah of both al-Hasan al-Basri and al-Kalbi. In some copies here is the phrase 'wal-irsalu taba'an li-Fakhr al-Islam' and it is also not impugnment as we mentioned. And riding the beast (rukud al-dabbah): just as some contemporaries impugn Muhammad ibn al-Hasan because of it, but it is a permissible act of mujahidin and is not valid as jarh. And joking (al-mizah): it is not valid as jarh because the Prophet (peace be upon him) joked often but only said the truth, as he said to an old woman: 'Old women do not enter Paradise.' When she left crying, he said: 'Tell her the saying of Allah: Indeed, We have produced them in a [new] creation and made them virgins, loving, of equal age.' And young age (hadath al-sinn): meaning smallness, as Sufyan al-Thawri said to Abu Hanifa: 'What does this young man say?' But many Companions narrated in their youth with the condition of proficiency at the time of learning and justice at the time of teaching. And lack of habit in narrating ('adam al-i'tiyad bi al-riwayah): for Abu Bakr was not accustomed to narrating, yet no one equaled him in precision and proficiency. And gathering many fiqh questions (istikthar masa'il al-fiqh): as some hadith scholars impugn our companions because of it, but that is evidence of strength and excellence. Abu Yusuf memorized twenty thousand fabricated hadith, so what about the authentic ones?
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Anwar is a commentary on Nur al-Anwar. It discusses the prerequisites for valid jarh (impugnment) of a narrator or scholar. The author first emphasizes that jarh is only acceptable from a person known for sincerity (nasihah) and free from bias (ta'assub). He laments that some ignorant or semi-educated people have become extremists, mislabeling acts. The commentator then lists eight specific things that are not considered valid grounds for impugnment, even if some critics use them. (1) Tadlis: concealing details in isnad. (2) Talbis: mentioning a shaykh by an unfamiliar kunyah or description. (3) Irsal: sending a hadith without full chain. (4) Rukud al-dabbah: riding a horse fast (like Muhammad ibn al-Hasan did). (5) Mizah: joking. (6) Hadath al-sinn: young age. (7) 'Adam al-i'tiyad bi al-riwayah: not being a frequent narrator. (8) Istikthar masa'il al-fiqh: possessing many fiqh rulings. For each, he gives a counterargument or example from the Salaf. The Hanafi stance is that these do not impugn a narrator's reliability unless accompanied by actual lying or major sin.

Key Terms
التدليس (al-tadlis): Concealing defects in a transaction or, in hadith, hiding the details of an isnad by saying 'haddathana fulan 'an fulan' instead of specifying the hearing mode.
التلبيس (al-talbis): Mentioning a shaykh by an unfamiliar kunyah or description to avoid recognition and criticism.
المزاح (al-mizah): Joking, even if frequent, provided it is truthful and not sinful. The Prophet's example shows it is not a flaw.
الإرسال (al-irsal): A narrator omitting the intermediary between him and the Prophet; mursal hadith.
ركض الدابة (rukud al-dabbah): Riding an animal fast, e.g., galloping a horse.
حداثة السن (hadath al-sinn): Young age.
عدم الاعتياد بالرواية ('adam al-i'tiyad bi al-riwayah): Lack of habit or practice in narrating hadith.
استكثار مسائل الفقه (istikthar masa'il al-fiqh): Having a large number of fiqh rulings (i.e., being a jurist).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT considered a valid ground for jarh (impugnment) of a narrator?
A) Tadlis (concealing isnad details)
B) Talbis (mentioning shaykh by unfamiliar kunyah)
C) Lying (kizb)
D) Mizah (joking)

Key Takeaway
Jarh is only accepted from a sincere, unbiased critic, and eight common criticisms (like tadlis, joking, or young age) do not constitute valid grounds for impugnment in Hanafi usul.

intermediate
10 min
The Hanafi Hierarchy for Resolving Contradictory Evidences
Explains hierarchy for resolving contradictions and the case of su'r al-himar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the four-step Hanafi hierarchy (Quran → Sunnah → Companions/Qiyas → Taqrir al-Asl) to resolve apparent contradictions between evidences, using the example of su'r al-himar.

Core Idea
When evidences conflict and cannot be reconciled, the Hanafi jurist moves down the hierarchy: Quran, Sunnah, Companions or Qiyas, then Taqrir al-Asl.

This passage from Ashraf al-Anwar presents the systematic method for resolving ta'arud (contradiction) between legal evidences. Hanafi scholars prioritize sources in a fixed order. When two Quranic verses contradict, both are set aside and one resorts to the Sunnah. If hadiths contradict, one resorts to Companions' sayings or qiyas. If these also conflict, the principle of taqrir al-asl (original state) applies, as demonstrated in the famous case of a donkey's leftover water (su'r al-himar).

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting evidences
Determine whether the conflict is between two Quranic verses, two hadiths, or among lower sources (e.g., Companions' sayings vs qiyas).
Also check if reconciliation (jam') is possible before applying the hierarchy.
2
Attempt reconciliation (jam' wa tawfiq)
Check if the evidences can be harmonized without contradiction, e.g., through takhsis or taqyid. If possible, no need to move down.
This is the preferred first step in all madhahib.
3
Apply the hierarchy
If reconciliation fails, follow the order: Quranic verses → Sunnah → Companions' sayings or Qiyas → Taqrir al-Asl. Each step abandons the conflicting pair.
The passage shows that when two verses contradict, go to Sunnah; when two hadiths contradict, go to Companions/qiyas.
4
Exemplify with the donkey case
Trace how the hierarchy leads to taqrir al-asl when all proofs (hadiths, analogies) contradict. The water remains pure (original state) and the person remains impure.
This demonstrates the practical outcome: wudu is valid but combined with tayammum due to doubt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النَّبيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ صَلَّى صَلوةَ الْكَسَوْفِ رَكْعَتَيْنِ كُلِّ رَكْعَةٍ بِرُكُوعِ وسجدَتَيْنِ وَرَوَتْ عَائِشَةَ أَنَّهُ صَلاهَا بَارْبَعِ رُكُوعَاتٍ وَاربَعِ سَجْدَاتِ فَيَتَعَارَضَانِ فَيُصَارُ إِلَى الْقَيَاسِ بَعْدَهُ وَهُوَ الاِعْتِبَارُ بِسائر الصلوة وَعِنْدَ الْعِجْزِ يَجِبُ تَقْرِيْرَ الأَصْوَلِ أَى إِذَا عَجِرٌ عَنِ الْمَصِيرِ باضن تَعَارَضَتِ المُتَنَانِ غَالِبُ مَنْ فِيْرَ أَنَّهُ قَالَ لرّسول الله صلى الله عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ لَمْ يَبْقَ مِنْ مَالِي الأمُمَيْرَاتِ فَقَالَ كُلُّ مِنْ سمِيْنَ مَالِكَ فَابَاحَ لَحُوْمَهَا فَلَمَّا وَقَعَ التَّعَارُضُ فِي لُحُومِهَا لَزِمَ الإِسْتِبَاهُ فِي سوْرِهَا لأَنَّهُ مُتَوَلدٌ مِنْهَا. وحُكْمُها بَيْنَ الآيَتَيْنِ الْمَصِيرُ إلى السنة اور معارضے کا حکم یہ ہے کہ جب دو آئوں ترجمہ و تشریح میں ہو تو سنت کی طرف رجوع کیا جائے گا۔ کیوں کہ دو آیتیں جب متعارض ہوں گی تو ساقط ہو جائیں گی۔ اس لئے عمل کرنے کے لئے ان کے مابعد کی طرف جاتا ہوگا اور وہ سنت ہے اور تیسری آیت کی طرف جانا ممکن نہیں ہے کیوں کہ یہ کثرت دلائل کی بنیاد پر ترجیح کی طرف لے جاتا ہے اور وہ جائز نہیں ہے۔ اس کی مثال میں آیت فَاقْرُوا مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنَ الْقُرْآنِ کو آیت وَإِذَا قُرِئَ الْقُرْآنِ فَاسْتَمِعُوا کے ساتھ پیش کیا جاتا ہے کیوں کہ اول آیت اپنے عموم کی وجہ سے مقتدی پر قرآت کو واجب کرتی ہے۔ اور دوسری آیت اپنی خصوص کے سبب مذکورہ حکم کی نفی کرتی ہے۔ حالانکہ دونوں آیتیں نماز کے باب میں وارد ہوئی ہیں۔ لہذا دونوں ساقط العمل ہو جائیں گی پھر اس کے بعد حدیث کی طرف رجوع کیا جائے گا اور وہ حدیث یہ ہے۔ مَنْ كَانَ لَهُ إِمَامٌ فقراءة الإمام قراءة له. وَبَيْنَ السَّنْتَيْنِ الْمَصِيرُ إلى أقوال الصحابہ اور جب دوستوں کے درمیان تعارض ہو تو اقوال صحابہ یا قیاس کی طرف رجوع کیا جائے گا ایام فخر الاسلام نے اس طرح کلمہ او" کے ساتھ ذکر کیا ہے لہذا دونوں اقوال صحابہ اور قیاس میں ترتیب کا لحاظ نہ کیا جائے گا اور بعض لوگوں نے کہا ہے کہ اقوال صحابہ قیاس پر مقدم ہیں برا یہ ہے کہ قیاس مدرک با القیاس ہو یا مدرک با لقیاس نہ ہو۔ اور بعض لوگوں نے کہا ہے کہ ان دونوں اقوال میں تعمیق دی جائے گی۔ کہ اقوال صحابہ فِيْمَا لا يُدْرَكَ بِالْقَيَاسِ میں مقدم ہیں اور مدرک بالقیاس میں قیاس ہم رکھا جائے گا۔ اور اس کی مثال وہ حدیث ہے جسے روایت کیا گیا ہے کہ نبی کریم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے صلوۃ کسوف نے دو رکعتیں پڑھائیں جس میں ایک رکوع اور دو سجدے کئے اور حضرت عائشہ رضی اللہ عنہما نے روایت کیا ہے کہ جناب نبی کریم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے چار رکوع کئے اور چار سجدے لہذا دونوں متعارض ہو گئیں۔ لہذا اس کے بعد قیاس کی طرف رجوع کیا گیا اور وہ یہ ہے کہ صلوۃ کسوف کو دیگر نمازوں کے ساتھ قیاس کیا گیا ہے۔ وَعِنْدَ الْعِجْزِ يَجِبُّ تَقْرِيرُ الاصول اور عجز کے وقت تقریر اصول واجب ہو گی یعنی جب امور مذکورہ میں کتے کی طرف رجوع کرنے سے عاجزی اور مجبوری ظاہر ہو جائے۔ اس طور پر کے دوحہ میں ایک دوسرے سے متعارض ہوں اقوال صحابہ اور قیاس بھی آپس میں تعارض ہوں یا ان چیزوں کے بعد کوئی دلیل موجود نہ ہو تو اس وقت تقریر اصول واجب ہو گی اور ہرٹی کو اس کی اصلیت پر قائم رکھنا ہو گا اور جو چیز جس چیز پر قائم ہے اسے اس پر باقی رکھنا ہوگا۔ كَمَا فِي سُوْرِ الْحِمَارِ جیسے سور حمار (گدھے کے جھوٹے میں) کے باب میں کہ جب تمام دلائل باہم متعارض ہوئے تو تقریر اصول واجب ہو گی کیوں کہ روایت ہے اہلی حمار کا گوشت کھانے سے حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے یوم خیر میں منع فرمایا تھا اور ان ہانڈیوں کے الٹ دینے کا حکم فرمایا جن میں ان کا گوشت پک رہا تھا اور حضرت قالب بن فھر نے روایت کی ہے کہ انھوں نے حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم سے عرض کیا میرے پاس کوئی بال باقی نہیں رہ گیا سوائے چند گدھوں کے اور کچھ باقی نہ رہا۔ آنحضرت صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا کھاؤ تم اپنے نفع دینے والے (موٹے ) مال سے اس حدیث میں آپ نے گدھوں کا کھانا حلال قرار دیا۔ لہذا جب گدھوں کے گوشت کے بارہ میں تعارض واقع ہوا تو ان کے سور کے بارے میں اشتباہ پیدا ہوا کہ کیوں کہ لعاب اسی سے بنتا ہے۔ وَأَيْضًا رَوَى جَابِرٌ أَنَّهُ سَئَلَ انَتَوَصَا بِمَاءٍ هُوَ فُضَالَةُ الْحُمُرِ قَالَ نَعَمْ وَرَوَى أَنَس أَنَّهُ نَهَى عَنِ الْحُمْرِ الأَهْلِيَةِ وَقَالَ إِنَّهَا رِجْسٌ وَهَذَا يَدُلُّ عَلَى فَجَاسَةٍ سُورهَا وَالْقَيَاسِنَانِ أَيْضًا مُتَعَارِضَانِ لانه لايُمْكِنُ الْحَاقَّهُ بِالْعِرقِ لِيَكُونُ طَاهِرًا لِقِلْةٍ الضُّرُورَةِ فِيْهِ وَكَثْرَتِهَا فِي الْعِرْقِ وَلَا يُمْكِنُ الْحَاقُهُ بِاللَّبَنِ لِيَكُونَ نَجْسًا بِجَامِعِ التَّوَلُدِ مِنَ اللَّحْمِ لِوُجُودِ الضَّرُورَةِ فِي السَّوْرِ دُونَ اللَّبَن وَكَذَا لَا يُمْكِنُ الْحَاقَّة بِسوْرِ الْكَلْبِ لِيَكُونَ نَجَسًا لِكَيْن الضَّرُورَةِ فِي الْحِمَارِ دُونَ الْكَلْبِ وَلَا يُمْكِنُ الْحَاقَّة بسور الهرة لِيَكُونَ طَاهِرًا لِوُجُودِ الضَّرُورَةِ فِي الْهرُةَ أَكْثَرِ مِمَّا يَكُونُ فِي الْحِمَارِ فَلَمَّا تَعَارَضَ هَذَا كَلُّهُ وَانْسَدَّ بَابُ التَّرْجِيْحِ وَجَبَ تَقْرِيرُ كُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِن الْمُتَوَضَى وَالْمَاءِ إِلَى أَصْلِهِ فَقِيْلَ إِنَّ الْمَاءَ عُرِفَ طَاهِرًا فِي الْأَصْلِ فَلَا يَتَنَجَّسُ فَوَجَبَ اسْتِعْمَالُ الطَّاهِرِ وَالتَّوْضِي بِهِ وَالأَدَمِنْ لَمَّا كَانَ فِي الْأَصْلِ مُحَدَثًا بَقِيَ كَذَلِكَ وَلَمْ يَزَلْ بِهِ الْحَدَتْ لِلتَّعَارُضِ فَوَجَبَ ضَمُّ التَّيَمُّمِ إِلَيْهِ وَلَا يُقَالُ إِنَّ الْمَاءِ كَان
The Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed the eclipse prayer two rak'ahs, each rak'ah with one bowing and two prostrations. And Aisha narrated that he prayed it with four bowings and four prostrations. So they are contradictory, thus one resorts to analogy after that, and it is considering it analogous to other prayers. And when unable, it is obligatory to establish the original principle: that is, if one is unable to resort to the textual evidence because the two texts are contradictory, and the sayings of the Companions and analogy also contradict, and there is no proof after that, then it is obligatory to establish everything upon its original state and keep what was as it was, as in the case of the leftover water of the donkey. When the proofs became contradictory, it was necessary to establish the original principle. For it is narrated that he forbade the meats of domesticated donkeys on the day of Khaybar and ordered the throwing away of the pots in which their meat was cooked. And Ghalib bin Fihr narrated that he said to the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him: 'I have nothing left of my wealth except some she-donkeys.' He said: 'Eat from the fat of your wealth,' so he permitted their meat. When contradiction occurred regarding their meat, confusion necessarily arose regarding their leftover water because it is generated from them. And the rule between two verses: resort to the Sunnah. The rule of contradiction is: when two verses conflict in meaning and explanation, one resorts to the Sunnah because when two verses are contradictory, they become inoperative. So for action, one must go to what comes after them, and that is the Sunnah. And it is not possible to go to a third verse because that would lead to preference based on abundance of proofs, which is not permissible. An example is the verse 'So recite what is easy of the Quran' and the verse 'And when the Quran is recited, listen to it.' The first verse, due to its generality, makes recitation obligatory upon the follower; the second verse, due to its specificity, negates that ruling, although both verses are in the chapter of prayer. Therefore, both become inoperative, then after that one resorts to the hadith, and that hadith is: 'Whoever has an imam, the recitation of the imam is recitation for him.' And between two hadiths: resort to the sayings of the Companions. And when two hadiths conflict, one resorts to the sayings of the Companions or analogy. Fakhr al-Islam has mentioned it with the word 'or', so no order is observed between sayings of Companions and analogy. Some have said that sayings of Companions are preferred over analogy, regardless of whether the analogy is based on a rational source or not. And some have said that there is a distinction: sayings of Companions are preferred in matters not attainable by analogy, but in matters attainable by analogy, analogy is given precedence. An example is the hadith narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed the eclipse prayer two rak'ahs with one bowing and two prostrations each, and Aisha narrated that he did four bowings and four prostrations. So they contradicted, and after that one resorted to analogy, which is that the eclipse prayer is analogized to other prayers. And when unable, it is obligatory to establish the original principle. That is, when one is unable to resort to the mentioned matters because the two texts contradict each other, the sayings of Companions and analogy also contradict each other, or there is no proof after these, then establishing the original principle is obligatory, and everything must be kept upon its original state, and what is established remains as it is. As in the case of the leftover water of the donkey (su'r al-himar): when all proofs contradicted, establishing the original principle became obligatory. For it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade eating the meat of domesticated donkeys on the day of Khaybar and ordered the overturning of the pots in which their meat was cooking. And Ghalib bin Fihr narrated that he said to the Prophet: 'I have nothing left of my wealth except some donkeys' and the Prophet said: 'Eat from the fat of your wealth,' permitting their meat. So when contradiction occurred regarding their meat, confusion arose regarding their leftover water because saliva is generated from it. And also Jabir narrated that he asked: 'May we perform ablution with water that is leftover of donkeys?' He said: 'Yes.' And Anas narrated that he forbade domesticated donkeys and said: 'They are impure,' which indicates the impurity of their leftover water. And the two analogies also contradict because it is not possible to analogize it to sweat to be pure due to lesser necessity in it and greater necessity in sweat; and it is not possible to analogize it to milk to be impure due to the commonality of generation from meat because the necessity in leftover water exists, not in milk; similarly, it is not possible to analogize it to the leftover water of a dog to be impure because the necessity in the donkey is greater than in the dog; and it is not possible to analogize it to the leftover water of a cat to be pure because the necessity in the cat is greater than in the donkey. So when all this contradicted and the door of preference was closed, it became obligatory to establish each of the one performing ablution and the water upon its original state. So it was said: the water is known to be pure originally, so it does not become impure; thus it is obligatory to use the pure water and perform ablution with it. And the person, since he was originally in a state of minor impurity, remains so, and his impurity is not removed due to the contradiction; therefore, it is obligatory to combine tayammum with it. And it cannot be said that the water was...
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage is a classical Hanafi usul al-fiqh discussion on the rules for resolving contradictions (ta'arud) between different types of evidence. The commentator explains the hierarchy: when two Quranic verses contradict each other and cannot be harmonized, both become inoperative and one must resort to the Sunnah. The example given is the apparent conflict between the general command to recite Quran in prayer and the command to listen when Quran is recited. Both apply in the context of prayer, so they cancel each other, and the hadith 'The imam's recitation suffices for the follower' resolves the issue. When two hadiths contradict, one resorts to either the sayings of the Companions or analogy (qiyas), without a fixed order according to Fakhr al-Islam. Some scholars give priority to Companions' sayings, others distinguish based on whether the matter is rational or not. The eclipse prayer example illustrates: conflicting hadiths about the number of bowings lead to analogizing the eclipse prayer to regular prayers. When all evidence fails and the door of preference (tarjih) is closed, the principle of 'taqrir al-asl' (establishing the original ruling) applies. This is demonstrated in the case of a donkey's leftover water (su'r al-himar): conflicting hadiths and analogies regarding purity lead to the conclusion that the water remains pure (as originally known) and the person remains in need of purification, thus combining wudu with tayammum. This reflects the Hanafi approach of preserving original states when certainty is impossible.

Key Terms
تعارض (ta'arud): Contradiction or conflict between two evidences that cannot be reconciled, requiring recourse to a lower-level evidence or original principle.
تقرير الأصل (taqrir al-asl): The legal principle that when evidence is inconclusive, every matter is presumed to remain in its original state (e.g., water is pure, a person is in a state of impurity) until contrary proof is established.
سور الحمار (su'r al-himar): The water left after a donkey drinks from a container. Its ruling (pure or impure) was disputed among companions and later scholars; this passage uses it as an example of contradictory evidence requiring taqrir al-asl.
أقوال الصحابة (aqwal al-sahaba): Sayings of the Companions of the Prophet; considered a source of law when Quran and Sunnah are absent or contradictory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling when two Quranic verses contradict each other?
A) Both are applied in different contexts.
B) Both become inoperative and one resorts to the Sunnah.
C) The later verse abrogates the earlier.
D) The more specific verse overrides the general.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi method for ta'arud provides a clear hierarchy: Quran → Sunnah → Companions/Qiyas → Taqrir al-Asl, ensuring systematic resolution of conflicting proofs.

Bayan al-Darurah: Types and Legal Implications
Explaining bayan al-darurah and its subtypes with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four types of bayan al-darurah and apply the Hanafi principle that silence in necessity constitutes valid legal clarification.

Core Idea
Silence becomes binding clarification when necessity requires it.

This passage defines bayan al-darurah, a unique type of legal clarification arising through necessity rather than explicit speech. While silence is not inherently communicative, Hanafi usul recognizes specific contexts where it carries legal weight. You will learn the four subtypes, from implied speech to tacit approval, and see how they operate in Quranic verses, Prophetic practice, and everyday transactions.

Guided Path
1
Define bayan al-darurah
Identify the term and understand that it is clarification obtained through necessity, occurring via silence—contrast with explicit bayan tafsir.
Silence is not originally placed for clarification, but necessity renders it informative.
2
List the four subtypes
Enumerate: (1) silence in status of speech, (2) silence indicating approval from context, (3) silence to prevent deception, (4) silence due to prolixity.
Each subtype has distinct conditions and examples.
3
Analyze the first subtype
Examine the Quranic inheritance verse: 'And his parents inherit him, so for his mother is the third.' The father's share is clarified by necessity without explicit mention.
This shows how silence can function like speech through necessary implication.
4
Analyze the second subtype
Examine Prophetic silence upon witnessed actions (e.g., mudarabah, partnerships) indicating permissibility, and Companion silence as consensus when able to object.
Conditions include ability to object and the agent being Muslim.
5
Analyze the third subtype and intra-madhhab dispute
Master's silence when seeing his slave trade: Hanafi view holds it becomes permission (idhn) to prevent deception; Imam Zufar disagrees, citing possible anger.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf): slave is considered authorized in Hanafi school.
6
Analyze the fourth subtype
Example: 'I owe you one hundred and dirham' – the conjunction clarifies that the hundred is also dirhams, avoiding repetition due to prolixity.
Prolixity leads to omission for conciseness, but the meaning is clear by necessity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أَوْ بَيَانُ ضَرُورَةٍ عَطَفَ عَلَى قَوْلِهِ بَيَانُ تَفْسِيرٍ أَيِ الْبَيَانُ الْحَاصِلُ بِطَرِيقِ الضَّرُورَةِ وَهُوَ نَوْعُ بَيَانٍ يَقَعُ بِمَا لَمْ يُوضَعْ لَهُ أَيِ السُّكُوتُ إِنَّ الْمَوْضُوعَ لِلْبَيَانِ هُوَ الْكَلَامُ دُونَ السُّكُوتِ وَهُوَ إِمَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ فِي حُكْمِ الْمَنْطُوقِ أَيِ الْبَيَانُ إِمَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ فِي حُكْمِ الْمَنْطُوقِ أَوِ الْكَلَامِ الْمُقَدَّرِ الْمَسْكُوتِ تَعْيِينِ نَصِيبِ كُلٍّ مِنْهُمَا ثُمَّ تَخْصِيصُ الْأُمِّ بِالثُّلُثِ صَارَ بَيَانًا لِأَنَّ الْأَبَ يَسْتَحِقُّ الْبَاقِيَ فَكَأَنَّهُ قَالَ فَلِأُمِّهِ الثُّلُثُ وَلِأَبِيهِ الْبَاقِي. أَوْ ثَبَتَ بِدَلَالَةِ حَالِ الْمُتَكَلِّمِ كَسُكُوتِ صَاحِبِ الشَّرْعِ عِنْدَ أَمْرٍ يُعَايِنُهُ عَنِ التَّغْيِيرِ يَعْنِي أَنَّ الرَّسُولَ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ إِذَا رَأَى أَمْرًا يُبَاشِرُونَهُ وَيُعَامِلُونَهُ كَالْمُضَارَبَاتِ وَالشَّرُكَاتِ أَوْ رَأَى شَيْئًا يُبَاعُ فِي السُّوقِ وَلَمْ يُنْكِرْ عَلَيْهِ عُلِمَ أَنَّهُ مُبَاحٌ فَسُكُوتُهُ أُقِيمَ مَقَامَ الْأَمْرِ بِالْإِبَاحَةِ وَفِي حُكْمِهِ سُكُوتُ الصَّحَابَةِ بِشَرْطِ الْقُدْرَةِ عَلَى الْإِنْكَارِ وَكَوْنِ الْفَاعِلِ مُسْلِمًا كَمَا رُوِيَ أَنَّ أُمَةً أَبْقَتْ وَتَزَوَّجَتْ رَجُلًا فَوَلَدَتْ أَوْلَادًا ثُمَّ جَاءَ مَوْلَاهَا وَرَفَعَ هَذِهِ الْقَضِيَّةَ إِلَى عُمَرَ فَقَضَى بِهَا لِمَوْلَاهَا وَقَضَى عَلَى الْأَبِ أَنْ يَفْدِيَ عَنِ الْأَوْلَادِ وَيَأْخُذَهُمْ بِالْقِيمَةِ وَسَكَتَ عَنْ ضِمَانِ مَنَافِعِهَا وَمَنَافِعِ أَوْلَادِهَا وَكَانَ ذَلِكَ بِمَحْضَرٍ مِنَ الصَّحَابَةِ فَكَانَ إِجْمَاعًا عَلَى أَنَّ مَنَافِعَ وَلَدِ الْمَغْرُورِ لَا تُضْمَنُ بِالْإِتْلَافِ. أَوْ ثَبَتَ ضَرُورَةَ دَفْعِ الْغُرُورِ عَنِ النَّاسِ وَهُوَ حَرَامٌ كَسُكُوتِ الْمَوَالِي حِينَ رَأَى عَبْدًا يَبِيعُ وَيَشْتَرِي فَإِنَّهُ يَصِيرُ إِذْنًا لَهُ فِي التِّجَارَةِ عِنْدَنَا لِأَنَّهُ لَوْ لَمْ يَكُنْ مَأْذُونًا يَتَضَرَّرُ النَّاسُ بِهِ وَدَفْعُ الْغُرُورِ عَنْهُمْ وَاجِبٌ وَقَالَ زُفَرُ لَا يَكُونُ مَأْذُونًا لِأَنَّ سُكُوتَهُ يَحْتَمِلُ أَنْ يَكُونَ الرِّضَا بِتَصَرُّفِهِ وَأَنْ يَكُونَ لِفَرْطِ الْغَيْظِ وَالْمُحْتَمِلُ لَا يَكُونُ حُجَّةً. أَوْ ثَبَتَ ضَرُورَةَ كَثْرَةِ الْكَلَامِ أَي كَثْرَةِ اسْتِعْمَالِهِ أَوْ طُولِ عِبَارَتِهِ يَدُلُّ عَلَى مَا هُوَ الْمُرَادُ كَقَوْلِهِ لَهُ عَلَيَّ مِائَةٌ وَدِرْهَمٌ فَإِنَّ الْعَطْفَ جُعِلَ بَيَانًا لِأَنَّ الْمِائَةَ أَيْضًا دَرَاهِمُ فَكَأَنَّهُ قَالَ لَهُ عَلَيَّ مِائَةُ دِرْهَمٍ وَدِرْهَمٌ وَإِنَّمَا حُذِفَ لِطُولِ
Or clarification by necessity, attached to his statement 'clarification of interpretation', meaning the clarification obtained by way of necessity, and it is a type of clarification that occurs by what is not placed for it, i.e., silence, for that which is placed for clarification is speech not silence. And it is either in the status of the spoken word... like His statement 'And his parents inherit him, so for his mother is the third'... Or it is established by the implication of the speaker's state, like the silence of the Lawgiver upon seeing an action... Or it is established by the necessity of removing deception from people... Or it is established by the necessity of prolixity of speech...
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage defines and elaborates on 'bayan al-darurah' (clarification by necessity), a type of bayan where the clarification is derived from necessity rather than explicit speech. It begins by stating that this type is attached to 'bayan tafsir' (clarification by interpretation). The author explains that it occurs through silence, which is not originally designed for clarification. Then he divides it into four categories. The first is silence that has the status of spoken words, illustrated by the Quranic verse on inheritance: when Allah says 'if his parents inherit him, to his mother one-third,' the father's two-thirds (or remaining) is clarified by necessity. The second is silence established by the implied state of the speaker, like the Prophet's silence upon seeing permissible transactions (mudarabah, partnerships), which indicates approval. The same applies to the Companions' silence when they are able to object, as in the case where Caliph Umar ruled that a runaway slave-girl's master gets her and the father pays for the children, but was silent about compensation for her services—this silence indicated consensus that such compensation is not due. The third is silence out of necessity to prevent deception, such as a master's silence when seeing his slave trading; in the Hanafi view, this becomes permission for the slave to trade to prevent people from being misled (since if the slave were unauthorized, people would suffer). Imam Zufar disagreed, arguing that silence could be due to anger, so it is not binding. The fourth is silence due to prolixity, such as saying 'I owe you one hundred and dirham' where the conjunction clarifies that the hundred is also dirhams (i.e., one hundred and one dirhams), avoiding repetition. The text thus provides a comprehensive analysis of how silence can serve as a legal clarification.

Key Terms
بيان الضرورة (bayan al-darurah): A type of clarification (bayan) that occurs through necessity, typically via silence, making the silent person's implication legally binding.
سكوت (sukut): Silence that, under certain conditions, serves as a legal indicator or clarification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what legal effect does a master's silence have when he sees his slave buying and selling in the market?
A) The slave is considered not authorized (ghayr ma'dhun) until explicit permission is given.
B) The slave becomes authorized (ma'dhun) to trade due to necessity to prevent deception.
C) The silence is irrelevant and requires no legal consideration.
D) The slave is fined for trading without permission.

Key Takeaway
Bayan al-darurah is a critical Hanafi usul concept that validates silence as legal clarification under necessity, encompassing four distinct subtypes with specific conditions.

The Invalidity of Deduction from Lack of Evidence (Adam al-Wijdan) as a Legal Proof
Discusses the permissibility of using lack of evidence as a proof in legal reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when an argument uses lack of evidence as a proof and evaluate its validity according to Hanafi usul, citing the Quranic evidence from Surah al-Baqarah.

Core Idea
Lack of evidence is not a valid proof in Shari'ah — the burden of proof applies to both affirmation and negation.

This lesson examines the principle of istidlal bi 'adam al-wijdan, or deduction from lack of evidence. While some argue that the absence of textual proof indicates permissibility, the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools firmly reject this as a method of legal reasoning. We will explore the Quranic basis for this rejection and learn why the burden of proof cannot be satisfied by mere non-discovery.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Claim
Identify what istidlal bi 'adam al-wijdan means and note the initial argument: some scholars claim it is valid in Shar'i matters because of the Prophet's statement in Surah al-An'am.
The claim is that lack of evidence can serve as proof for a ruling, especially for permissibility.
2
Examine the Alleged Support
Recall the verse from Surah al-An'am (6:145) where the Prophet says 'I do not find in what has been revealed to me anything forbidden.'
Some interpret this as using lack of evidence to declare something not forbidden.
3
Present the Hanafi Response
Understand the Hanafi rebuttal: this verse does not establish a general principle; it is a specific case. The general rule is from Surah al-Baqarah (2:111), which demands proof for all claims, including negations.
The verse commands: 'Say, bring your proof, if you are truthful.'
4
Understand the Rational vs. Shar'i Distinction
Some scholars differentiate between rational matters (where absence of evidence is insufficient because existence/non-existence requires proof) and Shar'i matters (which are based on transmission). However, Hanafis reject this distinction.
Hanafis hold that both types of matters require positive proof.
5
Conclude with the Accepted Position
State the final Hanafi (and Shafi'i) ruling: adam al-wijdan is not a valid proof for either affirmation or negation in Shari'ah.
The mufta bihi position is that both parties must provide evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
میں نہیں پاتا اس چیز میں کہ میری طرف وحی فرمائی گئی ہے کسی چیز کو حرام اس آیت میں اللہ نے اپنے پیغمبر عليه السلام كوقل لا اجد فيها أوحى إلى شقی سے استدلال کرنا بطور دلیل کے بتایا کہ یہ حرام نہیں ہے۔ دیکھئے اللہ تعالی نے اس آیت میں اپنے نبی عے کو چیزوں کے حرام نہ ہونے پر عدم وحدان کی دلیل سے استدلال کرنا بتایا ہے۔ اور بعضوں نے کہا ہے کہ عدم دلیل سے استدلال احکام شرعیہ میں جائز ہے مگر امور عقلیہ میں جائز نہیں ہے اس وجہ سے امور عقلیہ میں کسی چیز کی نفی یا اثبات کادعونی در اصل اس کے وجود یا عدم کا دعوی کرنا ہوتا ہے۔ جب کہ نفس الا مرضی کا وجود و عدم محتاج دلیل ہوا کرتے ہیں اسلئے حکم کا مکہ کرنے قبل استدلال ضروری ہے عدم وجدان دلیل ھی کی نفی کرنے کے لئے ناکافی ہوتا ہے بخلاف ان امور کے جو شرعی ہیں۔ ان میں استدلال کی ضرورت نہیں ہے کیونکہ وہ نقل سے ثابت ہوتے ہیں۔ لیکن علماء احناف و علماء شواقع دونوں کے یہاں عدم وجدان دلیل سے استدلال درست نہیں ہوتا۔ نہ حکم سے اثبات میں اور نہ یکم کی نفی میں۔ ان کی دلیل قرآن مجید کی یہ آیت ہے ۔ وَقَالُو لَن يَدْخُلُ الْجَنَّةَ الخ - اور یہ لوگ کہتے ہیں کہ جنت میں ہر گز نہ جائیں گے مگر وہ لوگ جو میہودی ہوں، یا نصرانی ہوں، یہ آرزو میں باندھ لی ہیں انہوں نے آپ فرمادیجئے دلیل لے آؤ اگر تم سچے ہو۔ اس آیت میں اللہ تعالیٰ نے آنحضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم سے فرمایا کہ آپ اپنے دعوے پر اثبات و نفی دونوں میں دلیل کا مطالبہ کیجئے۔
I do not find in what has been revealed to me anything forbidden... In this verse, Allah taught His Prophet, peace be upon him, to argue using lack of evidence as a proof that it is not forbidden. And some have said that deduction from lack of evidence is permissible in Shar'i matters but not in rational matters because in rational matters, claiming negation or affirmation of something is essentially a claim of its existence or non-existence, and the existence or non-existence of the thing itself requires proof, so the lack of finding evidence is insufficient to negate it, unlike Shar'i matters which are established by transmission. However, according to both the Hanafi and Shafi'i scholars, deduction from lack of evidence is not valid, neither for affirmation nor negation. Their proof is this verse of the Qur'an: 'And they say, None shall enter Paradise except one who is a Jew or a Christian. That is their wish. Say, Bring your proof, if you are truthful.' In this verse, Allah commanded His Prophet, peace be upon him, to demand proof for both affirmation and negation.
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage discusses the principle of istidlal bi 'adam al-wijdan (deduction from lack of evidence). The author begins by referencing the Qur'anic verse from Surah al-An'am (6:145) where Allah teaches the Prophet to state that he does not find in revelation anything forbidden, using the lack of evidence as a basis for the ruling of permissibility. Some scholars argued that this method is valid in Shar'i matters but not in rational ones. However, both the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools reject it entirely. They cite Surah al-Baqarah (2:111) where Allah commands the Prophet to demand proof from those who make claims, including negations. This establishes that both affirmation and negation require external evidence, and lack of evidence cannot serve as a proof.

Key Terms
عدم الوجدان (adam al-wijdan): Lack of finding or lack of evidence for a ruling

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on using lack of evidence (adam al-wijdan) as a proof in Shar'i matters?
A) It is valid
B) It is not valid
C) It is valid only for affirmations
D) It is valid only for negations

Key Takeaway
Lack of evidence is not a proof in Shari'ah; both affirmation and negation require positive evidence.

Mu'aradah and Qalb in Hanafi Usul
Defining mu'aradah and its first type, qalb.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define mu'aradah, distinguish its two types, and apply the concept of qalb to reverse an opponent's analogy.

Core Idea
Qalb turns the opponent's own proof into a weapon against him by swapping cause and ruling.

In this passage, the author defines mu'aradah (counter-argument) as establishing a proof that contradicts what the opponent's proof has established. He then divides it into two types: one where the same proof is used (qalb) and another where a different proof is brought. The first type, qalb, is particularly powerful because it not only counters but also reveals a contradiction in the opponent's reasoning. The passage uses an example from the Shafi'i school on zina punishments to illustrate how Hanafi usul employs qalb. This lesson will break down the definition and demonstrate the mechanism of qalb, a key tool in Hanafi jadal.

Guided Path
1
Define mu'aradah
Read the first lines: 'wa amma al-mu'aradatu fa-naw'an...' Note that mu'aradah means establishing a proof (dalil) that is contrary to what the opponent's proof has established. Identify that it has two types.
The text says mu'aradah is 'iqamat al-dalil 'ala khilaf ma tam mat al-dalil 'alayhi al-khasm'.
2
Distinguish the two types
The first type is when the same original proof is used against the opponent (qalb). The second type is when a different proof is brought. Recognize that the passage focuses on the first type.
If the proof is the same, it is the first type; otherwise the second.
3
Understand qalb as reversal
Qalb is derived from turning a bowl upside down. It means making the illah (cause) into a hukm (ruling) and the hukm into an illah. The text explains that this only works if the description (wasf) in the qiyas can be transformed into a legal ruling, not a pure description.
The example of flogging and stoning illustrates this: flogging (hukm) becomes the illah for stoning in the Shafi'i qiyas, but Hanafis reverse it.
4
Apply the example of zina punishments
Analyze the Shafi'i analogy: disbelievers are like Muslims in that both receive flogging for virgin zina, so they should also receive stoning when married. The Hanafi response via qalb: since Islam is a condition for ihsan (required for stoning), the flogging ruling cannot be the illah for stoning; rather, the absence of Islam blocks the analogy. Thus, the same proof (the analogy) is turned against the Shafi'i claim.
This demonstrates how qalb functions in practice: the opponent's own reasoning is used to disprove his conclusion.

ثُمَّ يَعْدَ الْفَراغِ مِنْ دَفْعِ النَّقْضِ شَرَعَ فِي الْمُعَارَضَةِ الْوَارِدَةِ عَلَى الْعِلْةِ الْمُوثْرَةِ فَقَالَ وَأَمَّا الْمُعَارَضَةُ فَتَوْعَانِ وهِيَ اِقَامَةُ الدَّلِيل على خلاف ماتَامَ الدِّلِيلُ عَليهِ الْخَصْمَ فَإِنْ كَانَ هُوَ ذَالِكَ الدَّلِيلُ الأَولُ بِعَيْنِهِ فَهُوَ النّوع الأول والأ فَهو النوع الثَّانِي فَالنَّوع الأول الأَوَّلُ مُعارضةٌ فِيهَا مُنَافِضَةٌ وَهِيَ الْقَلْبُ فِي إِصْطلاحِ الأَصُولِ وَالْمُنَاظَرَةِ مَعًا فَهُوَ مِنْ حَيْثُ أَنَّهُ يَدلُّ عَلَى نَقِيض مُدَّعَى الْمُعَلِّلِ يسمى مُعَارَضَةٌ وَمِنْ حَيثُ أَنْ دَلِيْلَهُ لَمْ يُصلَحْ دَلِيْلاً لَهُ بَلْ صَارَ دَلِيلاً لِلْخَصم يُسمى مُنَا قِضَةٌ لِخَلَلِ فِي الدِّلِيلِ وَلَكِنَّ الْمُعَارَضَةُ أَصَلَّ فِيْهِ وَالفَقْضِ ضِمْتِى إِنَّ النَّقْصُ الْقَصَدِي لَآيَرِدُ عَلَى الدِّلِيلِ الْمُؤثِرِ وِلذَالِكَ سُمّى مُعَارَضَةٌ فِيهَا الْمُنَاقَضَةُ وَلَمْ يُسمَ مُنَاقَضَةٌ فِيهَا الْمُعَارَضَةُ . وَهُوَ نَوْعَانِ أَحَدُهُمَا قَلْبُ العِلْةِ حُكْمًا والحكم علةٌ وَهُوَ مَاخوذ مِنْ قَلب الْقَصْعَةِ أَىٰ جَعَل أَعْلَاهَا أَسْفَلَها وَأَسْفَلَهَا أَعْلَاهَا فَالْعِلْةُ أعْلَى وَالْحُكْمُ أسفل وَهُوَ لا يَتَحَقَّقُ إِلَّا إِذا جُعِلَ الْوَصْفُ فِي الْقَيَاسِ حُكْمًا شَرْعِيًا يَعْقِلُ الإِنْقِلابَ لَا الْوَصْف الْمَحِضَ الَّذِى لا يُقْبِلُهُ كَقَوْلِهِمْ أَي السَّافَعِيَةِ إِنَّ الْكُفَّارَ جِئْسٌ يُجْلَدٌ بِكَرَهِمْ مِائَةً فَيُرْجَمُ ثَبِتُهُمْ كَالْمُسْلِمِيْنَ يَعْنِي أَنَّ الإِسْلامَ لَيْسَ بِشَرِطٍ لِلإِحْصَانِ فَكَمَا أَنَّ الْمُسْلِمِيْنَ يُرْجُمُ بَعْضُهُمْ وَيُجْلَدَ بَعْضُهُمْ فَكَذَا الْكُفَّارُ فَجَعِلَ جَلد الْمِائَةِ عِلَّةٌ لِرَجْمِ الشَّيْبِ بِالْقَيَاسِ عَلَى الْمُسْلِمِينَ وَهُوَ فِي الْوَاقِعِ حُكُمْ شَرْعِيُّ وَعِنْدَنَا لَمَّا كَانَ الإسلامُ شَرْطًا لِلأَحْصَانِ وَالْكُفَّارِ لَيْسَ عَلَيْهِمْ إِلا الْجَلْد كرا كَانَ أَوْثَنَا عَارَضْنَا هُمْ بِالْقَلْبِ فَنَقُولُ الْمُسْلِمُونَ إِنَّمَا يُجْلَهُ بَكْرُهُمْ مَائَةٌ لأَنْهُ

پھر مصنف نقض کے دفع کرنے کے بعد اب اس معارضہ کو بیان کر رہے ہیں جو علی مؤثرہ پر وارد ہوتا ہے۔ پس فرمایا : وَالمُعَارَضَةُ فَنَوعان معارضہ کی دو قسمیں ہیں۔ معارضہ کہتے ہیں مخالف نے جس نے جس دعوے پر دلیل قائم کی ہے اس کے خلاف پر دلیل قائم کرنا۔ اس کی دو صورتیں ہیں۔ اول مخالف کی بیان کردہ دلیل ہی بعینہ اس کی دلیل ہے۔ تو یہ معارضہ کی قسم اول ہے اور بعینہ مخالف کی دلیل نہیں ہے بلکہ معارض نے دوسری دلیل دی ہے تو یہ دوسری قسم ہے۔
فَالنوع الأول نس نوع ایسا معارضہ ہے جو مناقضہ کو بھی شامل ہو۔ اس کا دوسرا نام قلب ہے علماء اصول اور ارباب مناظرہ دونوں کی اصطلاح میں۔ پس اس حیثیت سے کہ یہ معلل کے دعوے کے خلاف پر دلالت کرتا ہے اس کا نام معارصہ ہے۔ چونکہ معلل کی دلیل میں خلل واقع ہو گیا ہے۔ اس لیے خود معلل ہی کے حق میں دلیل نہیں رہی۔ بلکہ اس کے معارض کی دلیل بن گئی ہے۔ اس کا نام مناقضہ رکھا جاتا ہے۔ ولكن المعارضة أصل فيه ۔ مگر اس میں اصل معارضہ ہے اور ضمناً اس میں نقض پیدا ہو گیا ہے کیونکہ نقض ارادی اور قصدی علت موثرہ پر وارد نہیں ہوا کرتا۔ اسی وجہ سے اس کا نام الْمُعَارَضَةٍ فِيهَا المناقضة رکھا جاتا ہے اور مناقضه فيها المعارضه نام نہیں رکھا گیا۔
Then after finishing repelling the naqd, he began the mu'aradah that comes upon the effective cause. He said: As for mu'aradah, it is of two types. It is the establishment of a proof contrary to what the opponent's proof has established. If it is that same original proof itself, then it is the first type; otherwise it is the second type. The first type is a mu'aradah that contains a contradiction (munaqadah), and it is called qalb in the terminology of both usul and disputation. Insofar as it indicates the opposite of what the mu'allil claims, it is called mu'aradah; insofar as his proof is no longer valid for him but has become a proof for the opponent, it is called munaqadah because of a flaw in the proof. But mu'aradah is primary in it, and naqd is incidental because intentional naqd does not occur upon the effective cause. Therefore it is called 'mu'aradah that contains munaqadah' and not 'munaqadah that contains mu'aradah'. And it is of two types: one is qalb of the illah as a ruling and the ruling as an illah. It is derived from turning over a bowl, i.e., making its top its bottom and its bottom its top. So the illah is the top and the ruling is the bottom. It is only realized when the description in the qiyas is made a legal ruling that can be transformed, not a pure description that does not accept transformation. An example is the saying of the Shafi'is: The disbelievers (who commit zina) are to be flogged a hundred lashes as virgins, and their married ones are to be stoned, like Muslims. They mean that Islam is not a condition for ihsan. So just as among the Muslims, some are stoned and some are flogged, so too the disbelievers. So they made the flogging of a hundred a cause for stoning the married by analogy to Muslims, while in reality it is a legal ruling. According to us, since Islam is a condition for ihsan, and the disbelievers have nothing but flogging, whether they are virgins or married, we counter them with qalb and say: Muslims, their virgins are only flogged a hundred because... [Urdu: Then after the author finished repelling the naqd, he now explains the mu'aradah that comes upon the effective cause. He said: 'Wa al-mu'aradah fanaw'an'. Mu'aradah is of two types. Mu'aradah means to establish a proof contrary to the claim on which the opponent has established his proof. It has two forms. First, it is exactly the same proof that the opponent mentioned; that is the first type. Or it is not exactly the same proof, but the challenger provides a different proof; that is the second type. The first type is a mu'aradah that also includes munaqadah. Its other name is qalb in the terminology of both usul scholars and disputants. From the aspect that it indicates the opposite of the mu'allil's claim, it is called mu'aradah. Since the mu'allil's proof has become defective, it is no longer a proof for him but becomes a proof for his opponent; it is called munaqadah. But mu'aradah is primary in it, and naqd is incidental, because intentional naqd does not occur upon the effective cause. For that reason, it is called 'mu'aradah containing munaqadah' and not 'munaqadah containing mu'aradah'.]
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage defines mu'aradah (counter-argument) in usul al-fiqh and introduces its two types. The first type is qalb (reversal), which is both a mu'aradah and a munaqadah (contradiction) because the same proof that the opponent used becomes a proof against him. The author explains that qalb is called such because it turns the illah into a ruling and the ruling into an illah, like turning a bowl upside down. The second type (not detailed here) is a different proof. The example provided from the Shafi'i school illustrates qalb: The Shafi'is argue that disbelievers, like Muslims, are to be stoned if married, because they receive the same flogging for virginity, using an analogy. The Hanafi response, via qalb, argues that since Islam is a condition for ihsan (marital integrity for stoning), and disbelievers are not Muslims, the only punishment for them is flogging regardless of marital status. Thus, the Shafi'i's own analogy is reversed to disprove their claim. This lesson critically refines the understanding of how mu'aradah functions in jadal (disputation).

Key Terms
معارضة (mu'aradah): The establishment of a proof contrary to what the opponent's proof has established; it is of two types: qalb (reversal) and other (different proof).
قلب (qalb): The first type of mu'aradah, where the same proof that the opponent used becomes a proof against him, turning the illah into a ruling and vice versa.
مناقضة (munaqadah): A contradiction within the opponent's own proof: his proof no longer supports his claim but rather supports the challenger's claim.
نقض (naqd): An intentional refutation that attacks the effective cause directly; the passage notes it does not apply to the effective cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the definition of qalb (the first type of mu'aradah)?
A) Presenting a completely new proof against the opponent.
B) The same proof that the opponent used becomes a proof against him, turning the illah into a ruling.
C) Rejecting the opponent's proof without any counter-argument.
D) Showing that the opponent's illah does not apply to the original case.

Key Takeaway
Mu'aradah is a counter-proof; its first type, qalb, uses the opponent's own proof to reverse the illah and hukm, exposing a contradiction in his reasoning.

Qalb al-Illa: Inverting Cause and Effect in Hanafi Usul
Explains the first type of qalb and its application in a dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and apply the first type of qalb (qalb al-illa hukman wa al-hukm illa) as a valid objection in Hanafi usul, and distinguish it from inference (istidlal) as an escape.

Core Idea
Qalb al-illa invalidates causation only when equality exists; otherwise, inference escapes inversion.

This passage introduces the first type of qalb (inversion of cause and effect) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. You will see how the Hanafis counter the Shafi'i claim that lashing (jald) is the cause for stoning (rajm) by inverting the relationship. The text also presents an escape (mukhlis) from qalb by framing arguments as inference (istidlal) rather than causation. Understanding these nuances sharpens your ability to evaluate causal arguments in qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Define the first type of qalb
Identify the structure: the opponent's alleged cause is inverted into the ruling, and the ruling into the cause. This challenges the asymmetry of causation.
This works only if the two items are equal in the relevant properties.
2
Analyze the rajm-jald example
Examine the Shafi'i claim that jald is the cause for rajm among Muslims. The Hanafi response inverts: rajm is the cause for jald. This is an instance of qalb.
Note the condition: The Hanafis argue there is no equality (musawa) because rajm has extra conditions.
3
Understand the escape (mukhlis) through istidlal
If one frames the argument as inference (istidlal) rather than causation, the opponent cannot invert because in inference both sides can be evidence for each other (like fire and smoke).
The text says this escape does not help the Shafi'i because of the lack of equality.
4
Apply the concept to the fasting example
The Hanafi argument: fasting is an act of worship that obligates by extent (qadr), so it becomes binding when commenced. If the opponent inverts (saying it binds by vow because it binds by commencement), the Hanafi replies that equality exists, so inference can be used and qalb is harmless.
This shows that equality is the key condition for qalb to succeed or fail.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يَرْجَمُ تَيْبِهِمْ أى لأنسلْمُ أَنَّ الْجَلْدَ عَلْةُ لِلرَّجم فِى الْمُسْلِمِينَ بَلْ الرّجمُ عَلة لِلْجَلْدُ فِيهِمْ فَهَذِهِ مُعَارِضَةٌ لأَنَّهَا تَدَلُّ عَلى خِلافِ مُدْعِى المُعَلِّل الذي هُوَ رَجم الَّذِئ قَيْبهم وفِيهَا مُنَاقَضَةٌ لِدَلِيْلِهِمْ بِأَنَّهُ لا يَصْلَحُ عِلَّة وَالْمُخَلص مِنْهُ يَعْنِي أَنْ مَنْ أَرَادَ أَنْ لايَرِدَ عَلَى عِلْتِهِ الْقَلْبُ فِي الْمَالِ فَطَرِيقَة مِنَ الابْتِدَاءِ أَنْ يُخْرِجَ الْكَلامُ مَخْرَجَ الاستدلال فَإِنَّهُ يُمْكِنُ أَنْ يَكُونَ الشَّيْءُ دَلِيْلاً عَلَى شَيْءٍ وَذَالِكَ الشيءُ يَكُونُ دَلَيْلاً عَلَيْهِ كَالنَّارِ مَعَ الدُّخَانِ بخلاف العِليَةِ فَإِنْهَ يَتَعَيْنُ أَنْ يَكُونَ أَحَدُهُمَا علةٌ وَالآخَرُ مَعْلُولاً فَالقَلبُ يَضُرُّهُ ولكن هذ المخلص لا يُنْفَعُ هَبْنَا لِلشافعي إذلا مُساوَاةَ بَيْنَهُما لأن الرّجمَ عُقُوبَةٌ غَلِيلَةٌ وَلَهُ شروط وَالْجَلْدَ لَيْسَ كَذَالِك. وَهُوَ نَوْعَانِ أَحَدَها قلب العلة حكماً والحُكْمَ عِلة. وَيَنْفَعُنَا لَوْ قُلْنَا الصَّوْمُ عِبَادَةٌ تَلُومُ بِالقَدْرِ فَتَلزم بالشروع إِذْ لَو قَلْبَ الْخَصْمُ فَيَقُولُ إنَّمَا لاَمُ بالنذر لأنه يلزمُ بالشروع قُلْنَا بَيْنَهُمَا مُسارَاةٌ يُمْكِنُ أَنْ يَسْتَدِلُ بِحَالِ يَلْزَمُ كُلِّ مِّنْهُمَا عَلى الآخرِ وَلَاضَيْرَ فِيْهِ
They stone their married ones [meaning?] we do not accept that lashing is the cause for stoning among Muslims, rather stoning is the cause for lashing among them. So this is a counterargument because it indicates the opposite of what the claimant of causation claims, which is the stoning of the one who is married among them, and in it there is a contradiction of their proof in that it is not suitable as a cause. The escape from it means that whoever wants that qalb does not apply to his cause in [the area of] wealth, his method from the beginning is to present his speech in the form of inference (istidlal), for it is possible for something to be evidence for something else and that other thing to be evidence for it, like fire and smoke, unlike causation, for in it one of them must be the cause and the other the effect; so qalb would harm him. But this escape does not benefit us given [against] al-Shafi'i, since there is no equality between them because stoning is a severe punishment and has conditions, while lashing is not like that. And it is of two types: one is inverting the cause into a ruling and the ruling into a cause. And it benefits us if we say: fasting is an act of worship that obligates by extent, so it becomes binding by commencement; if the opponent inverts and says: it only becomes binding by vow because it becomes binding by commencement, we say: between them there is equality, so one can infer from each of them the other, and there is no harm in that.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
Passage type: Explanation of qalb (inversion) in legal argumentation, specifically the first type (qalb al-illa). The author presents the Shafi'i argument that lashing (jald) is the cause for stoning (rajm) among Muslims, and then the Hanafi counterargument that stoning is instead the cause for lashing. This is an instance of qalb because the opponent's causal relation is inverted. The text then discusses an escape (mukhlis) for the one who presents his argument as inference (istidlal) rather than causation (ta'lil), because in inference it is possible for two things to be evidence for each other, but in causation one must be the cause and the other the effect. However, this escape does not help the Shafi'i because there is no equality between stoning and lashing due to their different severity and conditions. The author then introduces the two types of qalb, focusing on the first type: inverting the cause into a ruling and the ruling into a cause. A further example is given regarding fasting: if one argues that fasting is an act of worship that obligates by extent, so it becomes binding by commencement, the opponent could invert and say it becomes binding by vow because it becomes binding by commencement. The reply is that if there is equality between the two, then inference is possible without harm. The Hanafi position is that qalb is a valid objection against causality, but it only applies when there is equality between the two things; otherwise it fails.

Key Terms
قلب العلة حكماً والحكم علة (qalb al-illa hukman wa al-hukm illa): The first type of qalb where the alleged cause is inverted into the ruling and the ruling into the cause, showing the causal link is symmetrical.
استدلال (istidlal): Inference: presenting one thing as evidence for another without claiming causation, allowing mutual evidence.
مخلص (mukhlis): An escape from the objection of qalb by framing the argument as inference rather than causation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view in this passage, why does the 'escape' (mukhlis) of presenting an argument as istidlal rather than ta'lil not help Imam al-Shafi'i in the rajm/jald example?
A) Because the opponent cannot frame rajm and jald as mutual evidence.
B) Because there is no equality (musawa) between rajm and jald due to the severity and conditions of rajm.
C) Because Imam al-Shafi'i did not use istidlal in his argument.
D) Because qalb only applies in cases of wealth (mal).

Key Takeaway
Qalb al-illa hukman wa al-hukm illa is a valid Hanafi objection when there is inequality between the cause and effect, but if equality exists, inference (istidlal) can escape the inversion.

Qalb al-Wasf: Inverting the Descriptor Against the Opponent
Explaining the second type of qalb and its application to the fasting intention debate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define qalb al-wasf, apply it to the fasting intention debate, and distinguish it from the first type of qalb.

Core Idea
Qalb al-wasf turns the opponent's own descriptor into evidence against him, revealing a contradiction in his proof.

This lesson introduces the second type of qalb (inversion) in Hanafi usul: inverting a descriptor (wasf) used by the opponent to support his claim, making it a witness against him. We will explore the analogy of turning a sack inside out and then apply it to a real fiqh dispute about the intention for fasting in Ramadan. By the end, you will see how this dialectical tool can dismantle an opponent's reasoning by using his own premise.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of qalb
Recognize that this passage explains the second type (qalb al-wasf) as opposed to the first type (qalb al-illa). The author uses the analogy of inverting a sack to illustrate how the descriptor flips from supporting the opponent to opposing him.
The first type inverts cause and effect; the second inverts a descriptive attribute.
2
Understand the analogy
Visualize a sack: its outer side becomes inner and inner becomes outer. Similarly, the descriptor (wasf) that the opponent used as a witness for his claim is turned so that it becomes a witness against him.
This is called 'muqarasa bil qalb' (biting with inversion).
3
Analyze the opponent's argument
The opponent argues: Ramadan is an obligatory fast, so it must require specifying intention (like qada). The opponent uses the descriptor 'obligatory nature' (fardiyya) as a reason for specification.
This is a qiyas: all obligatory acts need intention, so Ramadan needs intention.
4
Apply qalb al-wasf
The Hanafi inverts: the obligatory nature actually indicates no specification is needed. Since Ramadan is already specified by the Lawgiver through the month and the hadith 'When half of Sha'ban remains, do not fast except for Ramadan', the servant does not need to specify the intention. The same applies to qada, which only needs specification once.
The descriptor (obligatory nature) is turned into proof against specification.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis do not require explicit specification of intention for Ramadan (general intention suffices), while Shafi'is require explicit specification for all obligatory fasts.
This shows how qalb al-wasf affects actual legal practice.
