وَالثَّانِي قَلْبُ الْوَصْفِ شاهِدًا عَلَى الْخَصْمِ بَعْدَ أَنْ كَانَ شَاهِدًا لَهُ أَى لِلْخَصْمِ فَهُوَ كَقَلبِ الْجَرَابِ بِجَعَلِ ظَهْرِهِ بَطَنًّا وَبَطَنَهُ ظَهْرُ فَإِنْ ظَهَرَ الْوَصْفُ كَانَ إِلَيْكَ وَالْوَجهُ إِلَى الْخَصمِ فَإِن قَلْبَ بَعْدَهُ فَصَارَ ظَهْرُهُ إِلَيْهِ وَجْهُهُ اِلَيْكَ فَهُوَ مُعَارِضَةٌ مِنْ حَيْثُ أَنَّهُ يَلُ عَلَى خِلَافٍ مُدْعِى الْخَصْمَ وَفِيْهِ مَنَاقِضَةٌ مِنْ حَيْثُ أَنْ دَلِيْلَة لَمْ يَدَلُّ عَلَى مُدَّعَاهُ وَهَذَا هُوَ الَّذِى يُسمِّيْهِ أَهْلُ الْمُنَاظَرَةِ بِالْمُقَارَصَةِ بِالْقَلْبِ وَيَجْرِى فِى كَثِيرٍ مِنَ الأَحْيَانِ فِي الْمُغَالَطَةِ الْعَامَّةِ الْوُرُدِ وَكَمَا يَقْنُوْهُ فِي كُتُبِهِمْ كَقَوْلِهِمْ فِي صَوْمِ رَمَضَانَ أَنَّهُ صَوْمُ فَرَضَ فَلَا بِتَادُئ إلَّا بِتَعْيِيْنِ النُّيَةَ كَصَوْمِ الْقَضَاءِ فَجُعِلَتْ الْفَرْضِيَةُ مِلَّةَ لِلتَّعِيْنِ فَعَارَ صَنَاهُ بِالْقَلِبِ وَجَعَلْنَا الْفَرْضِيَةَ دَلِيْلاً عَلَى عَدَمِ التَّنْبِيْنِ فَقُلْنَا لَمَّا كَانَ صَوْمًا فَرْضًا اسْتَغْنَى عَنْ تَعْبِيْنِ النّيَةِ بَعْدَ تَعْيِنُه كَصَومِ الْقَضاءِ إِنَّمَا يَحتَاجُ إِلى تَشِييْنِ وَاحِدٍ فَقَطْ لَأَزَائِدٌ فِيهِ هذَا كَذَالِك لكنه انما يتعين بالشرُوعِ هَذَا تَعْيِينُ قَبْلَهُ مِنْ جَانِبِ السَّارِعُ حَيْثُ قَالَ إِذَا إِنْسَبْحَ شَعْبَانُ فَلا صَوْمَ إِلا عَنْ رَمْضَانَ فصوم رمضان وَصَوْمُ الْقَضاءِ سوَاءٌ فِى أَنَّهُ لا يَحْتَاجُ إِلى تَعْيِينِ يَعْدَ تَعَيَيْن لَكِنَّ الرَّمَضَانَ لَمَّا كَانَ مُعَيَّنًا قَبْلَ الشروعِ فَلاَ يَحْتَاجُ إِلى تَعيينِ الْعَبْدِ وَصَوْمُ الْقَضَاءِ لَمَّا لَمْ يَكْنُ مُتَعينًا قَبْلَ الشروع احتاج الى تعيين الْعَبْد مرة
And the second type is inverting the descriptor (wasf) so that it becomes a witness against the opponent after it was a witness for him, i.e., for the opponent. It is like inverting a sack by making its outer side inner and its inner side outer. So if the descriptor appears, it is towards you and its face towards the opponent, then if he inverts it after that, its edge becomes towards him and its face towards you. So it is a counterargument in that it indicates the opposite of what the opponent claims, and in it there is a contradiction in that his evidence does not support his claim. This is what the dialecticians call 'muqarasa bil qalb' (biting with inversion) and it occurs often in common fallacies. And as they state in their books, like their statement concerning the fast of Ramadan: it is an obligatory fast, so it cannot be commenced except with specific intention (niyya) like the fast of make-up (qada). So they made the obligatory nature a cause for specification. Then we countered by inversion and made the obligatory nature a proof for lack of specification. We said: since it is an obligatory fast, it is independent of specifying the intention after [the month] is specified, like the fast of make-up. The fast of make-up only needs specification once because there is no increase in it. This is the same, but it is specified by commencement. This is a specification before it from the side of the Lawgiver, where he said: 'When half of Sha'ban remains, do not fast except for Ramadan.' So the fast of Ramadan and the fast of make-up are alike in that they do not need specification after [the time] is specified. But Ramadan, since it is specified before commencement, does not need the slave's specification, while the fast of make-up, since it is not specified before commencement, needs the slave's specification once.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
Passage type: Explanation of the second type of qalb (inversion) called 'qalb al-wasf' (inverting the descriptor). The author describes it using the analogy of turning a sack inside out: what was evidence for the opponent becomes evidence against him. This is a counterargument (mu'arada) that indicates the opposite of the opponent's claim and reveals a contradiction in his proof because his evidence does not actually support his claim. The dialecticians call this 'muqarasa bil qalb' (biting with inversion) and it is common in fallacious arguments. The author illustrates with the example of the fast of Ramadan. The opponent argues that the fast of Ramadan requires specifying the intention (niyya) because it is obligatory, just like the fast of make-up (qada). The Hanafi responds by inverting: the obligatory nature of Ramadan actually proves that no specific intention is needed after the month is specified by the Lawgiver, because Ramadan is already determined by time, unlike qada which is not specified beforehand. The hadith 'When half of Sha'ban remains, do not fast except for Ramadan' shows that Ramadan is specified from the Lawgiver's side, so the servant does not need to specify the intention; qada, on the other hand, is not specified beforehand, so the servant must intend it once. Thus, the opponent's own descriptor (obligatory nature) is turned against him to prove the opposite.

Key Terms
قلب الوصف (qalb al-wasf): The second type of qalb: inverting the descriptor (wasf) used by the opponent so that it becomes evidence against him.
مقارصة بالقلب (muqarasa bil qalb): A term used by dialecticians for a type of inversion that 'bites' the opponent, turning his own argument against him.
تعيين النية (ta'yin al-niyya): Specifying the intention for a particular fast, e.g., identifying it as Ramadan or qada.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example of fasting, how does the Hanafi use qalb al-wasf to counter the Shafi'i argument that Ramadan requires specifying intention?
A) By arguing that Ramadan is not obligatory and therefore needs no intention.
B) By inverting the obligatory nature: since it is obligatory and the Lawgiver already specified it, no further specification is needed.
C) By stating that all fasts require the same intention without exception.
D) By rejecting the hadith about Sha'ban.

Key Takeaway
Qalb al-wasf is a powerful dialectical tool that turns the opponent's own descriptor into evidence against him, exposing the contradiction in his argument.

Preference of Essence Over Attribute in Tarjih Conflicts
Usul rule with applied example and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that when two preference factors conflict, the factor in the essence (dhat) outweighs the factor in the attribute (sifah), and explain the thamarah al-khilaf with the Shafi'i position using the goat example.

Core Idea
When tarjih factors conflict, the one rooted in the essence defeats the one rooted in the attribute.

This lesson introduces a key principle in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: when two preferential factors (tarjih) conflict—one inherent in the essence (dhat) and one in an attribute (sifah)—the essence-based factor wins. The reasoning is that the attribute depends on the essence and follows it. The famous example of a usurped goat illustrates the rule and its practical difference from the Shafi'i position.

Guided Path
1
State the Rule
Identify the core rule: when two preference factors conflict, the one related to the essence (dhat) is stronger than the one related to the attribute (sifah).
The rule is a general usul principle, not limited to this goat case.
2
Analyze the Goat Example
Walk through the hypothetical: A usurper takes a goat, slaughters, cooks, and roasts it. Identify the two conflicting factors: the owner's original ownership (essence-based) vs. the usurper's transformative act (attribute-based).
The essence here is the meat; the attribute is the cooking/roasting.
3
Apply the Rule
Apply the rule: The usurper's act (sifah) is fully established in the very substance of the meat (dhat). Therefore, the usurper's right takes precedence, cutting off the owner's ownership.
This makes the attribute 'rise' to the level of essence for this ruling.
4
Compare with Shafi'i Position
Contrast: Imam al-Shafi'i holds the owner's right (original essence) is stronger because the usurper's act depends on the goat. The Hanafi response: the act is established in the essence in every respect, making it stronger here.
The thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafi gives meat to usurper, owner gets price; Shafi'i gives meat to owner.
5
Extract the Usul Principle
Generalize: The rule applies whenever two tarjih factors conflict—the factor in the dhat overrides the factor in the sifah. This is a tool for resolving conflicts in analogical reasoning.
Used in other fiqh disputes, e.g., priority of original ruling over derivative.

Source Text

قیاسوں کی اصول کے تعاضوں میں تعارض واقع ہو جائے كَانَ الرُّجْمَانُ فِي الدَّاتِ. تو جو وجہ بالذات پائی جائے وہ ترجیح کی زیادہ مستحق ہے اس وصف کے مقابلے میں جو وجہ کہ وصف میں پائی جاتی ہو یعنی جو وجہ فَيَنْقَطِعُ حَقَّ الْمَالِكِ بالطبخ والشنی اس وجہ سے مالک کا حق (گوشت سے ) منقطع ہو جاتا ہے پکا لینے یا اس کو بھول لینے سے یہ مذکورہ بالا قاعدہ پر تفریحی مثال ہے صورت اس کی یہ ہے کہ جب کسی شخص نے ایک شخص کی بکری غصب کر لیا پھر اس کو ذبح کر دیا اور اس کو پکا لیا اور بھون بھی لیا تو ہمارے نزدیک اس کو گوشت سے مالک کی ملک سبکری سے منقطع ہو جائے گی اور غاصب بکری کی قیمت کا ضمان دے گا اس وجہ سے کہ اس وقت ترجیح کے دو وجود میں تعارض واقع ہو گیا کیونکہ اگر اصل بکری کی طرف نظر کی جاتی ہے تو وہ گوشت مالک کا حق ہے مناسب ہے کہ اس گوشت کو مالک لے لے اور نقصان کا اس سے تاوان وصول کر لے اور اگر پکا لینے اور بھون لینے کی طرف نظر کی جاتی ہے تو ثابت ہوتا ہے کہ یہ دونوں کام غاصب نے کئے ہیں اس لئے سب ہے کہ گوشت کو غاصب اپنے پاس رکھے اور بکری کی قیمت کا تاوان ادا کرے لیکن موجودہ صورت عال میں غاصب کی جانب زیادہ مالک کا حق من وجہ ثابت ہے اور من وجہ ثابت نہیں ہے اور غاصب کا حق اس کی صنعت میں پورے طور پر قائم ہے۔ لہذا اس وقت صفت ذات کے درجہ میں ہے اور مین یعنی ذات و صف کے درجہ میں ہے اگر چہ واقعہ نفس الامر میں اس کے برعکس ہے جبکہ بکری صفت و صفہ ہے جیسا کہ امام شافعی کا نہ ہب ہے مصنف نے اپنے اگلے قول میں اسی کی طرف اشارہ فرمایا ہے۔ وَقَالَ الشافعي صاحِبُ الاَصلِ وَهُوَ الْمَالِكُ الخ اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا صاحب اصل یعنی بکری کا مالک زیادہ حق ہے کیونکہ غاصب کی صنعت، مصوع یعنی بکری کے ساتھ قائم ہے اور اس کے تابع ہے اس مسئلہ میں امام شافعی نے اس ظاہر پر میل فرمایا ہے اور ہم نے مسئلہ کی باریکی پر عمل کیا ہے۔
Then he (the author) intended to discuss the issue of preference. He said: When two types of preference conflict, e.g., two analogies conflict in their principles, then the factor that exists in the essence is more deserving of preference than the factor that exists in the attribute, because the attribute is established by the essence and follows it. Thus, the owner's right is cut off by cooking and roasting. This is an example: when someone usurps a goat, then slaughters, cooks, and roasts it, according to us the owner's ownership of the meat is cut off, and the usurper is liable for the price of the goat. This is because the two preferences conflict: if we look to the original goat, the meat is the owner's right; if we look to the cooking and roasting, they were done by the usurper. But here the usurper's side is stronger because his act is established in the essence in every respect, while the owner's right is established only in some respects. The usurper's right in his act is fully established. So at that point, the attribute (act) is at the level of essence, and the essence (goat) is at the level of attribute, though in reality it is opposite. Imam Shafi'i said: The owner of the original (goat) has more right because the usurper's act is attached to the goat and follows it. In this issue, Shafi'i relied on the apparent, and we acted upon the subtlety.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage explains a key principle in Hanafi usul regarding conflicting preferential factors (tarjih). The rule: if two aspects of preference conflict, one inherent in the essence (dhat) and one in an attribute (sifah), the one in the essence takes precedence. The reasoning is that the attribute is dependent on the essence and follows it. The example given is a goa: if someone usurps a goat, then slaughters, cooks, and roasts it, the usurper's act (sifah) is established in the very substance of the meat (dhat). Therefore, the usurper's right (due to his transformative act) outweighs the owner's right to the meat. The owner is compensated by the price of the goat. This is a well-known ruling in Hanafi fiqh, and the text contrasts it with the Shafi'i position, which gives the owner more right because the original ownership is considered stronger. The Hanafi position is considered more nuanced, taking into account the full establishment of the act in the essence.

Key Terms
ذات (dhāt): The essence or substance of a thing, independent of accidents.
صفة (ṣifah): An attribute or accident that inheres in the essence.
ترجیح (tarjīḥ): Preference given to one evidence or factor over another when they conflict.
قائم بالذات (qā'im bi-dhātihā): Established in the essence itself; fully inherent in the substance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) between Hanafi and Shafi'i in the goat example?
A) Hanafi: owner gets meat; Shafi'i: usurper gets meat.
B) Hanafi: usurper gets meat and pays price; Shafi'i: owner gets meat and usurper pays nothing.
C) Hanafi: owner gets meat and price; Shafi'i: usurper gets meat and pays price.
D) Hanafi: usurper gets meat and pays price; Shafi'i: owner gets meat.

Key Takeaway
When two preference factors conflict, the one fully established in the essence (dhat) overrides the one in the attribute (sifah), as illustrated by the usurper's cooking overriding the owner's original right.

Invalid Bases for Tarjih: Ghalabat al-Ashbah, Umum, Qillat al-Awsaf
Identifies three invalid methods of tarjih and refutes them

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain why the Hanafi school considers preference by preponderance of similarities, generality, and fewness of attributes as invalid methods of tarjih, and contrast the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Legal preference must be based on effect (ta'thir), not on number of similarities or generality.

This lesson examines three invalid methods of tarjih (preference) that the Shafi'i school accepts but the Hanafi school rejects. Through concrete examples—the brother's freedom, the riba cause, and the strength of a composite cause—we will see why Hanafi usul insists that only the actual legal effect (ta'thir) determines a cause's strength.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three invalid methods
Recognize that ghalabat al-ashbah, umum, and qillat al-awsaf are being examined. Note that the Hanafi school considers them invalid (fasid) while the Shafi'i school accepts them.
The passage explicitly states: 'وترجيح بغلبة الاشباه و العموم و قلة الأوصاف عندنا فاسد'.
2
Understand the Shafi'i argument for each method
For ghalabat al-ashbah: the brother resembles the cousin in many rulings (zakat, marriage, testimony) but the father/son only in mahramiyya, so the brother should be treated like a cousin (thus not freed upon ownership). For umum: edibility (ta'm) covers both small and large quantities, making it a more general cause than measurement. For qillat al-awsaf: a cause with fewer parts (e.g., ta'm alone) is more focused and thus stronger.
These arguments are presented in the passage as positions of 'Imam al-Shafi'i and his followers'.
3
Analyze the Hanafi refutation
Hanafi response: Ghalabat al-ashbah is merely preferring one qiyas over another, which is baseless. Umum does not give preference; a specific attribute is like a specific text (nass) that overrides general. Qillat al-awsaf is invalid because strength comes from legal effect (ta'thir), not simplicity; a cause with two parts can be stronger than one with one part.
The passage uses the phrase 'و عندنا هو بمنزلة ترجيح أحد القياسين بقياس آخر' for ghalabat, and 'لأن الترجيح للتأثير دون القلة والكثرة' for qillat.
4
Recognize the underlying principle
The core Hanafi principle is that tarjih must be based on the actual legal effect (ta'thir) of the cause. Mere numerical similarities, generality, or fewness of components are not valid indicators of strength.
This principle is evident in the refutation: 'فرُبَّ علَّة ذات جزئين أقوى في التأثير من علَّة ذات جزء واحد'.
5
Apply the principle to new scenarios
Given a scenario with multiple analogies, determine whether a proposed preference is based on ta'thir or on superficial criteria. For example, if a Shafi'i argues that a cause is preferred because it has more similarities, reject it; instead, look for which cause actually produces a legal effect.
Example: In the riba case, the Hanafi cause (kayl + jins) has a clear effect in preventing exploitation, while the Shafi'i cause (ta'm) is based on generality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و الترجيح بغلبة الاشباه اور ترجیح دینا کثرت مشابہت عموم و صف اور قلت اوصاف سے ہمارے نزدیک فاسد ہے مگر جناب امام شافعی ان میں سے ہر ایک کے صحیح ہونے کی طرف گئے ہیں یعنی ان کے نزدیک ان تینوں امور سے جَوَازُ اِعْطَاءِ الزَّكَوَةِ كُل مِنْهُما للآخرِ وَجلُ نِكَاح حَلِيْلَةٍ كُلِّ مِنْهُما لِلآخَرِ وَقَبُول شَهَادَةِ كُلِّ مِنْهُمَا للآخرِ فَيَكُونَ الْحَاقَةَ بِابْنِ الْعَمُ أَوْلى فَلا يَعْتِقَ عَلَى الأخ إذا مَلَكَهُ وَعِنْدَنَا هُوَ بِمَنْزِلَةٍ وَلَةٍ تَرْجِيحٍ أحَدِ الْقَيَاسَيْنِ بِقِيَاسِ آخَرَ وَقَدْ عَرَفْتَ يُطْلَانَهُ وَمِثَالُ الْعُمُوم. قَوْلُ الشافعية إِنْ وَصَفَ الطَّعْم فِى حُرْمَةِ الرِّبوا أولى مِنَ الْقَدْرِ وَالْجِنْسِ لانه يعم القليل وَهُوَ الْحَقْنَةُ وَالْكَثِيرَ وَهُوَ الْكَيْلُ وَالتَّعْلِيلُ بِالْكَيْلَ لا يَتَنَاوَلُ إِلَّا الكَثِيرَ وَهَذا بَاطِلٌ عِنْدَنَا لأَنَّهُ لَمَّا جَازَ عِنْدَهُ التَّعْلِيلُ بِالْعِلْةِ الْقَاصِرَةِ فَلا رُجحان لِلْعَمُوم عَلَى الْخُصوص وَلَأَنَّ الْوَصفَ بِمَنْزِلَةِ النَّصَّ وَفِي النَّمِ الْخَاص رَاجِعٌ عِنْدَهُ عَلَى الْعَام فَيَنْبَغِي أَنْ يَكُونَ فَهُنَّا أَيْضًا كَذَالِكَ وَمِثَالُ قِلْةٍ الأَوْصَافِ قَوْلُ الشَّافَعِيَةِ إِنَّ وَصَفَ الطَّعْمِ وَحْدَهُ وَالثَّمَنِيَةِ وَحْدَهَا قَلِيلٌ فَيَفْضُلُ عَلى القَدْرِ وَالْجِنْسِ الَّذِي قُلْتُمْ بِهِ مُجْتَمِعَةٌ وَهَذا بَاطِلٌ عِنْدَنَا لأَن التَّرْجِيحَ للتاثيرِ دُونَ الْقِلَّةِ وَالْكَثْرَةِ فَرُبَّ عِلَّةٍ ذات جُزْلَيْنِ أَقْوَىٰ فِي التَّاثِيرِ مِنْ عَلَّةٍ ذَاتِ جزءٍ وَاحِدٍ وَإِذَا ثَبَت دَفْعُ الْعِلْلِ بِمَا ذَكَرْنَا هَذَا شَرُوعٌ يَحْبٍ فِي انْتِقَالِ الْمُعَلَّلِ إلى كلام آخَرَ بَعْدَ الْرَامِهِ أَنْ إِذَا ثَبَتَ رَفْعُ الْعِلْلِ الطَّرْدِيَةِ وَالْمُوثَرَةِ بِمَا ذَكَرْنَا مِنَ الاعْتِرَاضَاتِ  ُأوْدَفع العِللِ الطَّرْدِيَةِ فَقَط عَلَى مَايُفهمُ مِنْ كَلامَ الْبَعْض كَانت غَايَتُهُ أَنْ يَلْجنى الى الانْتِقَال أَى غَايَةُ الْمُعَلِّل أن يُضطر إلى الإِنْتَقَال فَمِثَالُ غَلَبَةَ الأَسْبَاهِ پس غلبہ اشیاء کی مثال شوافع کا قول ہے کہ بھائی اپنے والد اور کڑ کے ترجمه و تشریح کے ساتھ فقط محرمیت میں مشابہ ہوتا ہے اور ابن العم (چچازاد بھائی) کے ساتھ کثیر وجوہ سے مشابہ ابہ ہوتا ہے ایک وجہ یہ ہے کہ ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک دوسرے کو ز کوۃ کا مال دے سکتا ہے (۲) چچازاد بھائی کی مطلقہ بیوی سے نکاح کا حلال ہوتا ہر ایک ان دونوں میں سے دوسری کی مطلقہ بیوی سے نکاح کر سکتا ہے (۳) ان دونوں ( چچازاد بھائی اور یہ ) میں سے ہر ایک کی شہادت دوسرے کے حق میں قابل قبول ہوتی ہے لہذا دوسرے احکام میں بھائی کا الحاق چچازاد بھائی کے ساتھ اولی ہو گا ( حقیقی بھائی کے مقابلے میں) لہذا بھائی جب اس کی ملکیت میں آجائے گا تو بھائی پر آزاد نہ ہو گا۔ وَعِنْدَنَا هُوَ بِمَنْزِلَةٍ تَرْجِهُم أَحَدَ الْقِهَاستين ، اور ہمارے نزدیک غلبہ اشباہ سے ترجیح دینا ایک قیاس پر دو قیاس کو تر جیح دینے کے حکم میں ہے اور تم اس کے باطل ہونے کو معلوم کر چکے ہو۔
And preference by preponderance of similarities, by generality, and by fewness of attributes is invalid according to us, but Imam Shafi'i considered each of them valid. Example of preponderance of similarities: The Shafi'is say that a brother resembles the father and son only in terms of forbidden marriage (mahramiyya), while he resembles the cousin in many respects: each may give zakat to the other, marriage with each other's divorced wife is permissible, and each's testimony is accepted for the other. Therefore, in other rulings, the brother should be attached to the cousin rather than the father/son, so a brother does not be free upon the other if owned. According to us, this is like preferring one analogy over another, which you already know is invalid. Example of generality: The Shafi'is say that the attribute of edibility (ta'm) in riba prohibition is more suitable than measurement and genus because it includes both small (muftahi) and large (kayl), while reasoning by measurement only covers the large. This is invalid according to us because they allow reasoning with a confined cause, and generality has no preference over specificity, and because the specific text (nass) overrides the general, so it should be same here. Example of fewness of attributes: The Shafi'is say that the attribute of edibility alone and price (thaman) alone are few, so they should be preferred over measurement and genus combined as you hold. This is invalid because preference is based on effect, not fewness or manyness; sometimes a cause with two parts is stronger in effect than a cause with one part. And when the invalidity of these methods is established, the opponent is forced to move to another proof. Our position is that such preference is like preferring one analogy over another, whose invalidity you already know.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage discusses three invalid methods of tarjih according to the Hanafi school, while the Shafi'is accept them. First: preponderance of similarities (ghalabat al-ashbāh). The Shafi'i argue that a brother shares more similarities with a cousin than with a father/son in legal rulings (zakat, marriage, testimony), so the brother should be treated like a cousin, not like a father/son. Therefore, if a brother owns his brother, he does not become free (i.e., the brother does not inherit freedom). The Hanafi response: this is merely preferring one qiyas over another, which is invalid. Second: generality (umūm). The Shafi'i claim that the attribute of edibility is more general (covers both small and large quantities) than measurement (which only covers large). So in riba, edibility should be the effective cause. Hanafi: this is invalid because a specific attribute is like a specific text (nass), which takes precedence over general text; and because the cause itself must be effective, not just general. Third: fewness of attributes (qillat al-awṣāf). The Shafi'i argue that fewer attributes are stronger because they are more focused. Hanafi: preference is based on the effect of the cause, not on the number of components; a cause with two parts may have a stronger effect than a single-part cause. The passage concludes that once these are invalidated, the opponent must move to another proof. The overall message is that only established, effective attributes count for tarjih, not mere numbers of similarities or generality.

Key Terms
غَلَبَة الأَشبَاه (ghalabat al-ashbāh): Preponderance of similarities; using the fact that one thing shares more attributes with another to establish a legal analogy.
عُمُوم (umūm): Generality; using the more general application of an attribute to prefer it as a cause.
قِلَّة الأَوْصَاف (qillat al-awṣāf): Fewness of attributes; the idea that a cause with fewer components is stronger.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is preference by 'ghalabat al-ashbah' invalid?
A) Because similarities are not legally relevant
B) Because it amounts to preferring one analogy over another without valid reason
C) Because the brother's case is unique
D) Because only Quran and Sunnah determine rulings

Key Takeaway
Ghalabat al-ashbah, umum, and qillat al-awsaf are invalid for tarjih because only ta'thir determines the strength of a cause.

Division of Rights: Huquq Allah and Huquq al-'Ibad
Explains the division of rights into two categories with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between Huquq Allah and Huquq al-'Ibad and state the definition and example of a self-subsisting right (haqq qa'im bi nafsihi).

Core Idea
A self-subsisting right belongs solely to Allah; the ruler acts as His deputy to collect and distribute it.

In Hanafi usul, rights are divided into those belonging to Allah and those belonging to individuals. This lesson unpacks the unique category of 'haqq qa'im bi nafsihi' — a right that does not require the servant's action — illustrated by the khums of spoils and mines.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of rights
The passage first presents Huquq Allah and Huquq al-'Ibad. Locate the description of each.
Huquq Allah are rights that are self-subsisting; Huquq al-'Ibad are rights that belong to individuals.
2
Define 'haqq qa'im bi nafsihi'
This is a right that is established by itself, without requiring the servant's performance. The ruler is appointed as the caliph to handle it.
It is not obligatory upon the servant to perform it; it is Allah's right.
3
Apply to khums of spoils
Jihad is Allah's right, so all spoils would be His, but He has granted four-fifths to the fighters as a favor, keeping one-fifth (khums) for Himself.
The khums is collected by the ruler.
4
Apply to mines (ma'adin)
Minerals like gold and silver are created by Allah and thus would be entirely His, but He has permitted the finder to keep four-fifths as a favor.
The remaining fifth is for the public treasury.
5
Contrast with Huquq al-'Ibad
These are rights like compensation, blood money, ownership in sales and marriage. They are owed to individuals and are not self-subsisting.
They depend on the servant's claim.

اشرف الانوار شرح اردو نور الانوار جلد سوم
ساتھ ہی اس میں عقوبت کے معنی بھی پائے جاتے ہیں کیونکہ یہ فقط کفار پر واجب ہوتا ہے جو لوگ صرف دنیا کی سمیتی میں مصروف ہیں اور آخرت کی کھیتی کو پس پشت ڈال رکھا ہے۔
وَحَق قَائِمٌ بِنَفْسِهِ (۸) اور ایسا حق جو بذات خود قائم ہو یعنی وہ حق خود ہی ثابت ہو بغیر اس کے کہ بندہ کے ذمہ کے ساتھ کوئی چیز متعلق ہو حتی کہ اس پر اس کی ادائے گی واجب ہے بلکہ خود حق تعالی نے اس کو اپنے لئے باقی رکھا ہے اور دنیا میں اس کو لینے وصول کرنے) اور تقسیم کرنے کے لئے اپنا خلیفہ اور نائب مقرر فرما دیا ہے اور وہ بادشاہ ہے۔ كَخَمْسِ الْغَنَائِمِ وَالْمَعَادِنِ فَإِنَّ الْجِهَادَ حَقٌّ اللَّهِ فَيَنْبَغِي أَنْ يَكُونَ الْمُصَابُ بِهِ وَهُوَ الْغَنِيمَةُ كُلُّها لِله تَعَالَى لَكِنْ أَوْجَبَ أَرْبَعَةَ أَخْمَاسِهِ لِلْغَائِمِيْنَ مِنْةٌ مِنْهُ وَأَبْقَى الْحُمْسَ لِنَفْسِهِ وَكَذَ الْمَعَادِنُ فَإِنَّهَا اسْمٌ خَلَقَهُ اللَّهُ فِي الْأَرْضِ مِنْ الذَّهَبِ وَالفِصْةِ فَيَنْبَغِي أَنْ يَكُونَ كُلَّهُ لِلَّهِ تَعَالَى وَلَكِنَّ الله تَعَالَى أَحَلُ لِلْوَاجِدِ أَوْ لِلْمَالِكِ أَرْبَعَةُ أَخْمَاسه مِنْةُ مِنْه وَفَضْلاً وَحَقُوقُ الْعِبَادِ كَبَدَلَ الْمُتَلِفَاتِ وَالْمَعْصُوبَاتِ وَغَيْرِهِمَا مِنَ الدِّيَةِ وَمِلْكِ الْمَبِيعِ وَالثَّمَنِ وَمِلْكِ النِّكَاحِ وَنَحْوِ وَهَذِهِ الْحُقُوقِ أَيْ جِئْسُهَا سَوَاءٌ كَانَ حَقًّا لِلَّهِ أَوْ لِلعَبْدِ لَا المَذْكُورِ عَنْ قَرِيبٍ تنقسم إلى أصلٍ وَخَلْفٍ يَقُوْمُ مَقامَ الأَصل عِنْدَ التَّعْذَر فَالإِيْمَانُ أَصلُه التَّصْدِيقَ وَالإقْرَارُ جَمِيعًا عِنْدَ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى ثُمَّ صَارَ الإِقْرَارُ وَحْدَهُ أَصْلاً مُسْتَجِدًا خَلْقًا عَنِ التَّصَدِيقِ فِي أَحْكَامِ الدُّنْيَا بِأَنْ يَقُومَ الإِقْرَارُ مَقَامَةٌ فِي حَقٌّ تَرَتِّبِ أَحْكامِهِ كَمَا فِي الْمُكْرَةِ عَلَى الإسلام أَجْرِى الإقْرَارُ مَقَامَ مَجْمُوع التَّصْدِيقِ وَالإقْرَارِ وَإِنْ عَدَمَ التَّصْدِيقُ مِنْهُ ثُمَّ صَارَ أَدَاءً أَحَدِ الْأَبَوَيْنِ فِي حَقِّ الصَّغِيْرِ خَلْقًا عَنْ إِدَاعِهِ أَنْ آدَاءِ الصَّغِيْرِ الإِيْمَانَ حَتَّى يُجْعَلَ مُسْلِمًا بِاسلام أَحَدِ الأَبَوَيْنِ وَيُجْرَى عَلَيْهِ أَحْكَامُهُ بِالْمِيْراثِ وَصَلوةِ الْجَنَازَةِ وَنَحْوهَا ثُمَّ صَارَت تَبْعِيَةُ أهْل الدَّار خَلْفًا عَنْ تَبْعِيَةِ الأَبْرَيْنَ فِي اثْبَاتِ الإسلام في الصني الَّذِي سَبَاهُ أَهْلُ الإسلام وَأَخْرَجُوْهُ إِلَى دَارِهِمْ يُحْكُمْ عَلَيْهِ بِالإسلام فِي الصلوةِ عَلَيْهِ بحُكْمُ التَّبْعِيَةِ وَلَيْسَ هَذَا خَلْفًا عَنْ خَلْفَ بَلْ كُل ذَالِكَ خَلْفٌ عِنْ أَدَاءِ الصَغيرِ لَكِنَّ الْبَعْضَ مُرْتُبْ عَلَى الْبَعْضِ وَكَذَالِكَ الطَّهَارَةُ بِالْمَاءِ أَصل والتيمم خَلْفٌ عَنْهُ وَهَذَا الْقَدْرَ بِلاخِلافِ ثُمَّ هَذَا الْخَلْفُ عِنْدَنَا مُطلَقَ حَتَّى يَرْتَفِعُ الْحَدَثُ بِالتَّيَمُ فَتَثْبُتُ بِهِ إِبَاحَةُ الصَّلوةِ إِلَى غَايَةِ وَجُوْدِ الْمَاءِ

اشرف الانوار شرح اردو نور الانوار جلد سوم
كَخَمْسِ الْغَنَائِمِ وَالْمَعَادِنِ جیسے مال غنیمت اور معدنیات کا خمس کیونکہ جہاد فی سبیل ترجمہ و تشریح اللہ اللہ تعالی کا حق ہے لہذا مناسب یہ ہے کہ جہاد کرنے سے جو چیز میں مال غنیمت کے طور پر ا حاصل ہوں سب کی سب اللہ کے لئے ہو جائیں لیکن اللہ تعالی نے چارٹس مجاہدین کے لئے واجب فرمائے بطور احسان کے اللہ کی جانب سے اور پانچواں حصہ اپنے لئے باقی رکھا اسی طرح معادن یعنی معدنیات زمین کے اندر سے نکلنے والے خزانے اور کانیں کیونکہ معدن نام ہے ان ذخیروں کا جن کو اللہ تعالی نے اپنی قدرت سے پیدا فرمائے ہیں مثلاً سونا ہے یا چاندی وغیرہ لہذ ا مناسب تھا کہ سب کا سب اللہ تعالی کے لئے ہو تا لیکن اللہ تعالی نے مالک یا پانے والے کے لئے چارے حصے حلال کئے اور پانچ ان حصہ اپنے لئے منظور فرمالیا جو محض اللہ کا فضل اور احسان ہے۔
وحقوق الْعِبَادِ كَبَدْلِ المُخلِفَاتِ اللہ اور دوسری قسم حقوق العباد ہے (یعنی خالص بندوں کے حقوق) جیسے کسی شخص کے ضائع ہونے کسی سے غصب کئے ہوئے مال کا ضمان وغیرہ جیسے دیت مبیع کی ملک شمن کی ملک ملک نکاح وغیرہ بے شمار حقوق ایسے ہیں جن کا شمار کرنا مشکل ہے۔
وهذه الحقوق اور یہ تمام حقوق یعنی جنس حقوق خواہ حقوق اللہ ہوں یا حقوق العباد سے وہ حقوق مراد ہیں جن کا قریب میں ذکر ہوا معظم الی اصل و خلف منقسم ہیں (1) اصل اور (۲) خلف کی طرف ایسا خلف سے مراد ہے جو اصل کے مسعود پر ہونے کے وقت قائم مقام ہو فالإيمان أصلُهُ المُصدِيقُ الخ چنانچہ ایمان کا اصل تصدیق اور اقرار دونوں میں یعنی اللہ تعالیٰ کے نزدیک ثم صار الاقرار وحده اصلا مستبداً الخ پھر تنہا اقرایی مستقل اصل اور تصدیق قلبی کا خلیفہ بن گیا احکام دنیا جاری کرنے کے حق میں پائیں صورت کہ اقرار باللسان تصدیق کے قائم مقام ہے احکام دنیا کے مرتب ہونے کے معاملے میں جیسے وہ شخص جس کو زبر دستی مسلمان کیا گیا ہو اس منکرہ شخص کے اقرار لسانی کو تصدیق قلبی اور اقرار لسانی کے قائم مقام کر دیا گیا۔ ہے اگر چہ اس سے تصدیق معدوم ہو۔
كم متاز أداء أحد الأنوفن پھر ماں باپ میں سے کسی ایک کا اقرار اسلام ان کے چھوٹے بچوں کی طرف سے ایمان لانے کا طلف بنایا گیا ہے یعنی اس کا ایمان لانا بچوں کے ایمان لانے کے قائم مقام ہے کہ احد الابوین کے ایمان لانے سے بچوں کو بھی مسلمان شمار کیا جائے گا اور ان پر احکام اسلام جاری ہوں گے مثالی ماں باپ کی میراث کا حقدار ہونا ان کی نماز جنازہ پڑھنا و غیره ثم صارت تبعية أهل الدار الخ پھر نا بالغ بچوں کے مسلمان قرار دینے میں دار الاسلام کے تابع ہونے کو ماں باپ کی تابعیت کے خلف مانا گیا ہے یعنی وہ نا بالغ بچے جن کو مسلمان قید کر کے وار الاسلام میں لے آئیں ماں باپ کے بجائے ) تو ان بچوں پر اسلام کا حکم دیا جائے گا اہل اسلام کے تابع ہونے کی حیثیت سے اور اگر ان کی موت واقع ہو جائے تو ان بچوں کی نماز جنازہ پڑھی جائے گی یہ در حقیقت نائب کے لئے نائب کا اثبات نہیں ہے بلکہ ان میں سے ہر ایک (یعنی احد الا بوین کا
Ashraf al-Anwar commentary on Nur al-Anwar volume 3. Alongside that, the meaning of punishment is also found because it is only obligatory upon disbelievers who are preoccupied only with the worldly life and have cast aside the cultivation of the Hereafter. And [there is] a right that is self-subsisting (8) - and a right that is established by itself, i.e., that right is itself proven without anything being attached to the servant's responsibility, such that its performance is not obligatory upon him; rather, Allah Himself has reserved it for Himself and appointed His caliph and deputy in the world to take, collect, and distribute it, and that is the king. Like the khums of spoils and mines: for Jihad is a right of Allah, so it should be that the acquired thing, which is the spoils, all of it is for Allah the Exalted, but He made four-fifths obligatory for the fighters as a favor from Him and kept the fifth for Himself. Similarly, mines: they are a name for what Allah created in the earth of gold and silver, so all of it should be for Allah the Exalted, but Allah the Exalted made four-fifths permissible for the finder or the owner as a favor and grace. And the rights of servants, like compensation for destroyed property, usurped items, and other such as blood money, ownership of the sold item, ownership of the price, ownership of marriage, and the like. And these rights - i.e., their genus - whether it is a right of Allah or a right of the servant that was mentioned shortly before, are divided into an original (asl) and a substitute (khalaf) that stands in the place of the original when [the original] is unattainable. So the original of faith is both affirmation (tasdiq) and declaration (iqrar) together in the sight of Allah the Exalted. Then declaration alone became an independent original and a substitute for affirmation in the rulings of this world, such that declaration stands in its place concerning the establishment of its rulings, as in the case of one who is coerced into Islam: declaration is made to stand in place of the combined affirmation and declaration, even if affirmation is absent from him. Then the performance of one of the parents concerning the young child became a substitute for the child's own performance of faith, such that the child is considered Muslim by the Islam of one parent and its rulings are applied to him regarding inheritance, funeral prayer, and the like. Then the adherence (taba'iyya) of the people of the abode (ahl al-dar) became a substitute for the adherence of parents in establishing Islam for the child taken as captive by the people of Islam and brought to their lands; he is judged to be Muslim concerning prayer over him by virtue of adherence. This is not a substitute for a substitute; rather, all of that is a substitute for the performance of the minor, but each is built upon the other. Similarly, purification with water is the original and tayammum is a substitute for it, and this much is without disagreement. Then this substitute according to us is absolute such that ritual impurity is removed by tayammum, and so permissibility of prayer is established by it until water is found. [Urdu commentary follows]
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the division of rights (huquq) into two categories: rights of Allah (huquq Allah) and rights of servants (huquq al-'ibad). It also introduces the key usul principle of asl (original) and khalaf (substitute), which is used throughout Hanafi fiqh to determine how rulings are transferred when the original is unavailable. The author first explains the concept of 'a right self-subsisting' (haqq qa'im bi nafsihi), meaning a right that is established without requiring the servant's performance. Examples include khums of spoils and mines: though spoils and minerals are created by Allah and belong to Him in principle, He has graciously allowed the fighters or finders to keep four-fifths, reserving one-fifth for Himself. This illustrates how some rights are inherently Allah's. Next, rights of servants are listed, such as compensation for destroyed or usurped property, blood money, ownership of goods and price in a sale, and marriage rights. Then the text explains that all rights, whether Allah's or servants', can be divided into an original (asl) and a substitute (khalaf) that stands in for the original when the original cannot be attained. Several examples are given: (1) Faith (iman): its asl is both tasdiq (affirmation of the heart) and iqrar (verbal declaration) together. However, for worldly rulings, iqrar alone becomes a khalaf, as seen in the case of a person coerced into Islam — their mere verbal declaration suffices to apply Islamic rulings even if inner affirmation is absent. (2) A parent's declaration of Islam serves as khalaf for a minor child's own faith; thus the child is deemed Muslim by the parent's Islam, inherits, and has funeral prayer performed. (3) The adherence (taba'iyya) of being in a Muslim land (dar al-Islam) becomes a khalaf for the adherence of parents for captured children — they are considered Muslim by virtue of being in the Muslim territory. (4) Tayammum is a khalaf for wudu (ablution with water), and according to the Hanafi school, tayammum completely removes ritual impurity, making prayer permissible until water is found. The passage emphasizes that these are all substitutes for the original performance of the minor, not a chain of substitutes. This principle is directly relevant to many fiqh rulings, especially in ibadat and family law.

Key Terms
حَقٌّ قَائِمٌ بِنَفْسِهِ (haqqun qā'imun bi nafsihī): A right that is established by itself without requiring any action from the servant; it is a right that Allah reserves for Himself and has appointed a representative (caliph) to collect and distribute.
خَمْسِ الْغَنَائِمِ (khums al-ghanā'im): One-fifth of the spoils of war that is reserved for Allah and distributed by the caliph; the remaining four-fifths are given to the fighters as a favor.
حُقُوقُ الْعِبَادِ (ḥuqūq al-'ibād): Rights that belong to individuals, such as compensation for damaged property, blood money, ownership rights in sales and marriage.
حَقُّ اللَّهِ (haqq Allah): A right belonging to Allah, often self-subsisting, collected and distributed by the ruler as His deputy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the primary characteristic of a 'haqq qa'im bi nafsihi'?
A) It requires the servant's action.
B) It is established by itself without servant's action.
C) It is only for the ruler.
D) It is a right of servants.

Key Takeaway
Huquq Allah are self-subsisting rights; the ruler acts as Allah's deputy for their collection and distribution, as seen in the khums of spoils and mines.

12 min
The Principle of Asl and Khalaf in Hanafi Usul
Explains the principle of asl and khalaf with multiple examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle of asl and khalaf to derive rulings in cases where the original is unattainable, using examples from faith, coercion, parent-child, dar al-Islam, and tayammum.

Core Idea
When the original cannot be performed, the substitute takes its place and carries the same rulings for worldly purposes.

One of the most powerful tools in Hanafi usul is the concept of asl and khalaf. This lesson traces the chain of substitutes from faith to tayammum, showing how the school maintains practical continuity of rulings even when the original is impossible or impractical.

Guided Path
1
Define asl and khalaf
Asl is the original primary form; khalaf is a substitute that stands in when the asl is unattainable. The khalaf carries the same worldly rulings.
The passage emphasizes that khalaf is not a weaker version; it fulfills the purpose completely.
2
Trace the first example: iman (faith)
The asl of faith is both tasdiq (heart affirmation) and iqrar (verbal declaration). For worldly rulings, iqrar alone becomes a khalaf, as in the case of a coerced convert.
This shows that the substitute operates even when the original element is missing.
3
Move to parents and minors
A parent's declaration of Islam is a khalaf for the child's own faith. The child is thus considered Muslim, inherits, and has funeral prayer performed.
This is a substitute for the child's performance.
4
Understand the chain: dar al-Islam
For a captive child brought to dar al-Islam, the child's adherence (being in Muslim territory) becomes a khalaf for the parent's adherence. This is not a substitute for a substitute but another khalaf for the original (the minor's own performance).
The passage clarifies that all these are substitutes for the minor's own faith act, arranged hierarchically.
5
Apply to tayammum
Tayammum is a khalaf for wudu with water. According to the Hanafi school, it is an absolute substitute: it removes ritual impurity and permits prayer until water is found.
This contrasts with other schools that consider tayammum a mere concession.

كَخَمْسِ الْغَنَائِمِ وَالْمَعَادِنِ جیسے مال غنیمت اور معدنیات کا خمس کیونکہ جہاد فی سبیل ترجمہ و تشریح اللہ اللہ تعالی کا حق ہے لہذا مناسب یہ ہے کہ جہاد کرنے سے جو چیز میں مال غنیمت کے طور پر ا حاصل ہوں سب کی سب اللہ کے لئے ہو جائیں لیکن اللہ تعالی نے چارٹس مجاہدین کے لئے واجب فرمائے بطور احسان کے اللہ کی جانب سے اور پانچواں حصہ اپنے لئے باقی رکھا اسی طرح معادن یعنی معدنیات زمین کے اندر سے نکلنے والے خزانے اور کانیں کیونکہ معدن نام ہے ان ذخیروں کا جن کو اللہ تعالی نے اپنی قدرت سے پیدا فرمائے ہیں مثلاً سونا ہے یا چاندی وغیرہ لہذ ا مناسب تھا کہ سب کا سب اللہ تعالی کے لئے ہو تا لیکن اللہ تعالی نے مالک یا پانے والے کے لئے چارے حصے حلال کئے اور پانچ ان حصہ اپنے لئے منظور فرمالیا جو محض اللہ کا فضل اور احسان ہے۔
وحقوق الْعِبَادِ كَبَدْلِ المُخلِفَاتِ اللہ اور دوسری قسم حقوق العباد ہے (یعنی خالص بندوں کے حقوق) جیسے کسی شخص کے ضائع ہونے کسی سے غصب کئے ہوئے مال کا ضمان وغیرہ جیسے دیت مبیع کی ملک شمن کی ملک ملک نکاح وغیرہ بے شمار حقوق ایسے ہیں جن کا شمار کرنا مشکل ہے۔
وهذه الحقوق اور یہ تمام حقوق یعنی جنس حقوق خواہ حقوق اللہ ہوں یا حقوق العباد سے وہ حقوق مراد ہیں جن کا قریب میں ذکر ہوا معظم الی اصل و خلف منقسم ہیں (1) اصل اور (۲) خلف کی طرف ایسا خلف سے مراد ہے جو اصل کے مسعود پر ہونے کے وقت قائم مقام ہو فالإيمان أصلُهُ المُصدِيقُ الخ چنانچہ ایمان کا اصل تصدیق اور اقرار دونوں میں یعنی اللہ تعالیٰ کے نزدیک ثم صار الاقرار وحده اصلا مستبداً الخ پھر تنہا اقرایی مستقل اصل اور تصدیق قلبی کا خلیفہ بن گیا احکام دنیا جاری کرنے کے حق میں پائیں صورت کہ اقرار باللسان تصدیق کے قائم مقام ہے احکام دنیا کے مرتب ہونے کے معاملے میں جیسے وہ شخص جس کو زبر دستی مسلمان کیا گیا ہو اس منکرہ شخص کے اقرار لسانی کو تصدیق قلبی اور اقرار لسانی کے قائم مقام کر دیا گیا۔ ہے اگر چہ اس سے تصدیق معدوم ہو۔
كم متاز أداء أحد الأنوفن پھر ماں باپ میں سے کسی ایک کا اقرار اسلام ان کے چھوٹے بچوں کی طرف سے ایمان لانے کا طلف بنایا گیا ہے یعنی اس کا ایمان لانا بچوں کے ایمان لانے کے قائم مقام ہے کہ احد الابوین کے ایمان لانے سے بچوں کو بھی مسلمان شمار کیا جائے گا اور ان پر احکام اسلام جاری ہوں گے مثالی ماں باپ کی میراث کا حقدار ہونا ان کی نماز جنازہ پڑھنا و غیره ثم صارت تبعية أهل الدار الخ پھر نا بالغ بچوں کے مسلمان قرار دینے میں دار الاسلام کے تابع ہونے کو ماں باپ کی تابعیت کے خلف مانا گیا ہے یعنی وہ نا بالغ بچے جن کو مسلمان قید کر کے وار الاسلام میں لے آئیں ماں باپ کے بجائے ) تو ان بچوں پر اسلام کا حکم دیا جائے گا اہل اسلام کے تابع ہونے کی حیثیت سے اور اگر ان کی موت واقع ہو جائے تو ان بچوں کی نماز جنازہ پڑھی جائے گی یہ در حقیقت نائب کے لئے نائب کا اثبات نہیں ہے بلکہ ان میں سے ہر ایک (یعنی احد الا بوین کا
Ashraf al-Anwar commentary on Nur al-Anwar volume 3. Alongside that, the meaning of punishment is also found because it is only obligatory upon disbelievers who are preoccupied only with the worldly life and have cast aside the cultivation of the Hereafter. And [there is] a right that is self-subsisting (8) - and a right that is established by itself, i.e., that right is itself proven without anything being attached to the servant's responsibility, such that its performance is not obligatory upon him; rather, Allah Himself has reserved it for Himself and appointed His caliph and deputy in the world to take, collect, and distribute it, and that is the king. Like the khums of spoils and mines: for Jihad is a right of Allah, so it should be that the acquired thing, which is the spoils, all of it is for Allah the Exalted, but He made four-fifths obligatory for the fighters as a favor from Him and kept the fifth for Himself. Similarly, mines: they are a name for what Allah created in the earth of gold and silver, so all of it should be for Allah the Exalted, but Allah the Exalted made four-fifths permissible for the finder or the owner as a favor and grace. And the rights of servants, like compensation for destroyed property, usurped items, and other such as blood money, ownership of the sold item, ownership of the price, ownership of marriage, and the like. And these rights - i.e., their genus - whether it is a right of Allah or a right of the servant that was mentioned shortly before, are divided into an original (asl) and a substitute (khalaf) that stands in the place of the original when [the original] is unattainable. So the original of faith is both affirmation (tasdiq) and declaration (iqrar) together in the sight of Allah the Exalted. Then declaration alone became an independent original and a substitute for affirmation in the rulings of this world, such that declaration stands in its place concerning the establishment of its rulings, as in the case of one who is coerced into Islam: declaration is made to stand in place of the combined affirmation and declaration, even if affirmation is absent from him. Then the performance of one of the parents concerning the young child became a substitute for the child's own performance of faith, such that the child is considered Muslim by the Islam of one parent and its rulings are applied to him regarding inheritance, funeral prayer, and the like. Then the adherence (taba'iyya) of the people of the abode (ahl al-dar) became a substitute for the adherence of parents in establishing Islam for the child taken as captive by the people of Islam and brought to their lands; he is judged to be Muslim concerning prayer over him by virtue of adherence. This is not a substitute for a substitute; rather, all of that is a substitute for the performance of the minor, but each is built upon the other. Similarly, purification with water is the original and tayammum is a substitute for it, and this much is without disagreement. Then this substitute according to us is absolute such that ritual impurity is removed by tayammum, and so permissibility of prayer is established by it until water is found. [Urdu commentary follows]
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the division of rights (huquq) into two categories: rights of Allah (huquq Allah) and rights of servants (huquq al-'ibad). It also introduces the key usul principle of asl (original) and khalaf (substitute), which is used throughout Hanafi fiqh to determine how rulings are transferred when the original is unavailable. The author first explains the concept of 'a right self-subsisting' (haqq qa'im bi nafsihi), meaning a right that is established without requiring the servant's performance. Examples include khums of spoils and mines: though spoils and minerals are created by Allah and belong to Him in principle, He has graciously allowed the fighters or finders to keep four-fifths, reserving one-fifth for Himself. This illustrates how some rights are inherently Allah's. Next, rights of servants are listed, such as compensation for destroyed or usurped property, blood money, ownership of goods and price in a sale, and marriage rights. Then the text explains that all rights, whether Allah's or servants', can be divided into an original (asl) and a substitute (khalaf) that stands in for the original when the original cannot be attained. Several examples are given: (1) Faith (iman): its asl is both tasdiq (affirmation of the heart) and iqrar (verbal declaration) together. However, for worldly rulings, iqrar alone becomes a khalaf, as seen in the case of a person coerced into Islam — their mere verbal declaration suffices to apply Islamic rulings even if inner affirmation is absent. (2) A parent's declaration of Islam serves as khalaf for a minor child's own faith; thus the child is deemed Muslim by the parent's Islam, inherits, and has funeral prayer performed. (3) The adherence (taba'iyya) of being in a Muslim land (dar al-Islam) becomes a khalaf for the adherence of parents for captured children — they are considered Muslim by virtue of being in the Muslim territory. (4) Tayammum is a khalaf for wudu (ablution with water), and according to the Hanafi school, tayammum completely removes ritual impurity, making prayer permissible until water is found. The passage emphasizes that these are all substitutes for the original performance of the minor, not a chain of substitutes. This principle is directly relevant to many fiqh rulings, especially in ibadat and family law.

Key Terms
أصل (aṣl): The original, primary form of a right or action that is the basis for its ruling.
خلف (khalaf): A substitute that stands in for the original when the original cannot be performed or attained; it carries the same ruling as the original for worldly purposes.
تعدّذ (ta'adhdhur): Unattainability; the condition that triggers the use of a khalaf.
تبعية (taba'iyya): Adherence; the legal connection to a person or territory that determines status.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the status of tayammum as a substitute for wudu in the Hanafi school?
A) It only permits prayer but does not remove impurity.
B) It removes ritual impurity completely and permits prayer until water is found.
C) It is only valid for travelers.
D) It is not a valid substitute.

Key Takeaway
The asl-khalaf principle allows the Hanafi school to maintain legal continuity: when the original is unattainable, the substitute carries the same rulings completely.

Sabab Haqiqi: The True Cause in Hanafi Usul
Defining sabab haqiqi via contrast and example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define sabab haqiqi, distinguish it from 'illa, shart, and 'alama, and apply the distinction to a case of liability.

Core Idea
A true cause leads to a ruling but has no effect on it – only the intervening 'illa creates liability.

In Hanafi usul, not every cause (sabab) directly affects a ruling. Some causes are mere paths—they lead to a ruling without having any causal effect. This lesson unpacks the concept of sabab haqiqi, a pure cause that merely indicates or facilitates but does not necessitate. We will explore how it differs from the effective cause ('illa), condition (shart), and sign ('alama), and why the holder of a true cause is not liable for the outcome. A classic example is someone who points out a person's property to a thief: the pointer is not liable for the theft because his action is only a true cause, not the effective cause.

Guided Path
1
Define Sabab Haqiqi
Read the Arabic definition: 'that which is a path to the ruling, leading to it in general.' Identify key phrases: it is a means, not an obligator or creator.
Note the negation of effect: 'no effect... either directly or indirectly.'
2
Distinguish from 'Illa, Shart, and 'Alama
Contrast sabab haqiqi with the effective cause ('illa) which directly necessitates the ruling, the condition (shart) which is required for existence, and the sign ('alama) which merely indicates without leading. Extract the three negations: (1) obligation not attributed to sabab, (2) existence not attributed to it, (3) no 'illa-like meaning in it.
These negations are unique to Hanafi usul.
3
Analyze the Example of Indication for Theft
Consider the example: a person indicates another's property to a thief. The indication is a true cause because it leads to the theft but does not cause it directly. The intervening 'illa is the thief's free choice. If the thief steals, the indicator is not liable.
The ruling (no liability) follows from the principle that a true cause holder is not the 'illa holder.
4
Examine the Later Fatwa on Slander
The text notes that later scholars made a slanderer who approaches a tyrant liable for damages, due to corruption of the times. This seems to contradict the principle. Discuss how the change is based on a new 'illa (public mischief) that overrides the default no-liability rule.
This shows that the classification can shift when the 'illa changes.
5
Apply the Concept to a New Scenario
Construct a similar scenario (e.g., a person leaves a door unlocked, enabling theft) and ask: Is the person liable? Apply the sabab haqiqi framework to determine if there is an intervening 'illa.
The key question: Is there an intervening free choice that breaks the causal link?

إِنْسانِ الغ خلا کسی شخص کا یا اس کے مال کا پتہ دوسرے کو بتادینا تا کہ وہ اس کو قتل کر دے یا اس کا مال چوری کرکے تو یہ دلالت اور رہنمائی چوری یا قتل کا حقیقی سبب ہے کیونکہ اس دلالت نے ہی وہاں تک پہونچایا ہے مگر نہ موجب ہے اور یہ اس کی موجد ہے نہ ہی فعل سرقہ میں اس کی کوئی تاثیر ہی ہے لیکن اس ذلالت اور فعل سرقہ کے درمیان واقع ہوئی ہے ایسی علیت جو دلالت کی طرف منسوب نہیں ہے اور وہ با تیار چور کا فعل اور ارادہ ہے کیونکہ ضروری نہیں ہے کہ اگر کسی نے کسی برے کام کی خبر دی یا دلالت کی تو مدلول ( جس کو خبر دی گئی ہے) اس فعل کو یقینی طور پر کر ڈالے بلکہ ممکن ہے کہ اللہ تعالی اس کو اس ہرے کام کو ترک کرنے کی توفیق عطا فرمادے ہاو جو یکہ بتلانے نے دلالت کر دی ہے لہذا اگر مدلول کی جانب سے چوری یا قتل کا واقعہ پیش کیا تو دلالت کرنے والا کوئی چیز منمان میں نہ دے گا تو کیو نکہ وہ تو صرف سبب محض نے وال نہ دے وہ والا ہے وہ علت والا نہیں ہے اور اسی بنیاد پر مناسب ہے کہ وہ شخص جو کسی ظالم بادشاہ کی طرف سے کسی شخص کے حق میں ناحق بھی کرے چغلی کرے حتی کہ اس سے مال تاوان میں وصول کرے کیونکہ وہ تو صرف صاحب سبب ف ہے لیکن علماء متاخرین نے ایسے سامی کے لئے تاوان ادا کرنے کا فتویٰ صادر فرمایا ہے کیونکہ غلط باتوں کو نبروں تک پہونچانے سے زمانے میں فساد پیدا ہو گا اور ان سعی کرنے والوں (چغلی کرنے والوں) کی جرات
As for the second division of the aforementioned division at the beginning of the chapter, it is [the category of] things connected to rulings, and they are four: the first is al-sabab (the cause). And it is divided into four types. The first is a true cause (sabab haqiqi), which is what is a path to the ruling, i.e., leading to it in general, unlike the 'alama (sign), for it indicates the ruling but does not lead to it, without the obligation of the ruling being attributed to it as it is attributed to the 'illa, nor its existence as it is attributed to the shart. And the meanings of 'ilal are not found in it in any way, such that it has no effect on the existence of the ruling at all, either directly or indirectly. If it were like that, it would not be a true cause but rather a cause that has the semblance of 'illa or a cause that has the meaning of 'illa, but there intervenes between it — i.e., between the cause and the ruling — an 'illa that is not attributed to the cause. If it were attributed to the cause and the ruling were attributed to it, then the cause would be the 'illa of the 'illa, not a true cause, as will come. For example, a person indicating to another about his property or himself so that he may steal it or kill him. This indication is a true cause for the theft or murder because it leads to it without being a cause that necessitates or creates it, and it has no effect on the act of theft at all. But between the indication and the theft there intervenes an 'illa that is not attributed to the indication, namely the free choice and intention of the thief. For it is not necessary that if someone informs or indicates to another about a bad deed, the one informed will definitely do that deed; perhaps Allah may grant him success to abandon it despite the indication. So if theft or murder occurs from him, the one who indicated is not liable for anything, because he is merely a possessor of a cause, not of an 'illa. Based on this, it is fitting that one who speaks to a tyrannical ruler against another person unjustly, such that he takes his money, should not be liable, because he is merely a possessor of a pure cause. However, the later scholars have issued a fatwa for his liability due to the corruption of the times through false slander and the abundance of slanderers therein. And the second division from the aforementioned division at the beginning of the chapter, i.e., the matters to which rulings are connected: they are four types: (1) sabab, (2) 'alama, (3) shart, (4) 'alama. Then among them, the first type (1) sabab also has four types: (a) true cause (sabab haqiqi), and it is called what is a means to reach the ruling, i.e., that which conveys to the ruling in general, unlike the 'alama because the 'alama indicates the ruling, it does not convey to it, without the obligation of the ruling being attributed to it just as the obligation is attributed to the 'illa, and not its existence as attributed to the shart. And the meanings of 'ilal are not found in it in any way such that it has no effect on the existence of the ruling at all, either directly or indirectly, because if effect is found directly or indirectly, then it will not remain a true cause but will be called a cause that has the semblance of 'illa or a cause that has the meaning of 'illa. But there intervenes between it, i.e., between the cause and the ruling, an 'illa that is not attributed to the cause, because the ruling is always attributed to the 'illa. Now if its attribution were also to the side of the cause, it would necessitate that the cause is the 'illa of the 'illa and would not be a true cause, further explanation of which will come. For example, a person informing another about someone's property or himself so that he may kill him or steal his property, this indication and guidance is a true cause for theft or murder, because this indication led there but is not the obligator nor the creator, nor does it have any effect on the act of theft. But between this indication and the act of theft there occurs an 'illa that is not attributed to the indication, and that is the thief's free choice and intention, because it is not necessary that if someone gives news or indication of a bad deed, the one informed (the one who was told) will definitely do that deed; rather it is possible that Allah may grant him success to abandon this bad deed despite the indication. Therefore, if theft or murder occurs from the side of the informed one, the one who indicated will not give anything in compensation, because he is merely a possessor of a pure cause, not a possessor of an 'illa. And on this basis, it is appropriate that the person who slanders against someone to a tyrannical king unjustly, even to the extent that he takes money from him, should not be liable because he is simply a possessor of a pure cause. But the later scholars issued a fatwa for his liability due to the corruption of the times through false slander and the abundance of slanderers.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage is a usul al-fiqh definition of 'sabab haqiqi' (true cause). The author explains that sabab haqiqi is a means that leads to a ruling generally, but unlike 'illa (effective cause), it does not directly necessitate the ruling, and unlike shart (condition), it does not cause the ruling's existence. The key distinction is that a true cause has no effect on the ruling at all; an intervening 'illa (such as a thief's free choice) stands between the cause and the ruling. The example given is of a person who informs another about someone's property to facilitate theft. The informant is only a sabab, not an 'illa, so he is not liable for the theft. The same applies to a slanderer before a tyrant. However, the later scholars (mutakhkhirin) have issued a fatwa making the slanderer liable due to widespread corruption.

Key Terms
سبب حقيقي (sabab haqiqi): A true cause that leads to a ruling without directly affecting it.
علة (illa): The effective cause that directly necessitates the ruling.
علامت ('alama / alamat): A sign that indicates the ruling but does not lead to it.
شرط (shart): A condition for the existence of the ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi usul, what is the key difference between a sabab haqiqi (true cause) and an 'illa (effective cause)?
A) A sabab haqiqi directly necessitates the ruling, while 'illa indicates it.
B) A sabab haqiqi leads to the ruling without direct effect, while 'illa directly necessitates the ruling.
C) They are synonyms.
D) 'Illa applies only to acts of worship.

Key Takeaway
A true cause (sabab haqiqi) is a mere path to a ruling with no causal effect; liability requires an intervening 'illa that directly necessitates the outcome.

intermediate
8 min
Second Type of Sabab: Attributing the Intervening Cause
Explaining the second type of sabab with examples and legal effects on liability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and apply the Hanafi rule that when an intervening cause ('illah) is attributed to a sabab, the sabab becomes liable for compensation but not for criminal penalties.

Core Idea
Attributing the intervening cause to the sabab makes the sabab liable for compensation, but not for criminal penalties.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, causes (asbab) are classified into three types. This lesson focuses on the second type, where an intermediate cause ('illah) exists but is legally attributed to the original act. Using examples from a muhrim pointing to game and a depositary directing a thief, we see how liability for compensation arises, while criminal consequences like kaffarah and qisas remain unattached.

Guided Path
1
Recall the classification of sabab into three types
Briefly review that sabab can be direct, attributed via intervening cause, or metaphorical. This lesson covers the second type.
The first type is not discussed in this passage.
2
Identify the second type: sabab with attributing intervening 'illah
The key condition is that the intervening cause (e.g., the actual killing or theft) is attributable to the original act due to the lack of independent will of the intermediate agent.
Attribution makes the sabab effectively like a direct cause for compensation.
3
Analyze the muhrim example
A person in ihram points to game; another hunts it. The act of pointing is the sabab, the hunting is the intervening cause. Because the harmer acted based on the indication, the intervening cause is attributed to the muhrim, making him liable for the value.
The muhrim abandoned the trust of ihram by indicating.
4
Compare with the depositary example
A depositary (amin) directs a thief to the deposited item. The theft is the intervening cause, but it is attributed to the direction because the depositary failed in his duty of preservation.
The pattern: sabab + intervening cause attributable → liability for value.
5
Distinguish the driving/leading animal case
Driving or leading an animal that then tramples something is a sabab. The animal's action is the intervening cause, but it is NOT attributed to the driver/leader for criminal penalties (qisas, kaffarah, deprivation of inheritance) because the animal has no independent choice; yet it IS attributed for compensation (diyah, value). This refines the rule.
Thus, the second type applies only for compensation, not for penal consequences.

وَأَمَّا الْمُحْرِمُ الدَّالُ عَلَى صَيْدٍ فَإِنَّمَا ضَمِنَ قِيمَتَهُ لِأَنَّهُ تَرَكَ الْأَمَانَ الْمُلْتَزِمَ بِإِحْرَامِهِ بِفِعْلِ الدَّلَالَةِ، كَالْمُودِعِ إِذَا دَلَّ السَّارِقَ عَلَى الْوَدِيعَةِ يُضْمَنُ لِكَوْنِهِ تَارِكًا لِلْحِفْظِ الْمُلْتَزِمِ. فَإِنْ أُضِيفَتِ الْعِلَّةُ الْمُتَخَلِّلَةُ بَيْنَ السَّبَبِ وَالْحُكْمِ إِلَيْهِ، أَيْ إِلَى السَّبَبِ، صَارَ السَّبَبُ فِي حُكْمِ الْعِلَلِ فِي وُجُوبِ الضَّمَانِ عَلَيْهِ، لِأَنَّ الْحُكْمَ حِينَئِذٍ مُضَافٌ إِلَى الْعِلَّةِ، وَالْعِلَّةُ مُضَافَةٌ إِلَى السَّبَبِ، فَكَانَ السَّبَبُ عِلَّةَ الْعِلَّةِ. وَهَذَا هُوَ الْقِسْمُ الثَّانِي مِنَ السَّبَبِ. وَفِيهِ فَائِدَةُ الِاحْتِرَازِ عَنْ قَوْلِهِ: عِلَّةٌ لَا تُضَافُ إِلَى السَّبَبِ كَسَوْقِ الدَّابَّةِ وَقَوْدِهَا، فَإِنَّ كُلَّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا سَبَبٌ لِتَلَفِ مَا يُتْلَفُ بِوَطْئِهَا فِي حَالَةِ السَّوْقِ وَالْقَوْدِ، وَقَدْ تَخَلَّلَ بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ التَّلَفِ مَا هُوَ عِلَّةٌ لَهُ وَهُوَ فِعْلُ الدَّابَّةِ، لَكِنَّهُ مُضَافٌ إِلَى السَّوْقِ وَالْقَوْدِ لِأَنَّ الدَّابَّةَ لَا اخْتِيَارَ لَهَا فِي فِعْلِهَا سِيَّمَا إِذَا كَانَ أَحَدٌ سَائِقًا أَوْ قَائِدًا لَهَا. وَالْعِلَّةُ لَيْسَتْ صَالِحَةً لِلْحُكْمِ، فَيُضَافُ التَّلَفُ إِلَى عِلَّةِ الْعِلَّةِ فِيمَا يَرْجِعُ إِلَى بَدَلِ الْمَحَلِّ، وَهُوَ ضِمَانُ الدِّيَةِ وَالْقِيمَةِ. وَأَمَّا فِيمَا يَرْجِعُ إِلَى جَزَاءِ الْمُبَاشَرَةِ فَلَا يَكُونُ مُضَافًا إِلَيْهَا، فَلَا يَحْرِمُ مِنَ الْمِيرَاثِ وَلَا يَجِبُ عَلَيْهِ الْكَفَّارَةُ وَالْقِصَاصُ. وَالْيَمِينُ بِاللَّهِ تَعَالَى بِأَنْ يَقُولَ: وَاللَّهِ لَأَفْعَلَنَّ كَذَا أَوْ لَا أَفْعَلُ كَذَا، أَوْ بِالطَّلَاقِ وَالْعِتَاقِ بِأَنْ يَقُولَ: إِنْ دَخَلْتِ الدَّارَ فَأَنْتِ طَالِقٌ أَوْ أَنْتَ حُرٌّ، يُسَمَّى سَبَبًا مَجَازًا لِلْكَفَّارَةِ وَالْجَزَاءِ، وَهَذَا الْقِسْمُ الثَّالِثُ مِنَ السَّبَبِ. وَإِنَّمَا كَانَ سَبَبًا مَجَازًا لِأَنَّ الْيَمِينَ شُرِعَتْ لِلْبِرِّ، وَالْبِرُّ لَا يَكُونُ قَطُّ طَرِيقًا إِلَى الْكَفَّارَةِ فِي الْيَمِينِ بِاللَّهِ، وَلَا إِلَى الْجَزَاءِ فِي الْيَمِينِ بِغَيْرِ اللَّهِ، لِأَنَّهُ مَانِعٌ مِنَ الْحِنْثِ، وَبِدُونِ الْحِنْثِ لَا تَجِبُ الْكَفَّارَةُ وَلَا يَنْزِلُ الْجَزَاءُ. وَلَكِنْ لَمَّا كَانَ يَحْتَمِلُ أَنْ يُقْضَى إِلَى الْحُكْمِ عِنْدَ زَوَالِ الْمَانِعِ سُمِّيَ سَبَبًا مَجَازًا بِاعْتِبَارِ مَا يُؤُولُ إِلَيْهِ. وَعِنْدَ الشَّافِعِيِّ الْيَمِينُ بِاللَّهِ وَالْمُعَلَّقُ بِالشَّرْطِ سَبَبٌ حَقِيقِيٌّ لِلْكَفَّارَةِ وَالْجَزَاءِ. اور بہر حال محرم (جو شخص احرام باندھے ہو) اگر شکار کا پتہ بتا دیے تو وہ قیمت کا ضامن ہوتا ترجمہ و تشریح ہے کیونکہ اس نے اس امان کو ترک کر دیا ہے جو اس نے احرام باندھنے کے وقت اپنے اوپر لازم کیا تھا جس طرح امین (جس کے پاس امانت کا مال رکھا ہوا ہے) اگر چور کو ودیعت کے مال کی نشاندھی کردے اور چور اس مال ودیعت کو (اس کے پاس سے) چرا لے جائے تو امین اس کا ضامن ہو گا اس حفاظت کے ترک کرنے کی وجہ سے جس کو اس نے مال ودیعت کو اپنے پاس رکھتے ہوئے اپنے اوپر لازم کر لیا تھا۔ فَإِنْ أُضِيفَ الْعِلَّةُ الْمُتَخَلِّلَةُ (ب) جو علت سبب اور حکم کے درمیان ہے اگر اس کی نسبت سبب کی طرف ہو تو ایسا سبب علت کے حکم میں ہو جائے گا اس پر تاوان واجب ہونے کے بارے میں کیونکہ اس وقت حکم علت کی طرف منسوب ہے اور علت سبب کی طرف منسوب ہے لہذا سبب علیہ العلت ہو گیا اور یہی سبب کی قسم ثانی ہے اور اس میں احتراز کا فائدہ بھی حاصل ہو گیا اس کے قول عِلَّةٌ لَا تُضَافُ إِلَى السَّبَبِ كَسَوْقِ الدَّابَّةِ وَقَوْدِهَا جیسے جانور کو پیچھے سے بنا کر یا پیچھے سے کھینچ کرنے جانا کیونکہ یہ دونوں باتیں اس چیز کے تلف (پلاک) ہونے کا سبب ہیں جو چیز کہ اس جانور کے پیروں کے نیچے کچل کر ہلاک ہو جائے خواہ حالت سوق کی ہے (جانور کو بنگا کر لے جایا گیا ہو) یا حالت تور کی ہو کہ جانور کو آگے سے بیچ کر لے جایا گیا ہو) البتہ اس سبب اور تلف کے درمیان علت کا واسطہ موجود ہے یعنی جانور کا اس چیز کو اپنے چہروں سے کھل کر پامال کرنا مگر جانور کا یہ فعل بنگانے اور کھینچ کر لے جانے کی طرف کپ ہے اس وجہ سے کہ جانور کو اپنے فعل میں اختیار نہیں ہے بالخصوص اس صورت میں کہ جانور کو آگے سینچنے والا پیچھے سے بنگانے والا موجود ہو۔ وَالْعِلَّةُ لَيْسَتْ صَالِحَةً لِلْحُكْمِ اور تلف (حکم) کی نسبت جب علت (روند نے کچلنے) کی طرف نہیں ہو سکتی تو لا محالہ تلف کی نسبت علیہ العالی کی طرف ہو گی صرف تلف شدہ چیز کے بدل یعنی قیمت یا تاوان ازاء کمرنے کے حکم میں لیکن وہ سزا جو براہ راست مباشرت ارتکاب فعل) سے متعلق ہے جو بواسطہ علت سبب کی طرف منسوب نہیں ہوگی لہذا (اگر جانور سائق یا قائد کے مورث کو بلاک کر دے تو وہ میراث سے حروم نہیں ہو گا اور نہ کفارہ قتل یا قصاص واجب ہو گا۔ وَالْيَمِينَ بِاللَّهِ تَعَالَى (ج) اور اللہ کے نام پرسم مثلا یہ کہنا کہ وَاللَّهِ لَأَفْعَلَنَّ كَذَا (خدا کی قسم میں یہ کام ضرور کروں گا) یا یہ قسم کھائے کہ وَاللَّهِ لَا أَفْعَلُ كَذَا (خدا کی قسم میں ایسا کام نہیں کروں گا) أَوْ بِالطَّلَاقِ وَالْعِتَاقِ اور تعلیق بالطلاق اور تعلیق بالعتاق مثلنا اس شخص کا یہ کہنا کہ إِنْ دَخَلْتِ الدَّارَ فَأَنْتِ طَالِقٌ (اگر تو گھر میں داخل ہوئی تو تجھ کو طلاق ہے) یا یہ کہنا کہ تو آزاد ہے يُسَمَّى سَبَبًا مَجَازًا تو مجاز سبب کہا جائے گا کفارہ لازم آئے یا جزاء کے مرتب ہونے کے سلسلے میں یہ سب کی تیسری قسم ہے اس کو سبب مجازی اس وجہ سے کہتے ہیں کہ کیونکہ یمین (قسم) پوری کرنے کے لئے مشروع ہوتی ہے اور پورا ہونا کفارہ کا ذریعہ نہیں ہوا کرتا یمین باللہ کی صورت میں اور نہ جزاء کا سبب ہوتا ہے غیر اللہ کی قسم کھانے کے سبب سے کیونکہ پورا کرنا حنث ہونے سے مانع ہے اور بغیر حنث کے کفارہ واجب نہیں ہوتا اور نہ جزاء عائد ہوتی ہے لیکن چونکہ احتمال اس میں رکھتا ہے کہ حنث کی رکاوٹ نہ ہونے پر وہ یعنی قسم کفارہ یا جزاء تک پہنچا رہتا ہے اس لئے مآلاً کے اعتبار سے مجازاً اس کا نام سبب رکھ دیا گیا ہے۔ وَعِنْدَ الشَّافِعِيِّ الْيَمِينُ بِاللَّهِ وَالْمُعَلَّقُ بِالشَّرْطِ سَبَبٌ حَقِيقِيٌّ لِلْكَفَّارَةِ وَالْجَزَاءِ.
As for the muhrim (one in ihram) who points to game, he is liable for its value because he abandoned the trust he was obligated to by his ihram through the act of pointing, like the depositary if he directs the thief to the deposit, he is liable for abandoning the entrusted preservation. If the intervening cause between the sabab and the hukm is attributed to it, i.e., to the sabab, then the sabab becomes in the status of causes regarding the obligation of compensation upon him, because the hukm then is attributed to the cause, and the cause is attributed to the sabab, so the sabab becomes the cause of the cause. This is the second type of sabab. And in it is the benefit of avoiding his statement: a cause not attributed to the sabab, like driving and leading an animal, for each of them is a sabab for the destruction of what is destroyed by its trampling while driving or leading, and an intervening cause between it and the destruction, which is the animal's action, has intervened, but it is attributed to the driving and leading because the animal has no choice in its action, especially if someone is driving or leading it. And the cause is not suitable for the ruling, so the destruction is attributed to the cause of the cause regarding what pertains to the replacement of the thing, which is the guarantee of blood money and value. As for what pertains to the penalty of direct action, it is not attributed to it, so he is not deprived of inheritance, and kaffarah and qisas are not obligatory upon him. The oath by Allah Almighty, such as saying 'By Allah, I will surely do such and such' or 'I will not do such and such', or by divorce and manumission, such as saying 'If you enter the house, you are divorced' or 'you are free', is called a metaphorical sabab for kaffarah and penalty, and this is the third type of sabab. It is only a metaphorical sabab because the oath is legislated for piety, and piety is never a path to kaffarah in an oath by Allah, nor to penalty in an oath by other than Allah, because it is a preventer of breaking the oath, and without breaking the oath, kaffarah is not obligatory and penalty does not occur. But since it can lead to the ruling when the preventer is removed, it is called a metaphorical sabab considering what it leads to. According to al-Shafi'i, the oath by Allah and the conditional phrase are real causes for kaffarah and penalty. [Urdu commentary follows similarly.]
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the types of sabab (cause) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh, specifically the second and third types. The author begins by illustrating the second type with the example of a muhrim (one in ihram) who points out game to someone else, who then hunts it. The muhrim is liable for the value of the game because he abandoned the trust of ihram by indicating the game. This is analogous to a depositary (amin) who points out the deposited item to a thief and is held liable. In both cases, the intervening cause (the actual killing or theft) is attributed to the original sabab (the indication), making the sabab legally like a direct cause. This is the second type: when the intervening 'illah is added to the sabab. The benefit of this is to avoid the opposite case, where the 'illah is not attributed to the sabab, like driving and leading an animal. Here, the driving or leading is a sabab, but the actual destruction is due to the animal's action. However, because the animal has no choice, the destruction is attributed to the driving/leading for the purpose of compensation (diyah and value), but not for criminal penalties (kaffarah, qisas, deprivation of inheritance). The third type of sabab is metaphorical: oaths by Allah or conditional divorce/manumission. These are called sabab metaphorically because their primary purpose is piety or prevention, not to incur kaffarah or penalty. However, if the oath is broken or the condition occurs, they can lead to these consequences, so they are considered causes in a metaphorical sense by virtue of their outcome. Finally, the author notes that Imam al-Shafi'i considers these to be real causes, reflecting a difference in usul methodology regarding causation.

Key Terms
سَبَب (sabab): A cause that leads to a legal ruling, either directly, through an intervening cause, or metaphorically.
عِلَّة ('illah): The effective cause that directly produces the ruling; in the second type, it intervenes between the sabab and the hukm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi classification of the second type of sabab, a muhrim who points to game is liable for the value because:
A) He directly hunted the game himself.
B) The intervening act of hunting is attributed to his indication.
C) He broke his oath of ihram.
D) He committed a sin that requires expiation.

Key Takeaway
When an intervening cause is attributed to the sabab, the sabab is treated as a direct cause for compensation but not for criminal penalties.
