الشرْطُ سابقا عَلى العِلْةِ كَدَخُول الدار فِي قَوْلِهِ أَنْتِ طَالِقَ إِنْ دَخَلَتِ الدَّارَ إِذ هُوَ مُؤَخِّرٌ عَنْ تَكَلَّمَ قَوْلِهِ أَنْتِ طَالِقُ فَإِنَّهُ شَرْطٌ مَحْضَ دَاخِل فِي الْقِسم الاَوَّلِ كَمَا إِذَا خَلَّ قِيْدَ عَبَدٍ فَابَقَ فَإِنَّهُ شَرْطُ لِلآبَاقِ إِذا الْقَيْدِ وَكَانَ كَابَعًا وَإِزْللَّهُ شَرْطَ وَلَكِنْ تَخَلَّلَ بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ الآبَاقِ فِعْلُ فَاعِلِ مُخْتَارٍ وَهُوَ الْعَبْدُ وَلَيْسَ هَذَ الْفِعْلُ مَنْسَوْبًا إلى الشرط إذ لا يلزم أن يَكُونَ كُلُّ مَا يُحِلُّ القيد أبق النيئة وقد تقدم يَلْزَمُ الْقَيْدَ هذَا الْحَل عَلى الإِبَاقِ فَهُوَ فِى حُكْمِ الأَسْبَابِ فَلِهذا لا يَضْمِنَ الْحَالُ قِيْمَةُ الْعَبْدِ بِخِلافِ ما إذا أَمَرَ الْعَبُدَ بِالإِبَاقِ حَيْثُ يَضْمِنَ الأمِرُ وَإِنْ اِعْتَرَضَ فِعْلُ فَاعِل مختار لأن الأمر بالاباق استعمال لَهُ فَإِذَا الْقَيْدَ كَانَ مَا نِعًا فَارَ اللهُ شَرْطُ اسْتِعْمَالَ وَلَكِنْ فَإِذَا أَبْقَ بَامْرِه فَكَأَنَّهُ عَصَبَةَ بالاِسْتِعْمَال بِخِلَافٍ مَا إِذَا كَانَتِ الْوَاسِطَةُ المُتَخَلَّلَةُ مُضافة إلى السَّهَب فَإِنَّهُ يَضْمِنُ صَاحِبَ السَّبَبِ كَسَوْقِي الدَّابَّةِ وقَوْدُهَا إِذْ فِعْلُ الدَّابَّةِ وَهُوَ التَّلَفُ مُضَافُ إِلى السَّائِقِ وَالْقَائِدِ فَيَضْمِنَانِ مَا تَلْفَ بهَا وَالرَّابِعُ شَرْطُ اِسْمًا لَاحَكْمًا كَاوّل الشَّرْطَيْنِ فِي حُكُم تَعَلْقِ بِهَا لَقَوْلِهِ لِامْرَأَتِهِ إِنْ دَخَلَتِ هَذِهِ الدَّارَ فَهَذِهِ الدَّارَ فَانْتِ طَالِقٌ فَإِنْ دُخُولَ الدَّارِ الَّذِي يُوْجَدُ أَوْلاً يَكُون شرطًا اسمًا لاَ حُكْمًا إِذا حُكْمُ مُضافٌ إلى آخِرِ الشَّرْطَيْنِ وُجُوْدًا فَهُوَ شرطة إسما وحُكْمًا مِنْ جَمِيعِ الوُجُوهِ. ترجمه و تشریح والثالث شرط لَهُ حُكْمُ الاستبَاب (۳) ایسی شرط جو اسباب کے حکم میں ہو یہ وہ شرط کہلاتی ہے کہ جس کے اور مشروط کے درمیان فاعل مختار کے فعل کا فصل او ویل واقع ہو جائے فعل حمردہ فعل اس شرط کی طرف منسوب نہ ہو اور وہ شری فعل سے مقدم اور سابق ہو یہ کہہ کر اس فعل سے احتراز کرنا مقصود ہے جو فعل کے درمیان واقع ہوا ہے فاعل مختار کا طبیعی فعل ہو جیسے کنویں کا کھو وہ کیونکہ حفر البید علت کے حکم میں ہے اور بہر حال وہ فعل کہ جو اس شرط کی جانب منسوب ہو جیسے پرندے کے پنجرے کا اور کھول دینا کیونکہ پرندے کا اڑ جانا قفص سے کھولنے کی طرف منسوب ہے تو وہ فعل بھی امام محمد کے نزد یک ملت کے کے حکم میں ہے یہاں تک کہ کھولنے والا امام محمد کے نزد یک پرندے کا ضامن ہو گا البتہ اس میں شیخین (امام صاحب اور امام ابو یوسف ) کا اختلاف ہے ایسے ہی اس سے احتراز کرتا ہے کہ شرط علت سے مقدم نہ ہو جیسے دخول دار انت طالق ان دخلت الدار ہیں۔ کیونکہ و قول دار اس کے قول انت طالق الخ کے تکلم سے مؤخر ہے کیونکہ شرط محض ہے جو شرط کی قسم اول میں داخل ہے۔ كَمَا إِذا حَلْ قِيْدَ عَبْدَ فَأَبَق جیسے کسی نے غلام کی بیزی کھولدی اور غلام بھاگ گیا کہ بیری کا کھولدینا
نور الانوار جلد سوم
اشرف الانوار شرح اردو غلام کے بھاگ جانے کی شرط ہے کیونکہ میری (قید) بھاگنے سے مانع تھی لہذا بھاگنے کی شرط اس کا زائل کر دیتا ہے۔ یعنی بیری کا مگر اس شرط کھولنے اور بھاگنے کے درمیان فاعل مختار کا تعل واقع ہو گیا اور فاعل مختار غلام ہے اور یہ فعل شرط کی طرف منسوب نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہ ضروری نہیں ہے کہ جس کی قید و بند کو کھول دیا جائے تو د مسقینا بھاگ ہی جائے گا اور یہ حل (گرہ کا کھول دینا) بھاگنے سے مقدم ہی ہے لہذا اگرہ کا کھولنا اسباب حکم کے درجہ میں ہے فلهذا لا يضمن الحال لہذا گرو کا کھولنے والا غلام کی قیمت کا ضامن نہ ہو گا بخلاف اس کے کہ اس نے غلام کو بھاگنے کا مشورہ (حکم دیا تو آمر ضامن ہو گا اگر فاعل مختار کا فعل و بر میان میں پیش آگیا ہے اس وجہ سے کہ بھاگنے کا حکم دینا اس سے کام لینے کو شامل ہے پس جب غلام اس کے حکم سے بھاگ نکلا پس یوں سمجھا جائے گا کہ آمر نے اپنے استعمال میں لانے کے لئے اس کو غصب کر لیا ہے اس کے بر خلاف اگر واسطہ محللہ (آمر اور غلام کے بھاگنے کے درمیان کا واسطہ ) سبب کی طرف مضاف ہو (یعنی واسطہ کی نسبت سب کی طرف ہو تو صاحب سبب اس کا ضامن ہو گا جیسے جانور کو پیچھے سے ہنگا کر لے جانا یا جانور کو آگے آگے کھینچتے جانا اور جانور کو اس طرح پر لے جانا اس صورت میں واہ (جانور) کا فعل یعنی اس کا ہلاک ہو جانا قائد اور سائل کی طرف منسوب ہوگا۔ لہذا دونوں اس جانور کا تاوان دیں گے جو ان کے لے جانے سے ہلاک ہوا ہے والرابع شرط إسماً لا حُكْماً كَأَوْلِ الشَّرِطَيْنِ فِي حُكْم الخ (۴) چو تھی وہ شرط جو صرف اما ہو اور حکمانہ ہو جیسے ان دو شرطوں میں سے پہلی شرط جن دونوں کے ساتھ کسی حکم کا تعلق ہو مثلاً کوئی اپنی یوی سے کہے اِن دَخَلْتِ الدَّارَ فَهَذِهِ الدَّارَ فَانْتِ طَالِق (اگر تو اس گھر میں اور اس گھر میں داخل ہوئی تو تجھ کو طلاق ہے) کیونکہ دخول دار جو او لایا یا جائے گاوہ اس شرط کے بعد) برائے نام شرط ہو گا حکم میں شرط نہ ہو گا اس وجہ سے کہ وقوع طلاق کا حکم دونوں شرطوں میں سے آخری شرط پر موقوف ہے لہذاوہ اسماد حکمنا دونوں طریق پر اس کی دو قوع طلاق کی شرط ہے ہر اعتبار ہے۔ لووُجِدَ الشَّرْطَانِ فِي الْمِلْكِ بأن بَقِيَتْ مَنْكُوحَةٌ لَهُ عِنْدَ وُجُودِهِمَا فَلا شك أنه يَنْزِلُ الْجَرَاءِ وَإِنْ لَمْ يُوْجَدَا فِي الْمِلْكِ أوْ وُجد الأول في المِلْكِ دَوْنَ الثَّانِي فَلاً شكُ أَنَّهُ لَا يَنْزَلُ الْجَزَاء وَإِنْ وُجِدَ الثَّانِي فِي المِلْكِ دُونَ الأَوَّلِ بِأَنْ أَبَاتُهَا الرُّوْحُ فَدَخَلَتِ الدَّارَ الأولى ثُمَّ تَزَوْجَهَا فَدَخَلَتِ الدَّارَ الثَّانِيَةَ يَنْزِلُ الْجَزَاءُ وَتُطَلْقَ عِندَنَا لأَن المَدَارَ عَلَى آخِرِ الشَّرْطَيْنِ وَالْمِلْكُ إِنَّمَا يَحْتَاجُ إِلَيْهِ فِي وَقْتِ التَّعْلِيقِ وَفِي وَقْتِ نُزولِ الْجَزَاءِ وَأَمَّا فِى مَابَيْنَ ذَالِكَ فَلاً وعِنْدَ زَفَرَ لا تُطلق لأنه يقيس الشرْطُ الآخَرُ عَلى الأَوَّلِ اذْلَوْ كَانَ الأَوَّلُ يُوجَدُ فِي الْمِلْكِ دُونَ الآخَرِ لا تُطلق فَكَذَا عَكْسَهُ وَالْخَامِسَ شَرْطِ هُوَ كَالْعَلَامَةِ الْخَالِصَةِ كَالإِحْسَانِ فِي الزِّنَا شرط لِلرَّجم فِي مَعْنَى الْعَلَامَةِ وَقَدْ عَدُّوا هَذَا تَارَةً فِي الشَّرْطِ وَتَارَةُ فِي الْعَلَامَةِ
The condition is prior to the cause, like entering the house in his statement: 'You are divorced if you enter the house,' for it (the condition) is subsequent to his utterance of 'You are divorced.' So it is a pure condition falling into the first category. Similarly, when one unfastens the shackle of a slave and he runs away, for unfastening the shackle is a condition for the running away, since the shackle was preventing [him] and unfastening it is a condition. But between [unfastening] and the running away, the act of a free agent intervened—that is, the slave. And this act is not attributed to the condition, because it is not necessary that everyone whose shackle is unfastened runs away immediately. And this unfastening preceded the running away, so it is in the ruling of causes. Hence, the unfastener does not guarantee the value of the slave, unlike if he commanded the slave to run away, where the commander guarantees, even though the act of a free agent intervened. Because commanding the running away constitutes using him [as an instrument]; so when he runs away by his command, it is as if he (the commander) seized him by using him. Contrary to if the intervening medium is attributed to the cause, then the originator of the cause guarantees, like driving the animal from behind and leading it, for the act of the animal—that is, its destruction—is attributed to the driver and the leader; so both guarantee what perished by it. The fourth: a condition in name only, not in effect, like the first of two conditions in the ruling of attachment to it by his statement to his wife: 'If you enter this house and this house, then you are divorced.' For the entry into the house that occurs first is a condition in name only, not in effect, because the effect is attached to the last of the two conditions in existence; so that one (the last) is a condition in name and in effect in all respects. Translation and commentary: The third: a condition that has the ruling of causes. This is called a condition that is between it and the conditioned there occurs the intervening act of a free agent, and that act is not attributed to the condition, and it (the condition) is prior to the act. By saying 'this act' he intends to avoid the act that occurs in between, which is a natural act of a free agent, like digging a well, because digging is in the ruling of a cause. Nevertheless, the act that is attributed to the condition, like opening a bird's cage, because the bird's flying away is attributed to opening the cage, so such an act is also in the ruling of a cause according to Imam Muhammad, to the extent that the opener guarantees the bird according to Imam Muhammad, but there is disagreement between the two shaykhs (Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf). Similarly, he avoids that the condition not be prior to the cause, like 'entry into the house' in 'you are divorced if you enter the house,' for that statement is subsequent to the utterance of 'you are divorced,' because it is a pure condition that falls into the first category. As when one unfastens the shackle of a slave and he runs away: the unfastening of the shackle is a condition for the slave's running away, because the shackle was preventing him from running away, so the condition for running away is to remove it. But between this condition (unfastening) and the running away, the act of a free agent occurred—the slave. And this act is not attributed to the condition, because it is not necessary that whoever's shackle is unfastened immediately runs away. And this unfastening preceded the running away, so the unfastening is in the rank of causes. Hence, the unfastener does not guarantee the value of the slave, unlike if he gave the slave a command (or ordered him) to run away, then the commander guarantees even if the act of a free agent intervened. Because the command to run away includes using him; so when the slave runs away by his command, it is as if the commander seized him for his use. On the contrary, if the intervening medium is attributed to the cause, then the originator of the cause guarantees, like driving the animal from behind or leading it, for the act of the animal—its destruction—is attributed to the driver and the leader; so both guarantee the animal that perished by their driving. And the fourth: a condition in name only, not in effect, like the first of two conditions in the ruling of attachment... (4) The fourth is the condition that is only in name and not in effect, like the first of two conditions with which some ruling is attached. For example, a man says to his wife: 'If you enter this house and this house, then you are divorced.' Because the entry into the house that occurs first is a condition in name only, not in effect, because the occurrence of divorce is dependent on the last of the two conditions; hence that last one is a condition in name and effect in all respects. If both conditions are found in the marriage (i.e., she remains his wife at the time of their occurrence), then without doubt the consequence occurs. If both are not found in the marriage, or the first is found in the marriage but not the second, then without doubt the consequence does not occur. And if the second is found in the marriage but not the first—for example, she was divorced and then entered the first house, then he remarried her and she entered the second house—then the consequence occurs and she is divorced according to us, because the reliance is on the last of the two conditions, and marriage is only needed at the time of suspension and at the time of the consequence; as for in between, it is not needed. According to Zufar, she is not divorced, because he analogizes the other condition to the first: if the first is found in marriage without the second, she is not divorced; similarly, its reverse. And the fifth: a condition like a pure sign, like ihsan (being married) in zina (adultery) is a condition for stoning in the sense of a sign. And they have sometimes counted this as a condition and sometimes as a sign.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Anwar, a commentary on Nur al-Anwar, presents the categorization of conditions (shart) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh, focusing on the third, fourth, and fifth types. The author explains each type with legal examples and occasional disputes within the Hanafi school. The third type is a condition that has the ruling of a cause (shart lahu hukm al-asbab). This occurs when a condition is prior to the conditioned, but between them an act of a free agent intervenes that is not attributed to the condition. The example given: someone unfastens a slave's shackle, and the slave chooses to run away. The unfastening is a condition for the running, but since the slave's act (a free choice) is not necessarily caused by the unfastening, the unfastener is not liable for the slave's value. However, if he commands the slave to run away, he is liable because commanding implies using the slave as an instrument. This distinction shows that the condition here is treated like a cause (sabab) in terms of liability only when the intervening act is attributed to the condition. The passage also contrasts with cases where the intervening act is naturally attributed to the cause, like driving an animal: the animal's destruction is attributed to the driver, so he guarantees. The fourth type is a condition in name only (shart isman la hukman). This occurs when multiple conditions are stipulated in a single sentence, and only the last condition actually triggers the result. Example: 'If you enter this house and this house, you are divorced' – the first entry is a condition in name only; the divorce is triggered by both entries, but because the second entry is the last condition, it is the effective one. There is a dispute between the Hanafis and Zufar: if the first entry occurs without marriage (e.g., after divorce) and then the second entry occurs after remarriage, Hanafis say the divorce takes effect because only the last condition needs marriage at the time of occurrence; Zufar analogizes to the first condition. The fifth type is a condition like a pure sign (shart huwa kal-alamah al-khalisah), such as ihsan (being married) for zina, which is a condition for stoning not as a cause but as a sign that the crime is punishable by death. This type is sometimes considered a condition, sometimes a sign.

Key Terms
شرط له حكم الأسباب (shart lahu hukm al-asbab): A condition that has the ruling of a cause, used when an intervening free agent's act is attributed to the condition.
فاعل مختار (fa'il mukhtar): Free agent: a person who acts by their own choice, whose act is not necessarily caused by external conditions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example where someone unfastens a slave's shackle and the slave runs away, why is the unfastener not liable for the slave's value according to the passage?
A) Because the unfastening is a condition, not a cause.
B) Because the slave's act of running away is the act of a free agent and is not necessarily caused by the unfastening.
C) Because the unfastener did not command the slave to run away.
D) Both B and C

Key Takeaway
A condition that precedes a free agent's act does not create liability unless the act is attributed to the condition.

intermediate
8 min
The Fourth Type of Condition (Shart Isman La Hukman)
Defines the fourth category of shart with an example and an intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the fourth type of shart (shart isman la hukman) and apply it to determine which condition triggers a suspended ruling when multiple conditions are stipulated.

Core Idea
When multiple conditions are stated, only the last condition in existence actually determines the consequence.

The fourth category of conditions addresses cases where multiple conditions are suspended together. Not all conditions are equal: some are conditions in name only, while the last one has real legal effect. This lesson explores the example of two house entries and the dispute with Zufar.

Guided Path
1
Define the fourth type of shart
Identify the definition: a condition that is only a condition in name, not in effect (shart isman la hukman). This occurs when multiple conditions are stated together, and only the last condition in existence actually triggers the consequence.
The first condition is nominal; the last is effective.
2
Work through the two-house example
A man says: 'If you enter this house and this house, then you are divorced.' The condition is two entries. The first entry alone does not cause divorce; both must occur. But if the first occurs and then the second, the divorce is attached to the second entry because it is the last in existence.
The last condition is a condition in name and effect; the first is only in name.
3
Analyze the scenario with marriage
If the wife enters the first house after being divorced (no marriage), then remarries and enters the second house, Hanafis say divorce occurs. Marriage is only needed at the time of suspension (the conditional statement) and at the time the consequence triggers (the second entry). The first entry does not require marriage because it is nominal.
The reliance is on the last condition.
4
Compare with Zufar's view
Zufar analogizes the second condition to the first: if the first alone does not cause divorce when outside marriage, the second should not either. So he says no divorce.
Zufar uses qiyas on the first condition, while Hanafis distinguish based on which condition is effective.
5
Determine the practical consequence
In the given scenario, under Hanafi view the woman is divorced; under Zufar's view she is not. This shows the thamarah al-khilaf.
The difference hinges on whether the last condition is treated as independent or analogous to the first.

الشرْطُ سابقا عَلى العِلْةِ كَدَخُول الدار فِي قَوْلِهِ أَنْتِ طَالِقَ إِنْ دَخَلَتِ الدَّارَ إِذ هُوَ مُؤَخِّرٌ عَنْ تَكَلَّمَ قَوْلِهِ أَنْتِ طَالِقُ فَإِنَّهُ شَرْطٌ مَحْضَ دَاخِل فِي الْقِسم الاَوَّلِ كَمَا إِذَا خَلَّ قِيْدَ عَبَدٍ فَابَقَ فَإِنَّهُ شَرْطُ لِلآبَاقِ إِذا الْقَيْدِ وَكَانَ كَابَعًا وَإِزْللَّهُ شَرْطَ وَلَكِنْ تَخَلَّلَ بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ الآبَاقِ فِعْلُ فَاعِلِ مُخْتَارٍ وَهُوَ الْعَبْدُ وَلَيْسَ هَذَ الْفِعْلُ مَنْسَوْبًا إلى الشرط إذ لا يلزم أن يَكُونَ كُلُّ مَا يُحِلُّ القيد أبق النيئة وقد تقدم يَلْزَمُ الْقَيْدَ هذَا الْحَل عَلى الإِبَاقِ فَهُوَ فِى حُكْمِ الأَسْبَابِ فَلِهذا لا يَضْمِنَ الْحَالُ قِيْمَةُ الْعَبْدِ بِخِلافِ ما إذا أَمَرَ الْعَبُدَ بِالإِبَاقِ حَيْثُ يَضْمِنَ الأمِرُ وَإِنْ اِعْتَرَضَ فِعْلُ فَاعِل مختار لأن الأمر بالاباق استعمال لَهُ فَإِذَا الْقَيْدَ كَانَ مَا نِعًا فَارَ اللهُ شَرْطُ اسْتِعْمَالَ وَلَكِنْ فَإِذَا أَبْقَ بَامْرِه فَكَأَنَّهُ عَصَبَةَ بالاِسْتِعْمَال بِخِلَافٍ مَا إِذَا كَانَتِ الْوَاسِطَةُ المُتَخَلَّلَةُ مُضافة إلى السَّهَب فَإِنَّهُ يَضْمِنُ صَاحِبَ السَّبَبِ كَسَوْقِي الدَّابَّةِ وقَوْدُهَا إِذْ فِعْلُ الدَّابَّةِ وَهُوَ التَّلَفُ مُضَافُ إِلى السَّائِقِ وَالْقَائِدِ فَيَضْمِنَانِ مَا تَلْفَ بهَا وَالرَّابِعُ شَرْطُ اِسْمًا لَاحَكْمًا كَاوّل الشَّرْطَيْنِ فِي حُكُم تَعَلْقِ بِهَا لَقَوْلِهِ لِامْرَأَتِهِ إِنْ دَخَلَتِ هَذِهِ الدَّارَ فَهَذِهِ الدَّارَ فَانْتِ طَالِقٌ فَإِنْ دُخُولَ الدَّارِ الَّذِي يُوْجَدُ أَوْلاً يَكُون شرطًا اسمًا لاَ حُكْمًا إِذا حُكْمُ مُضافٌ إلى آخِرِ الشَّرْطَيْنِ وُجُوْدًا فَهُوَ شرطة إسما وحُكْمًا مِنْ جَمِيعِ الوُجُوهِ. ترجمه و تشریح والثالث شرط لَهُ حُكْمُ الاستبَاب (۳) ایسی شرط جو اسباب کے حکم میں ہو یہ وہ شرط کہلاتی ہے کہ جس کے اور مشروط کے درمیان فاعل مختار کے فعل کا فصل او ویل واقع ہو جائے فعل حمردہ فعل اس شرط کی طرف منسوب نہ ہو اور وہ شری فعل سے مقدم اور سابق ہو یہ کہہ کر اس فعل سے احتراز کرنا مقصود ہے جو فعل کے درمیان واقع ہوا ہے فاعل مختار کا طبیعی فعل ہو جیسے کنویں کا کھو وہ کیونکہ حفر البید علت کے حکم میں ہے اور بہر حال وہ فعل کہ جو اس شرط کی جانب منسوب ہو جیسے پرندے کے پنجرے کا اور کھول دینا کیونکہ پرندے کا اڑ جانا قفص سے کھولنے کی طرف منسوب ہے تو وہ فعل بھی امام محمد کے نزد یک ملت کے کے حکم میں ہے یہاں تک کہ کھولنے والا امام محمد کے نزد یک پرندے کا ضامن ہو گا البتہ اس میں شیخین (امام صاحب اور امام ابو یوسف ) کا اختلاف ہے ایسے ہی اس سے احتراز کرتا ہے کہ شرط علت سے مقدم نہ ہو جیسے دخول دار انت طالق ان دخلت الدار ہیں۔ کیونکہ و قول دار اس کے قول انت طالق الخ کے تکلم سے مؤخر ہے کیونکہ شرط محض ہے جو شرط کی قسم اول میں داخل ہے۔ كَمَا إِذا حَلْ قِيْدَ عَبْدَ فَأَبَق جیسے کسی نے غلام کی بیزی کھولدی اور غلام بھاگ گیا کہ بیری کا کھولدینا
نور الانوار جلد سوم
اشرف الانوار شرح اردو غلام کے بھاگ جانے کی شرط ہے کیونکہ میری (قید) بھاگنے سے مانع تھی لہذا بھاگنے کی شرط اس کا زائل کر دیتا ہے۔ یعنی بیری کا مگر اس شرط کھولنے اور بھاگنے کے درمیان فاعل مختار کا تعل واقع ہو گیا اور فاعل مختار غلام ہے اور یہ فعل شرط کی طرف منسوب نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہ ضروری نہیں ہے کہ جس کی قید و بند کو کھول دیا جائے تو د مسقینا بھاگ ہی جائے گا اور یہ حل (گرہ کا کھول دینا) بھاگنے سے مقدم ہی ہے لہذا اگرہ کا کھولنا اسباب حکم کے درجہ میں ہے فلهذا لا يضمن الحال لہذا گرو کا کھولنے والا غلام کی قیمت کا ضامن نہ ہو گا بخلاف اس کے کہ اس نے غلام کو بھاگنے کا مشورہ (حکم دیا تو آمر ضامن ہو گا اگر فاعل مختار کا فعل و بر میان میں پیش آگیا ہے اس وجہ سے کہ بھاگنے کا حکم دینا اس سے کام لینے کو شامل ہے پس جب غلام اس کے حکم سے بھاگ نکلا پس یوں سمجھا جائے گا کہ آمر نے اپنے استعمال میں لانے کے لئے اس کو غصب کر لیا ہے اس کے بر خلاف اگر واسطہ محللہ (آمر اور غلام کے بھاگنے کے درمیان کا واسطہ ) سبب کی طرف مضاف ہو (یعنی واسطہ کی نسبت سب کی طرف ہو تو صاحب سبب اس کا ضامن ہو گا جیسے جانور کو پیچھے دیں گے جو ان کے لے جانے سے ہلاک ہوا ہے والرابع شرط إسماً لا حُكْماً كَأَوْلِ الشَّرِطَيْنِ فِي حُكْم الخ (۴) چو تھی وہ شرط جو صرف اما ہو اور حکمانہ ہو جیسے ان دو شرطوں میں سے پہلی شرط جن دونوں کے ساتھ کسی حکم کا تعلق ہو مثلاً کوئی اپنی یوی سے کہے اِن دَخَلْتِ الدَّارَ فَهَذِهِ الدَّارَ فَانْتِ طَالِق (اگر تو اس گھر میں اور اس گھر میں داخل ہوئی تو تجھ کو طلاق ہے) کیونکہ دخول دار جو او لایا یا جائے گاوہ اس شرط کے بعد) برائے نام شرط ہو گا حکم میں شرط نہ ہو گا اس وجہ سے کہ وقوع طلاق کا حکم دونوں شرطوں میں سے آخری شرط پر موقوف ہے لہذاوہ اسماد حکمنا دونوں طریق پر اس کی دو قوع طلاق کی شرط ہے ہر اعتبار ہے۔ لووُجِدَ الشَّرْطَانِ فِي الْمِلْكِ بأن بَقِيَتْ مَنْكُوحَةٌ لَهُ عِنْدَ وُجُودِهِمَا فَلا شك أنه يَنْزِلُ الْجَرَاءِ وَإِنْ لَمْ يُوْجَدَا فِي الْمِلْكِ أوْ وُجد الأول في المِلْكِ دَوْنَ الثَّانِي فَلاً شكُ أَنَّهُ لَا يَنْزَلُ الْجَزَاء وَإِنْ وُجِدَ الثَّانِي فِي المِلْكِ دُونَ الأَوَّلِ بِأَنْ أَبَاتُهَا الرُّوْحُ فَدَخَلَتِ الدَّارَ الأولى ثُمَّ تَزَوْجَهَا فَدَخَلَتِ الدَّارَ الثَّانِيَةَ يَنْزِلُ الْجَزَاءُ وَتُطَلْقَ عِندَنَا لأَن المَدَارَ عَلَى آخِرِ الشَّرْطَيْنِ وَالْمِلْكُ إِنَّمَا يَحْتَاجُ إِلَيْهِ فِي وَقْتِ التَّعْلِيقِ وَفِي وَقْتِ نُزولِ الْجَزَاءِ وَأَمَّا فِى مَابَيْنَ ذَالِكَ فَلاً وعِنْدَ زَفَرَ لا تُطلق لأنه يقيس الشرْطُ الآخَرُ عَلى الأَوَّلِ اذْلَوْ كَانَ الأَوَّلُ يُوجَدُ فِي الْمِلْكِ دُونَ الآخَرِ لا تُطلق فَكَذَا عَكْسَهُ وَالْخَامِسَ شَرْطِ هُوَ كَالْعَلَامَةِ الْخَالِصَةِ كَالإِحْسَانِ فِي الزِّنَا شرط لِلرَّجم فِي مَعْنَى الْعَلَامَةِ وَقَدْ عَدُّوا هَذَا تَارَةً فِي الشَّرْطِ وَتَارَةُ فِي الْعَلَامَةِ
The condition is prior to the cause, like entering the house in his statement: 'You are divorced if you enter the house,' for it (the condition) is subsequent to his utterance of 'You are divorced.' So it is a pure condition falling into the first category. Similarly, when one unfastens the shackle of a slave and he runs away, for unfastening the shackle is a condition for the running away, since the shackle was preventing [him] and unfastening it is a condition. But between [unfastening] and the running away, the act of a free agent intervened—that is, the slave. And this act is not attributed to the condition, because it is not necessary that everyone whose shackle is unfastened runs away immediately. And this unfastening preceded the running away, so it is in the ruling of causes. Hence, the unfastener does not guarantee the value of the slave, unlike if he commanded the slave to run away, where the commander guarantees, even though the act of a free agent intervened. Because commanding the running away constitutes using him [as an instrument]; so when he runs away by his command, it is as if he (the commander) seized him by using him. Contrary to if the intervening medium is attributed to the cause, then the originator of the cause guarantees, like driving the animal from behind and leading it, for the act of the animal—that is, its destruction—is attributed to the driver and the leader; so both guarantee what perished by it. The fourth: a condition in name only, not in effect, like the first of two conditions in the ruling of attachment to it by his statement to his wife: 'If you enter this house and this house, then you are divorced.' For the entry into the house that occurs first is a condition in name only, not in effect, because the effect is attached to the last of the two conditions in existence; so that one (the last) is a condition in name and in effect in all respects. Translation and commentary: The third: a condition that has the ruling of causes. This is called a condition that is between it and the conditioned there occurs the intervening act of a free agent, and that act is not attributed to the condition, and it (the condition) is prior to the act. By saying 'this act' he intends to avoid the act that occurs in between, which is a natural act of a free agent, like digging a well, because digging is in the ruling of a cause. Nevertheless, the act that is attributed to the condition, like opening a bird's cage, because the bird's flying away is attributed to opening the cage, so such an act is also in the ruling of a cause according to Imam Muhammad, to the extent that the opener guarantees the bird according to Imam Muhammad, but there is disagreement between the two shaykhs (Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf). Similarly, he avoids that the condition not be prior to the cause, like 'entry into the house' in 'you are divorced if you enter the house,' for that statement is subsequent to the utterance of 'you are divorced,' because it is a pure condition that falls into the first category. As when one unfastens the shackle of a slave and he runs away: the unfastening of the shackle is a condition for the slave's running away, because the shackle was preventing him from running away, so the condition for running away is to remove it. But between this condition (unfastening) and the running away, the act of a free agent occurred—the slave. And this act is not attributed to the condition, because it is not necessary that whoever's shackle is unfastened immediately runs away. And this unfastening preceded the running away, so the unfastening is in the rank of causes. Hence, the unfastener does not guarantee the value of the slave, unlike if he gave the slave a command (or ordered him) to run away, then the commander guarantees even if the act of a free agent intervened. Because the command to run away includes using him; so when the slave runs away by his command, it is as if the commander seized him for his use. On the contrary, if the intervening medium is attributed to the cause, then the originator of the cause guarantees, like driving the animal from behind or leading it, for the act of the animal—its destruction—is attributed to the driver and the leader; so both guarantee the animal that perished by their driving. And the fourth: a condition in name only, not in effect, like the first of two conditions in the ruling of attachment... (4) The fourth is the condition that is only in name and not in effect, like the first of two conditions with which some ruling is attached. For example, a man says to his wife: 'If you enter this house and this house, then you are divorced.' Because the entry into the house that occurs first is a condition in name only, not in effect, because the occurrence of divorce is dependent on the last of the two conditions; hence that last one is a condition in name and effect in all respects. If both conditions are found in the marriage (i.e., she remains his wife at the time of their occurrence), then without doubt the consequence occurs. If both are not found in the marriage, or the first is found in the marriage but not the second, then without doubt the consequence does not occur. And if the second is found in the marriage but not the first—for example, she was divorced and then entered the first house, then he remarried her and she entered the second house—then the consequence occurs and she is divorced according to us, because the reliance is on the last of the two conditions, and marriage is only needed at the time of suspension and at the time of the consequence; as for in between, it is not needed. According to Zufar, she is not divorced, because he analogizes the other condition to the first: if the first is found in marriage without the second, she is not divorced; similarly, its reverse. And the fifth: a condition like a pure sign, like ihsan (being married) in zina (adultery) is a condition for stoning in the sense of a sign. And they have sometimes counted this as a condition and sometimes as a sign.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Anwar, a commentary on Nur al-Anwar, presents the categorization of conditions (shart) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh, focusing on the third, fourth, and fifth types. The author explains each type with legal examples and occasional disputes within the Hanafi school. The third type is a condition that has the ruling of a cause (shart lahu hukm al-asbab). This occurs when a condition is prior to the conditioned, but between them an act of a free agent intervenes that is not attributed to the condition. The example given: someone unfastens a slave's shackle, and the slave chooses to run away. The unfastening is a condition for the running, but since the slave's act (a free choice) is not necessarily caused by the unfastening, the unfastener is not liable for the slave's value. However, if he commands the slave to run away, he is liable because commanding implies using the slave as an instrument. This distinction shows that the condition here is treated like a cause (sabab) in terms of liability only when the intervening act is attributed to the condition. The passage also contrasts with cases where the intervening act is naturally attributed to the cause, like driving an animal: the animal's destruction is attributed to the driver, so he guarantees. The fourth type is a condition in name only (shart isman la hukman). This occurs when multiple conditions are stipulated in a single sentence, and only the last condition actually triggers the result. Example: 'If you enter this house and this house, you are divorced' – the first entry is a condition in name only; the divorce is triggered by both entries, but because the second entry is the last condition, it is the effective one. There is a dispute between the Hanafis and Zufar: if the first entry occurs without marriage (e.g., after divorce) and then the second entry occurs after remarriage, Hanafis say the divorce takes effect because only the last condition needs marriage at the time of occurrence; Zufar analogizes to the first condition. The fifth type is a condition like a pure sign (shart huwa kal-alamah al-khalisah), such as ihsan (being married) for zina, which is a condition for stoning not as a cause but as a sign that the crime is punishable by death. This type is sometimes considered a condition, sometimes a sign.

Key Terms
شرط اسمًا لا حكمًا (shart isman la hukman): A condition that is a condition only in name, not in effect, typically the first among multiple conditions.
التعليق (al-ta'liq): Suspension: attaching a legal consequence to the occurrence of a future condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario where a wife enters the first house after divorce and the second after remarriage, what is the Hanafi ruling according to the passage?
A) She is not divorced because the first entry was outside marriage.
B) She is divorced because the last condition is the effective one and marriage existed at that time.
C) She is divorced only if both entries occur within marriage.
D) The ruling depends on whether the husband intended the first or second entry.

Key Takeaway
When multiple conditions are stipulated, the last one in existence is the effective condition; earlier ones are nominal.

beginner
6 min
The Fifth Type of Condition: Condition as a Pure Sign (Shart Kal-Alamah)
Defines the fifth category of shart as a pure sign with the example of ihsan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the fifth type of shart (shart kal-alamah) and differentiate it from a true condition and a cause.

Core Idea
A condition that functions as a mere sign (alamah) indicates the ruling but does not cause or condition it.

The fifth and final category of conditions is unique: it is a condition in form only, really acting as a sign (alamah) that identifies when a ruling applies. The classic example is ihsan (being married) in zina, which is a condition for stoning but not a cause. Understanding this category prevents confusion between legal signs and actual conditions.

Guided Path
1
Define the fifth type of shart
Identify the definition: a condition that is like a pure sign (kal-alamah al-khalisah). It is not a cause or a true condition but an indicator that a particular ruling applies.
The usul scholars sometimes list this under conditions and sometimes under signs.
2
Work through the example of ihsan
Ihsan (being a free married Muslim) is a condition for stoning in zina. However, ihsan does not cause the stoning; it is a sign that the crime is punishable by death. The stoning is caused by the act of zina, not by the condition.
The sign indicates the threshold for the severe punishment.
3
Distinguish from other shart types
Unlike the first four types, this condition does not affect the existence or validity of the ruling; it merely classifies the ruling (e.g., whether it is lashing or stoning).
True conditions determine whether a ruling occurs; signs determine the intensity of the ruling.
4
Note the terminological flexibility
Scholars sometimes count this as a condition (shart) and sometimes as a sign (alamah). This reflects its borderline nature.
The passage says: 'وقد عدوا هذا تارة في الشرط وتارة في العلامة'.

الشرْطُ سابقا عَلى العِلْةِ كَدَخُول الدار فِي قَوْلِهِ أَنْتِ طَالِقَ إِنْ دَخَلَتِ الدَّارَ إِذ هُوَ مُؤَخِّرٌ عَنْ تَكَلَّمَ قَوْلِهِ أَنْتِ طَالِقُ فَإِنَّهُ شَرْطٌ مَحْضَ دَاخِل فِي الْقِسم الاَوَّلِ كَمَا إِذَا خَلَّ قِيْدَ عَبَدٍ فَابَقَ فَإِنَّهُ شَرْطُ لِلآبَاقِ إِذا الْقَيْدِ وَكَانَ كَابَعًا وَإِزْللَّهُ شَرْطَ وَلَكِنْ تَخَلَّلَ بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ الآبَاقِ فِعْلُ فَاعِلِ مُخْتَارٍ وَهُوَ الْعَبْدُ وَلَيْسَ هَذَ الْفِعْلُ مَنْسَوْبًا إلى الشرط إذ لا يلزم أن يَكُونَ كُلُّ مَا يُحِلُّ القيد أبق النيئة وقد تقدم يَلْزَمُ الْقَيْدَ هذَا الْحَل عَلى الإِبَاقِ فَهُوَ فِى حُكْمِ الأَسْبَابِ فَلِهذا لا يَضْمِنَ الْحَالُ قِيْمَةُ الْعَبْدِ بِخِلافِ ما إذا أَمَرَ الْعَبُدَ بِالإِبَاقِ حَيْثُ يَضْمِنَ الأمِرُ وَإِنْ اِعْتَرَضَ فِعْلُ فَاعِل مختار لأن الأمر بالاباق استعمال لَهُ فَإِذَا الْقَيْدَ كَانَ مَا نِعًا فَارَ اللهُ شَرْطُ اسْتِعْمَالَ وَلَكِنْ فَإِذَا أَبْقَ بَامْرِه فَكَأَنَّهُ عَصَبَةَ بالاِسْتِعْمَال بِخِلَافٍ مَا إِذَا كَانَتِ الْوَاسِطَةُ المُتَخَلَّلَةُ مُضافة إلى السَّهَب فَإِنَّهُ يَضْمِنُ صَاحِبَ السَّبَبِ كَسَوْقِي الدَّابَّةِ وقَوْدُهَا إِذْ فِعْلُ الدَّابَّةِ وَهُوَ التَّلَفُ مُضَافُ إِلى السَّائِقِ وَالْقَائِدِ فَيَضْمِنَانِ مَا تَلْفَ بهَا وَالرَّابِعُ شَرْطُ اِسْمًا لَاحَكْمًا كَاوّل الشَّرْطَيْنِ فِي حُكُم تَعَلْقِ بِهَا لَقَوْلِهِ لِامْرَأَتِهِ إِنْ دَخَلَتِ هَذِهِ الدَّارَ فَهَذِهِ الدَّارَ فَانْتِ طَالِقٌ فَإِنْ دُخُولَ الدَّارِ الَّذِي يُوْجَدُ أَوْلاً يَكُون شرطًا اسمًا لاَ حُكْمًا إِذا حُكْمُ مُضافٌ إلى آخِرِ الشَّرْطَيْنِ وُجُوْدًا فَهُوَ شرطة إسما وحُكْمًا مِنْ جَمِيعِ الوُجُوهِ. ترجمه و تشریح والثالث شرط لَهُ حُكْمُ الاستبَاب (۳) ایسی شرط جو اسباب کے حکم میں ہو یہ وہ شرط کہلاتی ہے کہ جس کے اور مشروط کے درمیان فاعل مختار کے فعل کا فصل او ویل واقع ہو جائے فعل حمردہ فعل اس شرط کی طرف منسوب نہ ہو اور وہ شری فعل سے مقدم اور سابق ہو یہ کہہ کر اس فعل سے احتراز کرنا مقصود ہے جو فعل کے درمیان واقع ہوا ہے فاعل مختار کا طبیعی فعل ہو جیسے کنویں کا کھو وہ کیونکہ حفر البید علت کے حکم میں ہے اور بہر حال وہ فعل کہ جو اس شرط کی جانب منسوب ہو جیسے پرندے کے پنجرے کا اور کھول دینا کیونکہ پرندے کا اڑ جانا قفص سے کھولنے کی طرف منسوب ہے تو وہ فعل بھی امام محمد کے نزد یک ملت کے کے حکم میں ہے یہاں تک کہ کھولنے والا امام محمد کے نزد یک پرندے کا ضامن ہو گا البتہ اس میں شیخین (امام صاحب اور امام ابو یوسف ) کا اختلاف ہے ایسے ہی اس سے احتراز کرتا ہے کہ شرط علت سے مقدم نہ ہو جیسے دخول دار انت طالق ان دخلت الدار ہیں۔ کیونکہ و نور الانوار جلد سوم
اشرف الانوار شرح اردو غلام کے بھاگ جانے کی شرط ہے کیونکہ میری (قید) بھاگنے سے مانع تھی لہذا بھاگنے کی شرط اس کا زائل کر دیتا ہے۔ یعنی بیری کا مگر اس شرط کھولنے اور بھاگنے کے درمیان فاعل مختار کا تعل دیں گے جو ان کے لے جانے سے ہلاک ہوا ہے والرابع شرط إسماً لا حُكْماً كَأَوْلِ الشَّرِطَيْنِ فِي حُكْم الخ (۴) چو تھی وہ شرط جو صرف اما ہو اور حکمانہ ہو جیسے ان دو شرطوں میں سے پہلی شرط جن دونوں کے ساتھ کسی حکم کا تعلق ہو مثلاً کوئی اپنی یوی سے کہے اِن دَخَلْتِ الدَّارَ فَهَذِهِ الدَّارَ فَانْتِ طَالِق (اگر تو اس گھر میں اور اس گھر میں داخل ہوئی تو تجھ کو طلاق ہے) کیونکہ دخول دار جو او لایا یا جائے گاوہ اس شرط کے بعد) برائے نام شرط ہو گا حکم میں شرط نہ ہو گا اس وجہ سے کہ وقوع طلاق کا حکم دونوں شرطوں میں سے آخری شرط پر موقوف ہے لہذاوہ اسماد حکمنا دونوں طریق پر اس کی دو قوع طلاق کی شرط ہے ہر اعتبار ہے۔ لووُجِدَ الشَّرْطَانِ فِي الْمِلْكِ بأن بَقِيَتْ مَنْكُوحَةٌ لَهُ عِنْدَ وُجُودِهِمَا فَلا شك أنه يَنْزِلُ الْجَرَاءِ وَإِنْ لَمْ يُوْجَدَا فِي الْمِلْكِ أوْ وُجد الأول في المِلْكِ دَوْنَ الثَّانِي فَلاً شكُ أَنَّهُ لَا يَنْزَلُ الْجَزَاء وَإِنْ وُجِدَ الثَّانِي فِي المِلْكِ دُونَ الأَوَّلِ بِأَنْ أَبَاتُهَا الرُّوْحُ فَدَخَلَتِ الدَّارَ الأولى ثُمَّ تَزَوْجَهَا فَدَخَلَتِ الدَّارَ الثَّانِيَةَ يَنْزِلُ الْجَزَاءُ وَتُطَلْقَ عِندَنَا لأَن المَدَارَ عَلَى آخِرِ الشَّرْطَيْنِ وَالْمِلْكُ إِنَّمَا يَحْتَاجُ إِلَيْهِ فِي وَقْتِ التَّعْلِيقِ وَفِي وَقْتِ نُزولِ الْجَزَاءِ وَأَمَّا فِى مَابَيْنَ ذَالِكَ فَلاً وعِنْدَ زَفَرَ لا تُطلق لأنه يقيس الشرْطُ الآخَرُ عَلى الأَوَّلِ اذْلَوْ كَانَ الأَوَّلُ يُوجَدُ فِي الْمِلْكِ دُونَ الآخَرِ لا تُطلق فَكَذَا عَكْسَهُ وَالْخَامِسَ شَرْطِ هُوَ كَالْعَلَامَةِ الْخَالِصَةِ كَالإِحْسَانِ فِي الزِّنَا شرط لِلرَّجم فِي مَعْنَى الْعَلَامَةِ وَقَدْ عَدُّوا هَذَا تَارَةً فِي الشَّرْطِ وَتَارَةُ فِي الْعَلَامَةِ
The condition is prior to the cause, like entering the house in his statement: 'You are divorced if you enter the house,' for it (the condition) is subsequent to his utterance of 'You are divorced.' So it is a pure condition falling into the first category. Similarly, when one unfastens the shackle of a slave and he runs away, for unfastening the shackle is a condition for the running away, since the shackle was preventing [him] and unfastening it is a condition. But between [unfastening] and the running away, the act of a free agent intervened—that is, the slave. And this act is not attributed to the condition, because it is not necessary that everyone whose shackle is unfastened runs away immediately. And this unfastening preceded the running away, so it is in the ruling of causes. Hence, the unfastener does not guarantee the value of the slave, unlike if he commanded the slave to run away, where the commander guarantees, even though the act of a free agent intervened. Because commanding the running away constitutes using him [as an instrument]; so when he runs away by his command, it is as if he (the commander) seized him by using him. Contrary to if the intervening medium is attributed to the cause, then the originator of the cause guarantees, like driving the animal from behind and leading it, for the act of the animal—that is, its destruction—is attributed to the driver and the leader; so both guarantee what perished by it. The fourth: a condition in name only, not in effect, like the first of two conditions in the ruling of attachment to it by his statement to his wife: 'If you enter this house and this house, then you are divorced.' For the entry into the house that occurs first is a condition in name only, not in effect, because the effect is attached to the last of the two conditions in existence; so that one (the last) is a condition in name and in effect in all respects. Translation and commentary: The third: a condition that has the ruling of causes. This is called a condition that is between it and the conditioned there occurs the intervening act of a free agent, and that act is not attributed to the condition, and it (the condition) is prior to the act. By saying 'this act' he intends to avoid the act that occurs in between, which is a natural act of a free agent, like digging a well, because digging is in the ruling of a cause. Nevertheless, the act that is attributed to the condition, like opening a bird's cage, because the bird's flying away is attributed to opening the cage, so such an act is also in the ruling of a cause according to Imam Muhammad, to the extent that the opener guarantees the bird according to Imam Muhammad, but there is disagreement between the two shaykhs (Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf). Similarly, he avoids that the condition not be prior to the cause, like 'entry into the house' in 'you are divorced if you enter the house,' for that statement is subsequent to the utterance of 'you are divorced,' because it is a pure condition that falls into the first category. As when one unfastens the shackle of a slave and he runs away: the unfastening of the shackle is a condition for the slave's running away, because the shackle was preventing him from running away, so the condition for running away is to remove it. But between this condition (unfastening) and the running away, the act of a free agent occurred—the slave. And this act is not attributed to the condition, because it is not necessary that whoever's shackle is unfastened immediately runs away. And this unfastening preceded the running away, so the unfastening is in the rank of causes. Hence, the unfastener does not guarantee the value of the slave, unlike if he gave the slave a command (or ordered him) to run away, then the commander guarantees even if the act of a free agent intervened. Because the command to run away includes using him; so when the slave runs away by his command, it is as if the commander seized him for his use. On the contrary, if the intervening medium is attributed to the cause, then the originator of the cause guarantees, like driving the animal from behind or leading it, for the act of the animal—its destruction—is attributed to the driver and the leader; so both guarantee the animal that perished by their driving. And the fourth: a condition in name only, not in effect, like the first of two conditions in the ruling of attachment... (4) The fourth is the condition that is only in name and not in effect, like the first of two conditions with which some ruling is attached. For example, a man says to his wife: 'If you enter this house and this house, then you are divorced.' Because the entry into the house that occurs first is a condition in name only, not in effect, because the occurrence of divorce is dependent on the last of the two conditions; hence that last one is a condition in name and effect in all respects. If both conditions are found in the marriage (i.e., she remains his wife at the time of their occurrence), then without doubt the consequence occurs. If both are not found in the marriage, or the first is found in the marriage but not the second, then without doubt the consequence does not occur. And if the second is found in the marriage but not the first—for example, she was divorced and then entered the first house, then he remarried her and she entered the second house—then the consequence occurs and she is divorced according to us, because the reliance is on the last of the two conditions, and marriage is only needed at the time of suspension and at the time of the consequence; as for in between, it is not needed. According to Zufar, she is not divorced, because he analogizes the other condition to the first: if the first is found in marriage without the second, she is not divorced; similarly, its reverse. And the fifth: a condition like a pure sign, like ihsan (being married) in zina (adultery) is a condition for stoning in the sense of a sign. And they have sometimes counted this as a condition and sometimes as a sign.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Anwar, a commentary on Nur al-Anwar, presents the categorization of conditions (shart) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh, focusing on the third, fourth, and fifth types. The author explains each type with legal examples and occasional disputes within the Hanafi school. The third type is a condition that has the ruling of a cause (shart lahu hukm al-asbab). This occurs when a condition is prior to the conditioned, but between them an act of a free agent intervenes that is not attributed to the condition. The example given: someone unfastens a slave's shackle, and the slave chooses to run away. The unfastening is a condition for the running, but since the slave's act (a free choice) is not necessarily caused by the unfastening, the unfastener is not liable for the slave's value. However, if he commands the slave to run away, he is liable because commanding implies using the slave as an instrument. This distinction shows that the condition here is treated like a cause (sabab) in terms of liability only when the intervening act is attributed to the condition. The passage also contrasts with cases where the intervening act is naturally attributed to the cause, like driving an animal: the animal's destruction is attributed to the driver, so he guarantees. The fourth type is a condition in name only (shart isman la hukman). This occurs when multiple conditions are stipulated in a single sentence, and only the last condition actually triggers the result. Example: 'If you enter this house and this house, you are divorced' – the first entry is a condition in name only; the divorce is triggered by both entries, but because the second entry is the last condition, it is the effective one. There is a dispute between the Hanafis and Zufar: if the first entry occurs without marriage (e.g., after divorce) and then the second entry occurs after remarriage, Hanafis say the divorce takes effect because only the last condition needs marriage at the time of occurrence; Zufar analogizes to the first condition. The fifth type is a condition like a pure sign (shart huwa kal-alamah al-khalisah), such as ihsan (being married) for zina, which is a condition for stoning not as a cause but as a sign that the crime is punishable by death. This type is sometimes considered a condition, sometimes a sign.

Key Terms
شرط كالعلامة الخالصة (shart kal-alamah al-khalisah): A condition that is like a pure sign; it indicates the ruling type but does not cause it.
إحسان (ihsan): In the context of zina, being a free married Muslim, which makes the punishment stoning instead of lashing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is ihsan considered a condition like a pure sign rather than a real condition?
A) Because ihsan does not affect the act of zina.
B) Because ihsan does not cause stoning; it only indicates that stoning is the appropriate punishment.
C) Because ihsan is not required for zina to be a crime.
D) Because the scholars disagree on its status.

Key Takeaway
Not all conditions are causes or suspenders; some are mere signs indicating the severity of the ruling.

Samawi and Kasbi Impediments to Legal Capacity
Enumeration of samawi and kasbi impediments to ahliyyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between samawi and kasbi impediments to legal capacity and list the specific impediments in each category.

Core Idea
Heavenly impediments are beyond human control; acquired impediments arise from human choice — and each has distinct legal effects on capacity.

We just learned about ahliyyah (legal capacity). Now we turn to the factors that can remove or diminish it. The Hanafis classify these into two broad categories: samawi (heavenly) and kasbi (acquired). This passage enumerates them, providing a foundation for understanding how each affects the validity of actions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose of classification
Understand that impediments (al-umur al-mu'taridah) are conditions that affect ahliyyah. They are divided into two types based on the source: from the Lawgiver without human choice (samawi) or from human actions (kasbi).
2
List the 11 samawi impediments
Memorize the list: childhood, insanity, imbecility, forgetfulness, sleep, fainting, slavery, illness, menstruation, postpartum bleeding, and death.
Note that some are temporary (sleep, illness) while others are permanent (death).
3
List the 7 kasbi impediments
Memorize the list: ignorance, drunkenness, [unclear in text — possibly 'azl or marad], travel, foolishness, error, and coercion.
Acquired impediments result from one's own actions or choices.
4
Reflect on legal effects
Consider how each impediment may affect ahliyyat al-wujub (capacity for rights) vs. ahliyyat al-ada' (capacity for actions). For example, death completely extinguishes capacity, while forgetfulness may only affect certain acts.
This step deepens understanding beyond memorization.
5
Apply the classification
Given a legal scenario, identify whether an impediment is samawi or kasbi and state how it influences the validity of an act.
This is the goal of the lesson: to use the classification for analysis.

وَلَمَّا فَرَغَ مِنْ بَيَانِ الأَهْلِيَةِ وَهُوَ مَا ثَبَتَ مِنْ قِبَلِ صَاحِبِ الشَّرْعِ بِلَا اخْتِيَارِ الْعَبْدِ فِيهِ وَهُوَ أَحَدَ عَشَرَ: الصِّغَرُ وَالْجُنُونُ وَالْعِتَةُ وَالنِّسْيَانُ وَالنَّوْمُ وَالإِغْمَاءُ وَالرِّقُ وَالْمَرَضُ وَالْحَيْضُ وَالنِّفَاسُ وَالْمَوْتُ، وَبَعْدَهُ يَأْتِي الْمُكْتَسَبُ الَّذِي ضِدَّ السَّمَاوِي وَهُوَ سَبْعَةٌ: الْجَهْلُ وَالسُّكْرُ وَالْعَزْلُ [؟] وَالسَّفَرُ وَالسَّفَهُ وَالْخَطَأُ وَالإِكْرَاهُ.
And when he finished explaining legal capacity—which is that which is established by the Lawgiver without the servant's choice—it is eleven: childhood, insanity, imbecility, forgetfulness, sleep, fainting, slavery, illness, menstruation, postpartum bleeding, and death. And after it comes the acquired (impediment) which is opposite to the heavenly, and it is seven: ignorance, drunkenness, [unclear], travel, foolishness, error, and coercion.
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage defines the two categories of impediments (al-umur al-mu'taridah) that affect legal capacity (ahliyyah). The first category is samawi (heavenly) impediments, which are beyond human control and are established directly by the Lawgiver. The author lists eleven: childhood (sighar), insanity (junun), imbecility ('itah), forgetfulness (nisyan), sleep (nawm), fainting (ighma'), slavery (riqq), illness (marad), menstruation (hayd), postpartum bleeding (nifas), and death (mawt). These are conditions that remove or diminish capacity without any choice from the person. The second category is kasbi (acquired) impediments, which arise from human actions or choices. Seven are listed: ignorance (jahl), drunkenness (sukr), [unclear], travel (safar), foolishness (safah), error (khata'), and coercion (ikrah). These are factors that can be avoided or are results of human action. This classification helps determine the legal validity of acts performed under such conditions.

Key Terms
الأهلية (Al-Ahliyyah): Legal capacity to acquire rights and obligations, and to perform legal acts.
سماوي (Samawi): Heavenly, that which is from the Lawgiver without human choice.
مكتسب (Muktasab): Acquired, that which results from human action or choice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many heavenly (samawi) impediments to legal capacity are listed in this passage?
A) Seven
B) Eleven
C) Ten
D) Twelve

Key Takeaway
Samawi impediments are decreed by Allah; kasbi impediments arise from human actions — and each category carries distinct legal consequences for ahliyyah.

Classification of Impediments to Legal Capacity: Samawi and Kasbi
Classification of accidental impediments to legal capacity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify accidental impediments (awarid) on legal capacity as samawi or kasbi and explain the legal effect of minority as a samawi impediment, applying the Hanafi usul principles of deficient capacity (ahliyyat al-ada' al-qasira).

Core Idea
Legal capacity is affected by two types of impediments: celestial (beyond human control) and acquired (from human action); minority is a celestial impediment that lifts full responsibility but not the obligation of faith.

In Hanafi usul, understanding the types of 'awarid that affect ahliyyah is crucial for determining when obligations apply. This lesson introduces the classification of impediments into samawi and kasbi, then delves into the celestial impediment of minority (sighar). We will see how the discerning child (mumayyiz) attains a deficient capacity of performance, with specific rulings on worship and faith.

Guided Path
1
Classify the two types
Identify the dividing line between samawi and kasbi – divine decree vs human acquisition. List the examples from the passage.
Samawi: 11 items; Kasbi: 7 items.
2
Analyze minority as a samawi impediment
Understand why minority is considered an 'arid despite being part of original creation. The text uses the example of Adam (as) to show childhood is accidental in progeny.
Minority is not part of human essence.
3
Compare minority and insanity
Use the illustrative scenario of a wife’s conversion to Islam: for a child, presentation of Islam is delayed until he understands; for an insane man, it is presented to his parents immediately because insanity has no foreseeable end.
This shows the difference in legal treatment of the two impediments.
4
Derive the rulings for the discerning child
State which obligations are dropped (acts of worship, hudud, kaffarat) and which are not (faith). Explain the concept of deficient capacity (ahliyyat al-ada' al-qasira).
The child's acts are valid without liability (sahih bi-la ahdah).
5
Summarize the legal effect
Full responsibility (ahdah) is lifted from the child; only apostasy is not forgiven. The child is not considered an apostate if he does not affirm faith before puberty.
Implication: rulings of Muslims apply if he professes faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والا مور المعترضة على الأهلية نوعان سماوي وكسبي. سماوي ما كان من جهة الشارع لا اختيار للعبد فيه: الصغر، الجنون، الغشية، النسيان، النوم، الإغماء، الرق، المرض، الحيض، النفاس، الموت. وكسبي ما كان من كسب العبد: الجهل، السكر، الهزل، السفر، السفه، الخطأ، الإكراه. وإذا عرفت هذا فالآن يذكر أنواع السماوي فيقول: وهو الصغر. إنما ذكره في الأمور المعترضة مع أنه ثابت بأصل الخلقة لأنه ليس بداخل في ماهية الإنسان، ولأن آدم عليه السلام خلق شابا غير صبي، فكان الصبا عارضا في أولاده. وهو في أول أحواله كالجنون بل أدنى حالا منه. ألا ترى أنه إذا أسلمت امرأة الصبي لا يعرض الإسلام على أبويه بل يؤخر إلى أن يعقل الصبي بنفسه فيعرض عليه. وإذا أسلمت امرأة المجنون يعرض الإسلام على أبويه، فإن أسلم أحدهم يحكم بإسلام المجنون تبعا، وإن أبيا يفرق بينه وبين امرأته. ولا فائدة في تأخير الفرض لأن الجنون لا نهاية له فيلزم الإضرار بامرأة مسلمة تكون تحت كافر وذلك لا يجوز. لكنه إذا عقل أي صار مائلا فقد أصاب ضربا من أهلية الأداء يعني القاصرة لا الكاملة لبقاء صغره. وهو مدرك يسقط به ما يحتمل السقوط عن البالغ من حقوق الله تعالى كالعبادات والحدود والكفارات، فإنها تحتمل السقوط بلا عذر وتحتمل النسخ والتبديل في نفسها. ولا تسقط عنه فرضية الإيمان حتى إذا أذاه كان فرضا فيترتب عليه الأحكام المرتبة على المؤمنين من وقوع الفرقة بينه وبين زوجته المشركة وحرمان الميراث منها وجريان الإرث بينه وبين أقاربه المسلمين. ووضع عنه إلزام الأداء أن رفع عن الصبي إلزام أداء الإيمان. فلو لم يقر في أوان الصبا أو لم يعد كلمة الشهادة بعد البلوغ لم يجعل مرتدا. وجعلة الأمر أن توضع عنه العهدة أي خلص الأمر الكلي في باب الصغر. وحاصل أحكامه أن تسقط عنه عمد ما يحتمل العفو يعني ما سوى الردة من العبادات والعقوبات، ويصح منه لو فعله بنفسه من غير عهدة ومطالبة.
And the accidental matters that affect legal capacity are of two types: celestial and acquired. Celestial: what comes from the Legislator without the servant's choice: minority, insanity, fainting, forgetfulness, sleep, swoon, slavery, illness, menstruation, postpartum bleeding, death. Acquired: what comes from the servant's own acquisition: ignorance, intoxication, jest, travel, foolishness, error, coercion. When you know this, now he mentions the types of celestial one, saying: It is minority. He mentioned it among the accidental matters even though it is established by original creation because it is not part of the essence of man, and because Adam peace be upon him was created as a youth not a child, so childhood is accidental in his children. In its initial state it is like insanity, even lower in state. Do you not see that if the wife of a child embraces Islam, Islam is not presented to his parents but rather delayed until the child himself understands, then it is presented to him. If the wife of an insane man embraces Islam, Islam is presented to his parents; if one of them accepts Islam, the insane man is judged Muslim by following, and if both refuse, separation is made between him and his wife. There is no benefit in delaying the obligation because insanity has no end, so it would cause harm to a Muslim woman being under a disbeliever, and that is not permissible. But when he understands i.e. becomes discerning, he has attained a kind of capacity of performance, i.e. deficient not complete due to remaining of his minority. He is discerning; by it what can be dropped from an adult of the rights of Allah Most High, like acts of worship, hudud punishments, and expiations, are dropped from him, because they can be dropped without excuse and they are subject to abrogation and change in themselves. But the obligation of faith is not dropped from him, so when he professes it, it becomes obligatory, and there are attached to him the rulings applicable to believers, such as separation occurring between him and his polytheist wife, being prevented from inheriting from her, and the inheritance flowing between him and his Muslim relatives. And the enforcement of performance is lifted from him, meaning the enforcement of performing faith is removed from the child. So if he did not affirm in the time of childhood or did not repeat the word of testimony after puberty, he is not considered an apostate. The gist of the matter is that full responsibility is removed from him. The summary of his rulings is that what can be forgiven is dropped from him, i.e. everything except apostasy from acts of worship and punishments, and it is valid from him if he does it himself without liability and claim.
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage classifies the 'awarid (impediments) that affect ahliyyah (legal capacity) into two categories: samawi (celestial) and kasbi (acquired). Celestial impediments are those from the Divine decree, beyond human control, and include minority, insanity, fainting, forgetfulness, sleep, swoon, slavery, illness, menstruation, postpartum bleeding, and death. Acquired impediments come from the servant's own actions and include ignorance, intoxication, jest, travel, foolishness, error, and coercion. The discussion then focuses on sighar (minority) as a celestial impediment. Although minority is part of the original creation of humans, it is accidental because Adam (peace be upon him) was created as an adult. So childhood is an accident in his descendants. The author compares minority to insanity, stating it is like or even lower than insanity in its initial state. Evidence: if a child's wife becomes Muslim, Islam is not presented to the child's parents but is delayed until the child himself can understand; whereas for an insane man, Islam is presented to his parents immediately because insanity has no foreseeable end and delaying would harm a Muslim wife. When a child reaches the age of discernment (tamyiz), he has a deficient capacity of performance (ahliyyat al-ada' al-qasira). This means that rights of Allah that can be dropped from an adult (like acts of worship, hudud, kaffarat) are dropped from him because they are subject to abrogation. However, the obligation of faith (iman) is not dropped from him. Thus, if he professes faith, it is binding, and he is subject to the rulings of Muslims (e.g., separation from a polytheist spouse, inheritance among Muslim relatives). The enforcement of performance is lifted from him, so if he does not affirm faith before puberty, he is not considered an apostate. The summary is that full responsibility (ahdah) is removed from the child, and only what can be forgiven (i.e., everything except apostasy) is dropped from him.

Key Terms
عارض (arid): An accidental impediment affecting legal capacity, either celestial or acquired.
أهلية الأداء القاصرة (ahliyyat al-ada' al-qasira): Deficient capacity of performance granted to a discerning child, where some obligations are dropped.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The classification of 'awarid into samawi and kasbi is foundational in Hanafi usul; minority as a samawi impediment establishes deficient capacity, allowing some obligations to be lifted while preserving the obligation of faith.

Qisas Between Free and Slave: Equality in Foundational Meaning
Hanafi ruling that a free person is killed for a slave in qisas, with qiyas proof and Shafi'i opposition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul rule that equality in the foundational meaning (an-nafs bi-n-nafs) suffices for qisas, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument regarding human honors.

Core Idea
Equality in basic life (nafs) suffices for qisas; extra honors (karamat) do not affect retaliation.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling that a free person is killed in retaliation for a slave. The passage establishes that the slave shares inviolability (isma) with the free, and the core element for qisas is equality in the original meaning of life, not additional honors. The Shafi'i school disagrees, requiring full equality in human excellence. Through this dispute, we explore the usul principle of how attributes affect legal rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position on qisas
Read the passage to find the explicit Hanafi ruling that a free person is killed for a slave in retaliation. Note that this is stated as 'عندنا' (according to us).
The ruling is conditional on equality in the original meaning (ma'na asli) upon which qisas is based.
2
Analyze the basis of equality: isma and its two types
The passage explains that a slave is like a free person in two types of inviolability: one based on faith and one based on residence in Dar al-Islam. Understand how each applies to the slave.
The second type depends on the master's protected status.
3
Examine the Hanafi proof: qiyas with male/female case
The Hanafi evidence is an analogy (qiyas) to the case of a man and a woman: a man is killed for a woman despite differences in blood money and honors. Identify the shared illa (effective cause): equality in the nafs.
The passage explicitly compares: 'كما يجري ذلك فيما بين الذكر والأنثى'.
4
Contrast the Shafi'i objection and the Hanafi response
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that the slave lacks eligibility for human honors (ahliyyat al-karamat al-insaniyya), so qisas is prevented. Understand the Hanafi response: karamat are additional attributes that do not affect the core ruling of qisas.
The Hanafi response uses the male/female analogy to show that extra attributes (e.g., blood money difference) do not block qisas.
5
Derive the thamarah al-khilaf and operative ruling
The practical consequence: in the Hanafi school, a free Muslim is executed for killing a slave; in the Shafi'i school, only diyya (blood money) is due. Identify which position is mufta bihi according to the text.
The text clearly adopts the Hanafi view as the relied-upon position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْعَبْدُ فِيهِ أَيْ فِي كُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْ الْعِصْمَتَيْنِ كَالْحُرُّ أَمَّا فِي الْإِيمَانِ فَظَاهِرٌ وَأَمَّا فِي الِاحْتِرَازِ فِي دَارِ الْإِسْلَامِ فَلَاتُهُ تَبَعٌ لِلْمَوْلَى فَإِذَا كَانَ الْمَوْلَى مُحْتَرِمًا فِي دَارِ الْإِسْلَامِ كَانَ الْعَبْدُ أَيْضًا مُحْتَرِمًا فِيهِ إِمَّا بِالْإِسْلَامِ أَوْ بِقُبُولِ الذِّمَّةِ وَإِنَّمَا يُؤَثِّرُ الرِّقُّ فِي نُقْصَانِ قِيمَتِهِ حَتَّى إِذَا بَلَغَتْ قِيمَتُهُ عَشْرَةَ آلَافِ دِرْهَمٍ يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يَنْقُصَ مِنْهُ عَشَرَةُ دَرَاهِمَ حَطَّا لِمَرْتَبَتِهِ عَنْ مَرْتَبَةِ الْحُرِّ وَلِهَذَا أَيْ لِكَوْنِ الْعَبْدِ مِثْلَ الْحُرِّ فِي الْعِصْمَةِ يُقْتَلُ الْحُرُّ بِالْعَبْدِ قِصَاصًا عِنْدَنَا إِذَا وُجِدَتِ الْمُسَاوَاةُ فِي الْمَعْنَى الْأَصْلِيِّ الَّذِي يَبْتَنِي عَلَيْهِ الْقِصَاصُ وَالْكَرَامَاتُ الْأُخَرُ صِفَةٌ زَائِدَةٌ فِي الْحُرِّ لَا يَتَعَلَّقُ بِهَا الْقِصَاصُ كَمَا يَجْرِي ذَلِكَ فِيمَا بَيْنَ الذَّكَرِ وَالْأُنْثَى وَإِنْ كَانَ يَنْتَقِصُ بَدَلُ دَمِهَا عَنْ بَدَلِ دَمِ الذَّكَرِ وَعِنْدَ الشَّافِعِيِّ لَا يُقْتَلُ الْحُرُّ بِالْعَبْدِ لِعَدَمِ أَهْلِيَّةِ الْكَرَامَاتِ الْإِنْسَانِيَّةِ فَامْتَنَعَ الْقِصَاصُ لِعَدَمِ الْمُسَاوَاةِ وَصَحَّ أَمَانُ الْمَأْذُونِ فِي الْقِتَالِ لَا الْمَأْذُونِ فِي التِّجَارَةِ لِلْكُفَّارِ لِأَنَّهُ كَمَا أَذِنَ لَهُ مَوْلَاهُ بِالْقِتَالِ صَارَ شَرِيكًا فِي الْغَنِيمَةِ فَالْأَمَانُ تَصَرُّفٌ فِي حَقِّ نَفْسِهِ قَصْدًا ثُمَّ يَكُونُ فِي حَقِّ غَيْرِهِ ضِمْنًا وَإِنَّمَا قَيَّدَ بِالْمَأْذُونِ لِأَنَّ فِي أَمَانِ الْمَحْجُورِ خِلَافًا فَعِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ لَا يَصِحُّ لِأَنَّهُ لَا حَقَّ لَهُ فِي الْجِهَادِ حَتَّى يَكُونَ مُسْتَقِلًّا بِحَقِّ نَفْسِهِ. وَعِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ وَالشَّافِعِيِّ يَصِحُّ أَمَانُهُ لِأَنَّهُ مُسْلِمٌ مِنْ أَهْلِ نَصْرَةِ الدِّينِ وَلَعَلَّ فِيهِ مَصْلَحَةً لِلْمُسْلِمِينَ. وَإِقْرَارُهُ بِالْحُدُودِ وَالْقِصَاصِ صَحَّ إِقْرَارُ الْعَبْدِ الْمَأْذُونِ بِمَا يُوجِبُ الْحُدُودَ وَالْقِصَاصَ وَإِنْ كَانَ يَسْتَرِكُ فِيهِ الْمَحْجُورُ أَيْضًا لِأَنَّ إِقْرَارَهُ يَصِيرُ مُلْزِمًا لِحَقِّ نَفْسِهِ الَّذِي هُوَ الدَّمُ وَإِنْ كَانَ الْإِتْلَافُ مَالِيَّةَ الْمَوْلَى بِطَرِيقِ الضَّمَانِ.
The slave in that, i.e. in each of the two types of inviolability, is like the free. As for faith, it is apparent. And as for protection in the abode of Islam, his protection is dependent on the master. So if the master is protected in the abode of Islam, the slave is also protected therein, either by Islam or by acceptance of dhimma. And slavery only affects the deficiency of his blood money, such that if his value reaches ten thousand dirhams, it should be decreased by ten dirhams to lower his rank from that of the free. And for this, i.e. because the slave is like the free in inviolability, the free is killed for the slave in retaliation according to us, when equality is found in the original meaning upon which retaliation is based. The other honors are an additional attribute in the free, with which retaliation is not concerned, just as that occurs between male and female, even though the blood money of the female is deficient compared to that of the male. And according to al-Shafi'i, the free is not killed for the slave due to the lack of eligibility for human honors, so retaliation is prevented due to lack of equality. And the aman (safe conduct) of a slave permitted for fighting is valid, not the one permitted for trade for the disbelievers, because when his master permitted him for fighting, he becomes a partner in the spoils, so the aman is a disposition in his own right intentionally, then it becomes for others incidentally. And he only restricted it to the permitted one because there is a difference of opinion regarding the aman of the maḥjūr (restricted slave). According to Abu Hanifa, it is not valid because he has no right to jihad so as to be independent in his own right. According to Muhammad and al-Shafi'i, his aman is valid because he is a Muslim from among the supporters of the religion, and perhaps there is benefit for the Muslims in it. And his confession regarding hudud and retaliation: the confession of the permitted slave is valid for what necessitates hudud and retaliation, even if the maḥjūr also participates in it, because his confession becomes binding for his own right which is blood, even though the destruction is the property of the master by way of guarantee.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage addresses the legal status of a slave in Hanafi fiqh regarding blood inviolability (ismah) and retaliation (qisas). It first establishes that a slave shares two types of inviolability with a free person: one based on faith (iman) and one based on residence in Dar al-Islam. Since the slave is dependent on his master, his protection in Dar al-Islam follows the master's status. However, slavery does reduce the slave's financial value (qima), exemplified by a notional deduction of ten dirhams from ten thousand to lower his rank. Crucially, because the core element of qisas—equality in the foundational meaning (an-nafs bi-n-nafs)—is present, a free person is killed in qisas for killing a slave according to the Hanafi school. Extra honors (karamat) attached to free status do not affect qisas, similar to the gender difference where a man is killed for a woman despite the woman's blood money being less. The text contrasts Imam al-Shafi'i's view that qisas does not apply due to the slave's lack of human excellence (ahliyyat al-karamat). The passage then discusses the validity of a slave's aman (granting safe conduct): a slave permitted by his master to fight can grant aman, because he has a stake in war and spoils; a slave permitted only for trade cannot. There is also the case of a restricted slave (mahjur): Abu Hanifa invalidates his aman, while Imam Muhammad and Shafi'i validate it due to his being a Muslim. Finally, a slave's confession (iqrar) for hudud and qisas is valid, as it concerns his own right (blood), even though the financial penalty falls on the master.

Key Terms
عصمة (isma): Inviolability that prohibits harm to a person; two types: one based on faith (sinful to harm) and one based on residence in Dar al-Islam (financial compensation).
كرامات (karamat): Honors and distinctions associated with free status beyond basic inviolability, such as guardianship (wilaya) and eligibility for multiple marriages.
مأذون (ma'dhun): A slave permitted by his master to engage in trade or fighting; the passage distinguishes between permission for trade and for fighting regarding the validity of granting aman.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is a free person killed in qisas for killing a slave?
A) Because the slave's life is considered equal in value to a free person's life.
B) Because the foundational meaning of equality in life (an-nafs bi-n-nafs) is present, and extra honors do not affect qisas.
C) Because the slave has the same eligibility for human honors as a free person.
D) Because the slave's master can waive the right to qisas.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that equality in basic life (nafs) suffices for qisas, and additional honors (karamat) do not affect retaliation, analogous to the gender case.

Distinguishing Mudabbir and Mortgaged Slave: Right in Possession vs. Ownership
Ruling on mudabbir and comparison with mortgaged slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the legal status of a mudabbir from a mortgaged slave by applying the Hanafi principle that rights attached to possession (yad) do not prevent a transaction from taking effect, while rights attached to ownership (raqaba) do.

Core Idea
A mudabbir's freeing is suspended until death because creditors' rights attach to his body; a mortgaged slave's freeing is immediate because the mortgagee's right is only in possession.

In this lesson, we examine a passage from Ashraf al-Anwaar that illustrates a key usul distinction: the nature of the right attached to a slave determines whether the master's freeing takes effect immediately or is suspended. The case of a sick person's mudabbir is compared to a mortgaged slave, revealing that the mortgagee's right is merely custodial (yad), not proprietary (raqaba). Understanding this distinction helps us apply the correct ruling in similar contexts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
The passage presents two situations: (1) a mudabbir declared by a terminally ill master, and (2) a mortgaged slave freed by the mortgagor. What are the rulings in each? For the mudabbir, freeing is suspended until death; for the mortgaged slave, the freeing is effective immediately.
2
Locate the implied question
The author addresses a muqaddar sual: 'You said freeing does not take effect when creditors/heirs have a right, yet you consider the freeing of a mortgaged slave effective even though the mortgagee has a right.' Identify the objection's basis.
The objection assumes both rights are equivalent.
3
Analyze the talil (reasoning)
The author distinguishes by stating that the mortgagee's right is in yad (possession) only, not in raqaba (the slave's person). How does this difference explain immediate effect? Since the mortgagee does not own the slave, the master retains ownership and can free him.
In contrast, creditors/heirs have a right in the raqaba because the slave is part of the estate.
4
Extract the usul principle
From this comparison, derive the Hanafi principle: the attachment of rights to the raqaba prevents immediate execution of transactions, while rights to mere yad do not. This is a form of limitation on the master's disposal.
The principle can be extended to other transactions like gifts and sales.
5
Apply to the mudabbir's status
Confirm that the mudabbir's case falls under the first type: if the slave's value exceeds one-third or if the master's assets are insufficient to cover debts, creditors/heirs have a right in the raqaba, so the freeing is suspended until death, after which the slave works to pay his value.
If the slave's value is within one-third and there are no debts, the freeing takes effect immediately.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The ruling of the mudabbir: before death he remains a slave in all rulings connected to the [protectorate?] of honors, and after death he becomes free and works to pay his value to creditors and heirs. But if there is in the property sufficient to cover the debt and it exits from one-third, then the freeing takes effect immediately due to no one's right being attached to him, unlike the freeing of the mortgagor where it takes effect. (This is the) answer to an implied question: You said that freeing does not take effect immediately when it occurs upon a [slave having] creditors and heirs, yet you judged the freeing of a mortgagor's slave effective while the mortgagee's right is attached. He answered: The freeing of the mortgagor is effective because the mortgagee's right is in possession not in the slave's body, since in the body remains the right of the mortgagor, and the validity of freeing is based on that. (Then Urdu commentary explaining the effects: that the sick person's transactions that can be rescinded are valid immediately but can be rescinded if needed; those that cannot be rescinded are suspended upon death, like freeing a slave, and the mudabbir is in the ruling of a slave until death, then becomes free and works to pay his value. The case of the mortgagor is distinguished because the mortgagee's right is only in possession not ownership.)
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the legal status of a mudabbir (a slave declared free upon the master's death) when the master is terminally ill. The author explains that before death, the mudabbir remains a slave with all rights, but after death he becomes free and must work to pay his assessed value to creditors and heirs. If the master has enough wealth to cover debts and the slave's value is within one-third of the estate, the freeing takes effect immediately because no one else's right is attached. This contrasts with the case of a mortgaged slave (rahn) where the master's freeing is immediately effective even though the mortgagee has a right. The reason given is that the mortgagee's right is merely custodial (in possession/actio) and not in the actual ownership of the slave's person (raqaba). The commentary expands on this by discussing the general principle that a sick person's transactions are valid if they can be rescinded (like gifts) and are suspended if not (like freeing). The key legal nuance is that the attachment of creditors' or heirs' rights only occurs when the slave's value exceeds one-third or there is insufficient other wealth to cover debts.

Key Terms
المدير (al-mudabbir): A slave who has been declared free by his master upon the master's death (tadbir).
الراهن (al-rahin): The person who gives an item as collateral for a debt.
المرتهن (al-murtahin): The creditor who holds the collateral.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because the mortgagee's right is only in possession (yad), not in the slave's body.
C) Because the mortgagor is not sick.
D) Because the mortgage dissolves upon freeing.

Key Takeaway
The distinction between rights in possession (yad) and rights in ownership (raqaba) determines whether a sick person's freeing of a slave takes effect immediately or is suspended until death.
